201 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Makarchuk


DA 07-0341


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 82; 349 Mont. 507; 204 P.3d 1213; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 89


June 4, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
March 17, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 3, 2009.
Post-conviction relief denied at Makarchuk v. STATE, 2014 MT 246N, 376 Mont. 550, 347 P.3d 265, 2014 Mont. LEXIS 507 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC 03-403B, Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead (Montana) of operating an unlawful clandestine methamphetamine laboratory. Defendant was sentenced to twenty years in prison with ten years suspended with conditions. The court denied his motion for new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by failing to credit defendant with the 264 days he spent on house arrest. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant was not required to wear an electronic monitoring device and was assigned to house arrest as a condition of his release on bond, rather than as a condition of his later suspended sentence. Defendant's release was ordered pursuant to a stipulation and was conditioned by use of the term "formal house arrest." Defendant argued that the difference in wording and the formal stipulation required sentencing credit. However, though the house arrest was described within the bond release order as "formal," and was stipulated to by the parties, it nonetheless did not meet the statutory definition of "home arrest" as contemplated in Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-203(7)(b). However, the trial court erred by imposing conditions upon defendant's parole release. The parole conditions imposed by the trial court were illegal as being beyond the authority of the court, and were properly challenged on appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed to the extent the conditions imposed by the trial court applied to defendant's parole. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

 

202 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Town & Country Foods, Inc. v. City of Bozeman


DA 07-0448


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 72; 349 Mont. 453; 203 P.3d 1283; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 74


May 28, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
March 10, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 27, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Cause No. DV 05-522. Honorable Wm. Nels Swandal, Presiding Judge.
Town And County Foods v. City of Bozeman, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 721 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer filed an application for approval of a new site to build six mini-stores in a neighborhood zoning district. When the city commission denied the developer's application, the developer sued appellee City raising several issues challenging the denial of its site plan approval application. The Eighteenth Judicial District Court, Gallatin County, granted the City's motion for summary judgment. The developer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the developer contended summary judgment was improper as the district court relied on disputed facts and the city commission acted arbitrarily and capriciously in reclaiming and denying its application. The supreme court disagreed, finding first that a constitutional substantive due process analysis was inapplicable under the facts of this case because the developer did not allege the zoning ordinance in question was unconstitutional. Further, the record showed that the city commission considered the relevant criteria listed in Bozeman, Mont., Unified Development Ordinance § 18.34.090(A) (including vehicle and pedestrian traffic, parking, wetlands, setbacks, and conformity with the neighborhood) and stated its reasons for deciding that the developer's site plan did not conform to the neighborhood business zoning district. The city commission followed its ordinance in reclaiming and passing on the developer's application by holding a public meeting and unanimously voting to reclaim the application from the planning director to head off of an eventual appeal and protecting public interest and safety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

203 of 699 DOCUMENTS


City of Billings v. Albert


DA 08-0140


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 63; 349 Mont. 400; 203 P.3d 828; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 80


January 28, 2009, Submitted on Briefs 
March 3, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 20, 2009
Related proceeding at Albert v. City of Billings, 2012 MT 159, 2012 Mont. LEXIS 208 (July 24, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC 07-0382. Honorable Russell C. Fagg, Presiding Judge.
City of Billings v. Albert, 2008 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 251 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of storage of salvage. The Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Montana, affirmed the conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with a violation of Billings, MT, Municipal City Code (BMCC) 27-601(g). The city's counsel presented witnesses about their repeated attempts to work with defendant to clean about his property. Numerous photographs depicting defendant's property were also admitted as evidence. At issue on appeal was: (1) whether BMCC 27-601(g) was unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant; (2) whether defendant was denied effective assistance of counsel; (3) whether the municipal court erred in denying defendant's motion to dismiss for insufficient evidence; and (4) whether the district court erred in determining defendant's sentence was legal. Additional definitions in the city code diminished the inconsistencies between "permanent storage" and "open storage." Moreover, there was nothing vague about how the ordinance was applied to defendant. Applying the first prong of the Strickland test, defendant's counsel was reasonably effective. There was sufficient evidence to sustain the conviction because witnesses testified that items remained in defendant's yard without moving for more than five days. Finally, the supreme court determined that defendant's sentence was legal.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

204 of 699 DOCUMENTS


In re G.M.


DA 08-0229


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 59; 349 Mont. 320; 203 P.3d 818; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 70


January 14, 2009, Submitted on Briefs 
February 25, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re G.M., 2009 Mont. LEXIS 654 (Mont., Mar. 17, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. ADI-1994-11. Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient was a developmentally disabled man in his mid-thirties who had been involuntarily committed and for about half of his life. Appellee State filed a petition to recommit the patient to a residential facility. The First Judicial District Court of Lewis and Clark County, Montana, continued the patient's then current commitment upon a finding that he continued to be seriously developmentally disabled. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the patient raised several issues contending the district court erred in recommitting him. The supreme court disagreed, finding that by stipulating to recommitment, the patient necessarily conceded that there was sufficient clear and convincing evidence to recommit him. As to the patient's challenge to the applicable standard, the supreme court determined that if it adopted the patient's position and imposed the mental illness standard from Mont. Code Ann. § 53-21-126(2), the most crucial issues in a commitment proceeding, including the existence of developmental disability and cognitive impairment, would still have been determined by a clear and convincing evidence standard. All medical testimony would have met the reasonable degree of medical certainty standard. Thus, the supreme court found no legal or factual reason to conclude that application of the standard of proof advocated by the patient would have protected individual constitutional rights to any greater degree than the present clear and convincing evidence standard. Thus, the district court correctly applied the clear and convincing standard of proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

205 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Violette


DA 07-0652


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 19; 349 Mont. 81; 201 P.3d 804; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 20


October 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
January 27, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 2009.


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Third Judicial District, In and For the County of Powell, Cause No. DC-06-36. Honorable Ray Dayton, Presiding Judge.
State v. Violette, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 707 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Third Judicial District, in and for the County of Powell, Montana, that found him not guilty of various offenses by reason of mental disease or defect and that committed him to the Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services for a period of 10 years, arguing that the district court erred in denying his motion to dismiss for violation of his right to a speedy trial.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendant's argument, the State contended that defendant's appeal must be dismissed because an appeal could not be taken from a judgment of not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect. In agreeing with the State's argument, the court ruled that a final judgment of conviction was a prerequisite for appellate review in criminal cases under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-20-104. Defendant was precluded from appealing because there was no judgment of conviction from which to appeal, and the denial of his motion to dismiss based upon a speedy trial violation, absent a judgment of conviction, was not itself an appealable order.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Dunsmore v. Mahoney


Docket No. OP 08-0571


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 Mont. LEXIS 51



January 21, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, Petition dismissed by, Motion denied by Dunsmore v. Crossroads Correctional Center, 2009 Mont. LEXIS 831 (Mont., Jan. 28, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Dunsmore v. Law, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 61209 (D. Mont., July 14, 2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Writ of mandamus denied, Motion granted by Dunsmore v. Flathead Dist. Court, 352 Mont. 550, 218 P.3d 498, 2009 Mont. LEXIS 622 (Mont., 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by, Motion granted by Dunsmore v. Eleventh Judicial District, 2010 Mont. LEXIS 61 (Mont., Jan. 26, 2010)
Related proceeding at Dunsmore v. State, 2010 Mont. LEXIS 257 (Mont., Mar. 16, 2010)
Related proceeding at Dunsmore v. Montana, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 93225 (D. Mont., July 16, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion granted by Dunsmore v. Dep't of Corr., 242 P.3d 1285, 2010 Mont. LEXIS 361 (Mont., 2010)
Related proceeding at Dunsmore v. State, 2012 Mont. LEXIS 469 (Mont., Nov. 20, 2012)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by Dunsmore v. Kirkgard, 374 Mont. 539, 346 P.3d 363, 2014 Mont. LEXIS 205 (Mont., 2014)
Related proceeding at State v. Dunsmore, 2015 MT 108, 378 Mont. 514, 347 P.3d 1220, 2015 Mont. LEXIS 177 (2015)
Related proceeding at, Writ denied by Dunsmore v. Allison, 379 Mont. 537, 353 P.3d 507, 2015 Mont. LEXIS 364 (Mont., 2015)
Related proceeding at Dunsmore v. Montana, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 31749 (D. Mont., Mar. 11, 2016)
Related proceeding at Dunsmore v. Montana, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 31750 (D. Mont., Mar. 11, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of child molestation in Washington in 1991. While his petition to release him from the Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-504 sex offender registration requirement was pending, he pled guilty to failing to register in exchange for deferred prosecution on an incest charge, which was dismissed. He sought habeas or mandamus relief arguing that a restitution condition violated Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-801.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that the petition was a postconviction petition that was time- and procedurally-barred under Mont. Code Ann. §§ 46-21-102 and 46-22-101(2). The court found that the claim against the Department of Correction (DOC) failed. Under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-244(6)(a), when an inmate owed restitution, the DOC had to take a percentage of funds deposited in the inmate's account administered by the DOC. The district court correctly refused to relieve the inmate of the registration requirement--his petition was untruthful in representing that he had been law abiding as required by Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-506(3) when, in fact, he had been charged with incest while the petition was pending. An ineffective assistance of counsel claim lacked merit: the inmate benefited from dismissal of the incest charges and signed the plea agreement acknowledging an understanding of the consequences. The petition was a postconviction petition. The inmate did not appeal his conviction or file a timely Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-102(1) postconviction relief petition. Regardless of the petition's character, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-201(2) did not entitle the inmate to appointment of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's request for appointment of counsel and denied and dismissed his petitions for a writ of habeas corpus or a writ of mandamus.

 

207 of 699 DOCUMENTS


In re C.D.H.


DA 08-0042


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2009 MT 8; 349 Mont. 1; 201 P.3d 126; 2009 Mont. LEXIS 10


November 19, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
January 13, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, In and For the County of Pondera, Cause No. DJ 07-01. Honorable Laurie McKinnon, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile challenged an order of the District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, in and for the County of Pondera, Montana, that denied his motion to delete the requirement that he register as a sex offender, arguing that he should have been sentenced under Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-1513(1)(d) (2005) rather than Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-1513(1)(d) (2007) and that the district court erred in denying his motion for substitution of judge.


OVERVIEW: The 13-year-old juvenile was adjudicated delinquent based upon his sexual abuse of his four-year-old half-brother. The district court placed the juvenile on probation, and although the district court did not require the juvenile to register as a sex offender, the juvenile's probation officer informed him that he would have to do so pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-1513(1)(d) (2007), which required a delinquent who had been adjudicated for a sexual offense to register. The juvenile registered before filing a motion to delete that requirement. On review of the district court's order denying the juvenile's motion, the court held that the juvenile was properly sentenced under the amended statute and not the statute that was in effect at the time he committed his offense because the legislature intended the statute to apply retroactively. Further, the judge to whom the case was assigned erred in denying the motion for substitution of judge based upon the juvenile's failure to pay a filing fee because juvenile proceedings were criminal proceedings that allowed a one-time judge substitution, and Mont. Code Ann. § 3-1-804(1)(d) excluded criminal case from the filing fee requirement.


OUTCOME: The order of the district court was affirmed, but a new judge was to preside over any future proceedings in this matter.

 

208 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Buhmann v. State


05-473


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 465; 348 Mont. 205; 201 P.3d 70; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 696


September 13, 2006, Argued; June 20, 2007, Submitted 
December 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wallace v. Montana, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7453 (U.S., Oct. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. ADV 2002-555. Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Presiding Judge.
Buhmann v. State, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1941 (2004)
Hagener v. Wallace, 2002 MT 109, 309 Mont. 473, 47 P.3d 847, 2002 Mont. LEXIS 206 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff farm owners appealed the order of the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, which denied their takings claims under the Fifth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution and Mont. Const. art. II, § 29.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs started a ranch after obtaining a game farm license in 1992. On November 7, 2000, the voters of Montana passed I-143, which prohibited fee-shooting on game farms. Plaintiffs alleged that I-143 was a unconstitutional taking of their private property in violation of the Fifth Amendment and Mont. Const. art. II, § 29. Defendant, the State Montana, was entitled to a change of venue under Mont. Code Ann. § 25-2-116 by virtue of the presence of multiple claims. The district court did not err by denying the motion to sever claims. Liability for plaintiffs' takings claims was a legal question properly decided by the district court instead of a jury. Mont. Const. art. II, § 29 did not provide any greater constitutional protection against the taking of private property than the Fifth Amendment to the U.S. Constitution. The Supreme Court of Montana held that plaintiffs' failed to prove a compensable taking. While I-143 impaired the profitable use of alternative livestock, it still allowed plaintiffs every other use of their alternative livestock.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

209 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Kafka v. Mont. Dep't of Fish, Wildlife & Parks


05-146


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 460; 348 Mont. 80; 201 P.3d 8; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 697


September 13, 2006, Argued; June 20, 2007, Submitted 
December 31, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Wallace v. Montana, 558 U.S. 945, 130 S. Ct. 394, 175 L. Ed. 2d 267, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 7453 (U.S., 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Hill, Cause No. DV 2002-059. Honorable David G. Rice, Presiding Judge.
Kafka v. Dept of Fish, 2003 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2778 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the owners and operators of alternative livestock game farms (owners), appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, in and for the County of Hill (Montana) denying their takings claims against defendants, the State of Montana and the Department of Fish, Wildlife and Parks (FWP), on the ground that an Initiative Measure No. 154 (I-143) impaired the profitability of their game farm operations.


OVERVIEW: The owners held valid alternative game farm licenses issued by the FWP. I-143 prohibited the owners from charging a fee to shoot alternative livestock by altering Mont. Code Ann. § 87-4-414(2) (2001). The owners contended that, by prohibiting fee-shooting, I-143 eliminated the most profitable use of the alternative livestock and the profitability of their game farms. The owners brought takings claims under the Mont. Const. art. II, § 29, and the U.S. Const. amend. V. The district court held that the enactment and enforcement of I-143 did not amount to a compensable taking of the owners' private property because the owners should have reasonably anticipated a measure like I-143. The court found that the district court's findings were not clearly erroneous. First, the owners' licenses were not compensable property interests because they were not transferable, exclusive, or free of any express statutory language precluding the formation of a property right. The court weighed the effects of I-143 and concluded that the owners were not entitled to compensation for the regulatory takings for goodwill and other intangible assets, real estate and fixtures, or alternative livestock.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.


 

210 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Kratovil v. Liberty Northwest Ins. Corp.


DA 07-0579


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 443; 347 Mont. 521; 200 P.3d 71; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 678


July 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
December 29, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: Montana Workers' Compensation Court, WCC No. 2006-1551. Honorable James Jeremiah Shea, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employer's insurer, sought review of an order from the Montana Workers' Compensation Court (WCC), which awarded appellee employee workers' compensation benefits on an occupational disease claim.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a plumber/pipefitter. He filed both a workers' compensation injury claim and an occupational disease claim, asserting hand and wrist injuries. The insurer denied liability. The WCC held the insurer liable for the occupational disease claim. On appeal, the court found that the WCC properly determined that the employee had an employment-related occupational disease, as defined in Mont. Code Ann. § 39-72-102(1) (2003), that might have been exacerbated by a motorcycle accident but was, nonetheless, compensable under the Montana Occupational Disease Act (ODA). The reports of an orthopedic surgeon indicated that the employee's hand and wrist injuries were clearly a preexisting condition occurring before his motorcycle accident and that his hand numbness occurred gradually over time and had gotten worse. The employee's work as a plumber/pipefitter significantly aggravated or contributed to his hand and wrist conditions, as required by Mont. Code Ann. § 39-72-408. The employer, as the employer at the time the employee was last injuriously exposed to the hazard of the disease, was liable under Mont. Code Ann. § 39-72-303.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the WCC. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Normandy


DA 07-0441


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 437; 347 Mont. 505; 198 P.3d 834; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 679


October 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
December 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2009.
Post-conviction proceeding at Normandy v. State, 2009 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 529 (2009)
Post-conviction proceeding at Normandy v. State, 2009 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 530 (2009)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at Normandy v. State, 2009 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 533 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Cause No. DC 2006-187. Honorable Jeffrey H. Langton, Presiding Judge.
State v. Normandy, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 409 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, in and for the County of Ravalli, Montana, that convicted him of partner or family member assault, arguing that he was denied a fair trial because of surprise in the introduction of expert testimony by a witness not designated by the State as an expert and that the district court erred in refusing to dismiss a prospective juror for cause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for assaulting his wife after his wife reported the assault to the police. After defendant was arrested, his wife also discussed the incident with a county victim advocate. During trial, the State called the victim advocate to testify as an expert, although she was not designated as an expert witness on the State's witness list. On review, the court noted that, while Mont. Code Ann. § 46-15-323 required a defendant to disclose expert witnesses to the State, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-15-322 only required the State to disclose its witnesses and did not require that the State indicate which were experts. While defendant contended that the discrepancy was unconstitutional, the issue was not reviewable because he failed to raise it before the trial court. The court further concluded that the district court did not err in failing to dismiss a prospective juror for cause under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-16-115(2)(j). Although the juror indicated that he had a predisposition against domestic violence because it affected his wife in her first marriage, he did not voice a predisposition regarding defendant's guilt or innocence and asserted that he could be fair and impartial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed.

 

212 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. VanDyke


DA 08-0087


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 439N; 348 Mont. 372; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 681


October 29, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
December 23, 2008, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. VanDyke, 211 P.3d 204, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 793 (Mont., Dec. 23, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC 07-322. Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.
City of Kalispell v. Vandyke, 2008 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 624 (2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Eleventh Judicial District Court, Flathead County, Montana, denying his motion to dismiss the charge of habitual traffic offender operating a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant's vehicle. A license check indicated that he had been declared a habitual traffic offender and his license had been revoked pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 61-11-211. Defendant was charged with a violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-11-213, habitual traffic offender operating a motor vehicle. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, arguing that his failure to receive notice that he was a habitual offender amounted to a violation of his due process rights. The district court did not err by denying defendant's motion to dismiss. The Supreme Court of Montana held that the government's interest in keeping those drivers who were unable to comply with traffic laws off of public highways justified the immediate revocation of an offender's driver's license. Allowing notice to the offender to become effective upon mailing most efficiently carried out that objective. Therefore, the notice provision of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-11-204 satisfied due process standards. Defendant also had constructive notice of his status as a habitual offender by virtue of his knowledge of his multiple traffic violations.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

213 of 699 DOCUMENTS



City of Whitefish v. Bd. of County Comm'rs of Flathead County


DA 08-0238


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 436; 347 Mont. 490; 199 P.3d 201; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 683


November 13, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
December 23, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 8, 2009.
Related proceeding at Phillips v. City of Whitefish, 2014 MT 186, 2014 Mont. LEXIS 416 (July 14, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV-2008-367(A). Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead (Montana), which denied its requested for a preliminary injunction and which ruled in favor of appellee county by finding that an interlocal agreement previously entered into between the city and the county was invalid.


OVERVIEW: The parties entered into an interlocal agreement. Later, the county issued a resolution unilaterally rescinding the county's consent to the agreement in violation of the express terms of the agreement. The court concluded that the district court erred in its application of Mont. Code Ann. § 27-19-103 when it determined that the county could not be prevented from executing a public statute for the public benefit and that the agreement could not be specifically enforced. The error was that both determinations were conclusions resolving the ultimate merits of the case even though the district court was only to make a determination as to the application for the preliminary injunction. The district court erred when it resolved the ultimate merits of the case rather than initially analyzing the propriety of the preliminary injunction under Mont. Code Ann. § 27-19-201. The city was entitled to a preliminary injunction because it made a prima facie showing of the existence of a duly executed contract between itself and the county, and a violation of its rights under the contract by virtue of the county's unilateral decision to breach the agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's judgment, vacated the district court's order denying the application for a preliminary injunction, and remanded the matter to the district court for entry of a preliminary injunction preserving the status quo pending a trial on the merits.


 

214 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Samples


DA 06-0552


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 416; 347 Mont. 292; 198 P.3d 803; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 655


October 31, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
December 11, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC 02-0590. Honorable Susan P. Watters, Presiding Judge.
State v. Samples, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 633 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Yellowstone County, Montana, to the offense of failure to register as a sex offender Defendant reserved the right to appeal the district court's previous denial of a petition to change defendant's level 3 sexual offender designation.


OVERVIEW: After his release from prison, defendant updated his registration each time he changed his address until defendant moved out of a shelter and became homeless. Defendant did not inform the appropriate authorities that he was no longer staying at the shelter. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that the provision of the Sexual and Violent Offender Registration Act requiring an offender to report a change of residence was void for vagueness; the 1999 version of the Act as applied to defendant deprived defendant of his constitutional right to due process of law because the Department of Corrections (DOC) set his sexual offender risk level without notifying him or giving him an opportunity to contest the designation. The supreme court concluded that defendant was denied his right to due process of law when DOC designated him as a level 3 sex offender because defendant did not have the opportunity to know what information was used to designate his risk level, defendant had no right to contest that information, and he had no ability to argue for a different designation.


OUTCOME: Defendant conviction for failure to register as a sex offender was affirmed. Defendant's level 3 sex offender designation is was vacated, and this matter is remanded to the district court for a hearing to appropriately determine defendant's sex offender level.

216 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lindberg


DA 06-0040


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 389; 347 Mont. 76; 196 P.3d 1252; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 634


February 28, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
November 18, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: December 5, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC-2003-519 (B). Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.
State v. Lindberg, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 980 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District (Montana), which convicted him of two felony counts of sexual assault, one felony count of sexual intercourse without consent, and one misdemeanor count of sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for two felony counts of sexual assault, one felony count of sexual intercourse without consent, and one misdemeanor count of sexual assault, but the supreme court affirmed. The victims were his girlfriend's children. While the supreme court did not condone the prosecutor's comments, it declined to invoke plain error review of defendant's claims because the comments did not rise to a level sufficient to invoke the doctrine. The prosecution did not comment upon defendant's post-Miranda silence, but instead offered personal opinions as to the credibility of the witnesses and the significance of defendant's failure to present evidence. Such comments did not have the effect of unconstitutionally shifting the burden of proof to defendant. Defendant did not receive the ineffective assistance of counsel since he failed to show that the prosecution instructed or suggested to a victim how a question should be answered and that, had counsel's objection been timely made, the district court would have concluded that the question was leading and would have been disallowed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

217 of 699 DOCUMENTS


J.C. v. Eleventh Judicial Dist. Court


OP 08-0411


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 358; 346 Mont. 357; 197 P.3d 907; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 588



October 22, 2008, Decided 
October 22, 2008, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother sought a writ of supervisory control pursuant to Mont. R. App. P. 14. The mother alleged that respondent judge had issued unlawful and unconstitutional orders adversely affecting the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The mother was sentenced to prison as a result of her involvement in a botched armed robbery. The child's relatives filed a petition to terminate parental rights, and they sought an order of adoption of the child. In the instant petition, the mother alleged that she has been deprived of her right to parent the child because of the amended petition for termination of parental rights and for adoption filed by the relatives. The supreme court held that the case met the requirements for the exercise of supervisory control. The relatives were not authorized by Mont. Code Ann. § 42-1-107(2) to place the child for adoption. Further, the child's relatives were not authorized under Mont. Code Ann. § 42-2-603(2) to petition for the termination of parental rights. Also, the relatives did not have standing to terminate parental rights based on abuse or neglect of the child. Further, the district court wrongly interpreted Mont. Code Ann. § 40-6-233. The district court erred in determining that the relatives had standing to bring a petition for termination of parental rights; however, the district court should appoint the relatives as guardians, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 72-5-222(1).


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of supervisory control was granted; the mother's request for sanctions against the relatives was denied. The district court's order granting temporary care of the child to the relatives was vacated. The matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

218 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Slade


DA 07-0537


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 341; 346 Mont. 271; 194 P.3d 677; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 574


September 17, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
October 9, 2008, Decided 
October 28, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Hill, Cause No. DC 2007-026. Honorable David Rice, Presiding Judge.
State v. Slade, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 759 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Hill (Montana), denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant was subsequently convicted by the jury of driving under the influence (DUI) and careless driving. Defendant appealed his DUI conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pointed to no caselaw demonstrating that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2) unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to defendant. Moreover, the trial court apprised the jury that evidence of the refusal to submit to a test to detect alcohol or drugs was a permissive, not conclusive, presumption that defendant was intoxicated. Additionally, upon reviewing the jury instructions as a whole, it was evident that the trial court informed the jury that the State had the burden of proving all the elements of the offense charged against defendant beyond a reasonable doubt. In addition, the trial court did not abuse it discretion in limiting defendant's questioning of a trooper under the Sixth Amendment and Mont. Const. art. II, § 24, preventing him from asking about the machine used to administer breath tests and the results that could occur. Also, because the rebuttable presumption in Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2) was constitutional and did not shift the burden of proof to defendant, it was not improper for the prosecutor to comment upon it and defendant's right to a fair trial was not undermined. Finally, the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Nelson v. State


05-694


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 336; 346 Mont. 206; 195 P.3d 293; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 566


October 25, 2006, Argued; November 28, 2006, Submitted 
October 6, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 5, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Liberty, Cause No. DV-03-3237. Honorable David Rice, Presiding Judge.
Nelson v. State, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 3051, 2004 ML 3417 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, widow and personal representative (widow), sought review of a judgment of the District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Liberty (Montana), which granted summary judgment to appellee State of Montana and denied the widow's motion for partial summary judgment in her action alleging that the State negligently and in violation of statute gave a physician's license to a doctor.


OVERVIEW: The doctor went through an extensive process to get his license in Montana because of discipline problems that he had in other states. The deceased had an appointment with the doctor and died before he could follow up. The widow claimed that the State should not have given the doctor his license. The trial court found that the decision of the Montana Board of Medical Examiners was protected by quasi-judicial immunity. The court held that, regardless of whether the Board's actions in investigating the doctor's license application and granting him temporary and permanent medical licenses were discretionary functions, its actions were not undertaken in the context of a controversy or adversarial proceeding as contemplated by Mont. Code Ann. § 2-15-102(10) and thus the Board was not entitled to quasi-judicial immunity for its actions in granting a medical license to the doctor. However, Mont. Code Ann. § 37-3-101 (1997) did not create a special relationship between the State and the deceased giving rise to a special duty. As a result, the statutory special relationship exception to the public duty doctrine did not exits and the State did not owe a duty of care to the deceased.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, even though the court found the trial court's reasoning to be incorrect.


 

220 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Johnston


DA 06-0169


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 318; 346 Mont. 93; 193 P.3d 925; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 473


October 26, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
September 12, 2008, Decided 
October 3, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and For the County of Lake, Cause No. DC 01-24. Honorable Deborah Kim Christopher, Presiding Judge.
State v. Johnston, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 280 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, in and for the County of Lake (Montana), which denied his motion to set aside the revocation of his probation for failure to register as a sex offender and denied his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: While on probation, defendant was arrested several times for various offenses. His probation officer reported all but one of them as probation violations, and he was jailed briefly. Defendant did not assert a violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-1012(4) on direct appeal. The court held that Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-105(2) did not bar defendant's claim that his probation was revoked in violation of the procedures set forth in § 46-23-1012(4); because subject matter jurisdiction was not affected, the State waived the procedural bar of § 46-21-105(2) by raising the issue for the first time on appeal. The court concluded that the term "arrest" in § 46-23-1012(4) was limited to the specific types of arrests that § 46-23-1012(2) permitted a probation officer to initiate; thus, proper procedure was followed when a violation report was made within 10 days of the probation officer's issuance of a warrant, but more than 10 days after an arrest. Due process was adequate without a preliminary probable cause hearing. Although double jeopardy precluded revocation based on violations for which defendant had been jailed and released, the previously unreported offense sufficed for revocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order.

 

221 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Goetz


No. 05-676, No. 05-539


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 296; 345 Mont. 421; 191 P.3d 489; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 444


July 19, 2006, Argued and Submitted 
August 20, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 5, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, Cause Nos. DC-04-354 and DC-04-390. The Honorable Mike Salvagni, Presiding Judge.
State v. Hamper, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1570 (2005)
State v. Goetz, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1569 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Gallatin (Montana), convicting them of felony criminal distribution of dangerous drugs after denying their motions to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were convicted after confidential informants purchased drugs from them while being electronically monitored and recorded. Defendants motions to suppress the recordings made of their conversations with the informants, arguing that the recordings, which were made without a warrant and without their knowledge or consent, violated their constitutional rights, were denied. On appeal, the court held that the electronic monitoring and recording of defendant's conversations with the confidential informants, notwithstanding the consent of the informants, constituted searches subject to the warrant requirement of Mont. Const. art. II, § 11 because defendants had a reasonable expectation of privacy in the conversations they had with the informants in their homes and vehicle. The electronic monitoring and recording of the conversations without a warrant or the existence of an established exception to the warrant requirement violated defendants' rights under Mont. Const. art. II, §§ 10 and 11. Therefore, the district court erred by denying defendants' motions to suppress evidence derived from the warrantless electronic monitoring and recording of the conversations.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions were reversed and the cases were remanded.

State v. Smith


DA 07-0479


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 290N; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 436


June 4, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
August 13, 2008, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Smith, 346 Mont. 545, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 546 (Mont., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Mineral, Cause No. DV 2007-011. Honorable Edward P. McLean, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Fourth Judicial District Court, Mineral County, Montana, entered judgment convicting defendant of failing to adequately secure a load of cargo he was transporting on a commercial vehicle, in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-10-154, Mont. Admin. R. 18.8.1502 (2006), and § 49 C.F.R. 393.1. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A Motor Carrier Services officer cited defendant for violating Mont. Code Ann. § 61-10-154, Mont. Admin. R. 18.8.1502 (2006), and § 49 C.F.R. 393.1 after he inspected a truck defendant was driving and noticed that eight pieces of structural steel were in danger of falling from the load. The charge was tried in a justice court, and a justice of the peace found defendant guilty. Defendant appealed his conviction to a district court and asked for a trial de novo, and the district court convicted defendant after the charge was tried to a jury. The state supreme court affirmed. All errors committed by the justice of the peace were cured when defendant was provided with a trial de novo in district court, defendant waived his right to a speedy trial under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-13-401(2) when he requested and received a continuance, defendant waived his Fourth Amendment right regarding search of his tractor-trailer by driving a commercial vehicle that was subject to inspection under the Code of Federal Regulations, and there was no merit to defendant's claim that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-10-154 was void because the State lacked a device for measuring the force required to secure a load.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

224 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Hernandez v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


OP 07-0745


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 251; 345 Mont. 1; 189 P.3d 638; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 388



July 15, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 1, 2008


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner justice of the peace filed an original petition for declaratory judgment with the court against respondent board of county commissioners, challenging the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. § 3-10-101(5), which provided for the creation of justice's courts of record within Montana counties. The State intervened pursuant to Mont. R. App. P. 27.


OVERVIEW: In accordance with Mont. Code Ann. § 3-10-101(5) the board passed a resolution making the existing county justice court a court of record. The justice argued that Mont. Code Ann. § 3-10-101(5) violated Mont. Const. art. VII, § 1, because justice courts were a specifically-designated constitutional court entitled to constitutional protection. The justice argued that the Legislature could create additional courts, but it could not abolish constitutional courts. The court rejected the justice's argument. Nothing in § 3-10-101(5) indicated an intent to abolish existing justice courts; rather, the statute gave counties a choice of whether they want their justice court to be one of record. The justice next argued that the elimination of de novo trials following appeal from justice's courts of record violated Mont. Const. art. VII, § 4(2). The court held that the phrase "unless otherwise provided by law" in art. VII, § 4(2), gave the Legislature the ability to provide for something other than de novo appeals in district courts.


OUTCOME: The court denied the justice's petition for declaratory judgment.

Newbury v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Ins. Co.


DA 06-0036


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 156; 343 Mont. 279; 184 P.3d 1021; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 225


October 11, 2006, Submitted on Briefs 
May 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 20,2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV-2003-643. Honorable Stewart E. Stadler, Presiding Judge.
Newbury v. State Farm Fire & Casualty Ins., 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1683 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured sought review of an order from the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, in and for the County of Flathead (Montana), which denied his motion for summary judgment and awarded summary judgment to defendant insurer in an action to recover outstanding medical payment benefits.


OVERVIEW: The insured was injured during the course of his employment while attempting to assist the driver of a vehicle stuck in a ditch. The insured incurred $ 18,405 in medical expenses. He received workers' compensation benefits for all but $ 1,175 of the expenses. He had two automobile policies with the insurer. The policies provided medical coverage of $ 5,000 per policy. The insurer paid the remaining $ 1,175. The insured brought an action against the insurer, seeking outstanding medical payment benefits in the amount of $ 8,824. The trial court granted the insurer's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that the workers' compensation provisions in the automobile policies were not ambiguous and did not violate public policy. The insurer was only required to pay the difference between the total medical expenses and the amount required to be paid by the workers' compensation fund. While it was reasonable for the insured to expect that his policies would pay his medical expenses once the workers' compensation fund had paid all it was required to pay, it was not reasonable for him to expect to receive funds in excess of his medical expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Timm v. Mont. Dep't of Pub. HHS


DA 06-0507


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 126; 343 Mont. 11; 184 P.3d 994; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 185


June 26, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
April 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by, On remand at Timm v. Mt. Dep't of Public Health & Human Svcs, 2009 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 190 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. CDV 2005-289. Honorable Thomas C. Honzel, Presiding Judge.
Timm v. Mont. Dep't of Public Health & Human Servs., 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 341 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband and wife challenged a decision of appellee Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services that affirmed a decision of the Montana Board of Assistance as to the wife's Medicaid eligibility. The District Court of the First Judicial District, in and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), affirmed the decision. The husband and wife appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The decision to include the husband's ownership interest in a trucking corporation in the resource application as a countable resource under the no corporation, no trust rule violated the couple's equal protection rights under Mont. Const. art. II, § 4, where the DPHHS failed to explain why the goal of cost control was served by allowing limited liability companies an exclusion of property in some situations, while denying outright any exclusions for property held in a corporate or trust form. The district court also erred in upholding the decision to deny the wife the ability to use her post-eligibility income to pay for nursing home care expenses incurred prior to her Medicaid eligibility because it was contrary to the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services' decision that services incurred prior to Medicaid eligibility had to be considered "not a Medicaid covered service" so long as they were not actually covered by Medicaid. However, the decision not to offset the couple's countable resources by the amount of their accumulated nursing home care expenses was affirmed as there was no legal authority to support the contention.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed as to the conclusion that the inclusion of the husband's interest in the trucking corporation was a countable resource that did not violate the equal protection of the laws. The decision was also reversed as to the conclusion that the wife could not use her post-eligibility income to pay for the nursing home care costs she incurred prior to her Medicaid eligibility. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

In re J.C.


DA 07-0588


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 127; 343 Mont. 30; 183 P.3d 22; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 187


February 20, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
April 21, 2008, Decided 
May 7, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at In re J.D., 2013 Vt. Unpub. LEXIS 63 (Vt., Apr. 1, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, In and For the County of Teton, Cause No. DN 2005-003. Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Department of Public Health and Human Services (DPHHS) filed a petition for adjudication of children in need of care and temporary legal custody of two children. The District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, in and for the County of Teton (Montana), terminated the parental rights of the biological mother and father. The father appealed the termination of his parental rights to his biological son.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that no youth in need of care (YINC) adjudication had occurred and that he had not stipulated that his biological son was a YINC. A YINC adjudication was not required for the DPHHS' temporary investigative authority petition where the father and mother had admitted that their children had been abused and neglected in the treatment plans they entered with the DPHHS. However, the district court erred in concluding that the children had been adjudicated YINC as no adjudication had occurred. Nonetheless, the error was harmless where the father was represented by counsel, stipulated in subsequent proceedings that the child was abused and neglected, and the evidence of abuse and neglect was overwhelming. Moreover, the father neither challenged the evidence of abuse and neglect, argued that he was misled during the subsequent proceedings, nor contended that those proceedings were fundamentally unfair. A reversal would also have had devastating effects on the child's rights under Mont. Const. art. II, § 15, and best interests.


OUTCOME: The termination of the father's and the mother's parental rights was affirmed.

 

228 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


DA 06-0347


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 116; 342 Mont. 485; 182 P.3d 80; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 122


September 6, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
April 9, 2008, Decided 
April 25, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, In and For the County of Toole, Cause No. DC-2005-019. Honorable Marc G. Buyske, Presiding Judge.
State v. Anderson, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 287 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant objected to a jury instruction on the grounds that it did not adequately track the language in Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2), and that its wording unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof to him. The District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, in and for the County of Toole, Montana, overruled the objections. Defendant was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI). Defendant was sentenced. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the district court violated his due process rights under the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Mont. Const. art. II, § 17 by implying to the jury through the instruction that he was required to present evidence rebutting his refusal to submit to a breath test. The court found that the instruction, when viewed in context with the other jury instructions, did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proof to defendant because another instruction made it unmistakably clear that defendant was innocent until proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt and that he was not required to present any evidence at trial. The 1995 amendments to DUI statutes did not constitute an ex post facto law under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Mont. Const. art. II, § 31. The 1995 amendments simply put defendant on notice that if he violated the DUI statute and had prior DUI or BAC convictions which were not expunged those prior violations could elevate a future DUI conviction to the level of a felony. As a result, it was not an ex post facto law, and the district court did not err in including defendant's 1992 BAC conviction for sentencing enhancement purposes.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

229 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


DA 07-0328


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 112; 342 Mont. 461; 182 P.3d 62; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 116


February 27, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
April 8, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC 06-206(C), Honorable Stewart E. Stadler, Presiding Judge.
State v. Clark, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 248 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, in and for the County of Flathead (Montana), which sentenced him to 15 years in prison, with 10 years suspended, for aggravated assault.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled nolo contendere to aggravated assault. The trial court sentenced him to 15 years in prison, with 10 years suspended. The trial court awarded defendant no credit for the time spent on formal house arrest after he was released on bond. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court imposed an illegal sentence when it failed to award credit for the time spent on house arrest. The court found that because defendant's sentence fell within the parameters of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-202(2), the sentence constituted a legal sentence. Further, no statute required or authorized a trial court to award credit for time served on house arrest prior to conviction or while released on bond, regardless of the formal nature of the house arrest. The trial court was not statutorily required to award defendant credit for time served on house arrest. Defendant's sentence fell within the statutory parameters for aggravated assault, and thus, the trial court did not impose an illegal sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Kirkland


DA 06-0749


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 107; 342 Mont. 365; 181 P.3d 616; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 105


November 21, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
April 1, 2008, Decided 
April 17, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Cause No. DC-05-151. Honorable Jeffrey H. Langton, Presiding Judge.
State v. Kirkland, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1044 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, in and for the County of Ravalli (Montana), which ordered him to pay $ 654 for the costs of counsel appointed to represent him in a revocation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to two counts of felony issuing a bad check. The trial court deferred imposition of sentence for a five-year period on each count. The State later filed a petition to revoke the deferred sentences. The trial court sentenced defendant to prison. The trial court also ordered him to pay $ 654 for the costs of counsel appointed to represent him in the revocation proceeding. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court imposed an illegal sentence when it ordered him to pay the costs of his court-appointed counsel. The court found that the trial court's imposition of the costs was within the parameters of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-8-113(1). The trial court's alleged failure to abide by the requirement of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-8-114 that it specify in its written judgment that payment of counsel costs be made to the Montana Office of the State Public Defender rendered imposition of the costs merely objectionable, not illegal. Defendant failed to present a colorable claim that his sentence fell outside statutory parameters and warranted review under the Lenihan rule. Consequently, the court declined to consider his arguments raised for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

231 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Miller


DA 07-0140


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 106; 342 Mont. 355; 181 P.3d 625; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 107


February 13, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
April 1, 2008, Decided 
April 17, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC 2006-0128, Honorable G. Todd Baugh, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Thirteenth Judicial District Court of Yellowstone County, Montana, convicted defendant of driving a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol and/or drugs, driving while license was suspended or revoked, and operating a motor vehicle without proof of liability insurance in effect. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the jury instruction derived from Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2) violated his right against self-incrimination and due process rights as it undermined the other instructions regarding the State's burden of proof and placed on defendant the burden of having to prove his innocence by giving a breath test. The supreme court disagreed, finding first that defendant's conclusory assertion that § 61-8-404(2) was "unconstitutional on its face" was a wholly inadequate presentation of an issue. Further, nothing about the instruction required the jury to infer from defendant's refusal that he was under the influence. To the contrary, the jurors were told that they "may" infer from his refusal that he was under the influence. The jurors were also instructed that defendant was presumed innocent, that the presumption was not overcome unless, from all the evidence, they could find him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt, and that defendant was not required to prove his innocence. As such, the jury was fully and fairly instructed regarding the applicable law and burden of proof was not unconstitutionally shifted to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
