State v. Michaud


DA 06-0553


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 88; 342 Mont. 244; 180 P.3d 636; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 98


July 25, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
March 18, 2008, Decided 
April 3, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC 2005-551. Honorable John W. Larson, Presiding Judge.
State v. Michaud, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 616 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in Justice Court for second offense misdemeanor driving under the influence (DUI). Defendant appealed, and the Fourth Judicial District of Missoula County, Montana, convicted him of misdemeanor driving under the influence. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the district court erred by limiting his right to voir dire the jury to 15 minutes; the district court abused its discretion by allowing police officer testimony pertaining to the Horizontal Gaze Nystagmus (HGN) test; and the inference contained in Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2) violated his due process rights. The supreme court held that the district court did not abuse its discretion in imposing the time-limit as it engaged in a comprehensive voir dire before turning the jury over to counsel, and counsel had the opportunity to engage in a colloquy with the jurors. However, the supreme court agreed that the State failed to establish the necessary foundation for admission of the officer's testimony on the HGN results or the inference he drew from these results; further, the State failed to meet its burden of proving that this admission was harmless. The inference in question was permissive and did not violate due process in that there was a rational connection between driving while intoxicated and refusing to take a sobriety test. Defendant had the opportunity to present evidence or argument to rebut the presumption, but did not do so.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed and the matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

233 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Weaver


DA 06-0366


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 86; 342 Mont. 196; 179 P.3d 534; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 87


May 16, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
March 12, 2008, Decided 
March 28, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-2005-160. Honorable John S. Henson, Presiding Judge.
State v. Weaver, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 481 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula (Montana), convicting him, pursuant to a guilty plea, of felony operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol or drugs (DUI) in violation of Mont. Code Ann. §§ 61-8-401, 61-8-731.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the district court erred by denying his motion to dismiss the DUI charge because his 1996 DUI conviction was invalid and could not be used as the basis for a charge of felony DUI. The court held that the district court did not err by denying defendant's motion to dismiss because it correctly held that the 1996 conviction could be used as a prior conviction to support the felony DUI charge, as the State presented sufficient oral and documentary evidence to support the conclusion that the 1996 conviction was not entered in violation of defendant's right to be present at the trial. The evidence showed that defendant appeared in court on April 22, 1996 and entered a plea of not guilty, that a public defender was appointed to represent defendant, that defendant stayed sufficiently in contact with the public defender to have her move to continue the August 30, 1996 trial due to defendant's health problems, and that defendant either knew of the November 20, 1996 trial date and was willfully absent or kept himself deliberately ignorant of the trial date. The 1996 trial was properly held without defendant's presence under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-16-122 (1995).


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

234 of 699 DOCUMENTS


In re Mental Health of A.S.B.


DA 06-0687


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 82; 342 Mont. 169; 180 P.3d 625; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 84


August 15, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
March 11, 2008, Decided 
March 27, 2008, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DI 06-082B, Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, in and for the County of Flathead, Montana, involuntarily committed appellant patient to the Montana State Hospital. The district court concluded that the patient suffered from a mental disorder that created an imminent threat of injury to himself or others. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient argued that Mont. Code Ann. § 53-21-126(1)(d) was unconstitutional because it purported to allow involuntary commitment based on the mere possibility that an individual's condition may worsen to a point where he posed a threat of harm to himself or others. The supreme court noted that the patient did not present his challenge to the constitutionality of the statute to the district court. The supreme court found that the district court's determination that the patient's mental condition would likely deteriorate if left untreated was not clearly erroneous. The State was not required to prove that the patient's mental condition would deteriorate if left untreated. There was substantial credible evidence that there was an imminent threat of injury to the patient. In light of the non-hearsay testimony received regarding the patient's mental disorder, the incorporation of the State's expert's report into the district court's order was harmless error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

235 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hood


DA 07-0100


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 78N; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 75


January 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
March 4, 2008, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hood, 2008 MT 78N, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 124 (Mar. 4, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. ADC-05-311. Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Presiding Judge.
State v. Hood, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 66 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade, Montana, imposed a restitution sentencing condition following defendant's conviction of the offense of arson. Defendant appealed from the condition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentencing condition (1) was illegal under applicable statutes, (2) was an unconstitutionally excessive fine for which he sought plain error review, and (3) violated his right to due process because one could not be required to pay restitution at a rate greater than one could reasonably bear. Defendant's arguments on appeal were not raised in the district court. Indeed, no objections were made to the restitution condition. The court found that defendant's due process claim was premature because nothing of record indicated that defendant's suspended sentence was revoked for failure to pay restitution despite his good faith efforts. The restitution defendant was ordered to pay was within statutory parameters because restitution was statutorily required. The other claimed errors did not go to the legality of the sentence, but only to alleged statutory errors. Thus, defendant's claims were not within the exception to the requirement that claims for review of a sentencing issue must first have been raised in the district court by way of an objection. Finally, the court declined to exercise plain error review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

236 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Bean v. State


DA 07-0049


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 67; 342 Mont. 85; 179 P.3d 524; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 65


January 16, 2008, Submitted on Briefs 
February 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. ADV 2004-707. Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Presiding Judge.
Bean v. State, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 861 (2006)
Bean v. State, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 283 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the State of Montana and the Montana Public Employee Retirement Administration, appealed two orders from the First Judicial District Court, Lewis and Clark County (Montana), which concluded that Mont. Code Ann. § 19-13-210(2) violated the equal protection rights of plaintiff, a National Guard firefighter hired before October 1, 2001, and awarding attorney fees and costs to plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: Section 19-13-210(2) differentiated between two similarly situated classes of employees, i.e., Guard firefighters who were hired on or after October 1, 2001, and who could participate in the firefighters retirement system, and those hired before the cut-off date who remained in the public employee retirement system. Plaintiff belonged to the latter group. On review, the supreme court noted that constitutional provisions against discrimination did not forbid statutes and statutory changes to have a beginning, and thus to discriminate between the rights of an earlier and later time. The alleged distinction would end once all Guard firefighters hired before October 1, 2001, retired. The statute represented a legislative choice to provide a prospective retirement solution for all newly hired Guard firefighters without affecting the retirement expectations of existing Guard firefighters. The statute operated equally upon members of each class of firefighters. The legislative approach to correcting a "long standing inequity" between Guard firefighters and other firefighters did not violate plaintiff's right to equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court orders granting summary judgment and awarding attorney fees and costs to plaintiff.


 

237 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Saucier v. McDonald's Rests. of Mont., Inc.


DA 06-0244


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 63; 342 Mont. 29; 179 P.3d 481; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 67; 102 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1584


January 10, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
February 26, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 14, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DV-2003-279. Honorable Gregory R. Todd, Presiding Judge.
Saucier v. McDonald's of Mont., 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1814 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limited guardian sued defendant restaurant chain and manager, alleging tort and discrimination claims arising from the manager's sexual relationship with her mentally disabled niece. The District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Yellowstone (Montana), granted the restaurant chain and manager summary judgment on all claims except the discrimination claims against the manager. The guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The restaurant chain failed to establish a complete absence of facts as to the niece's ability to effectively consent where there was some evidence that her mental disability precluded her from effectively consenting to sexual conduct with a supervisor in an employment setting. The non-consensual sex went beyond any reasonable conception of sexual harassment and fell outside the Montana Human Rights Act's definition of discrimination in employment. The allegations of non-consensual sex sounded in tort and not in discrimination. While the guardian sought relief for discrimination in the Department of Labor and Industry, she also sought relief in the district court for tortious conduct. When the Human Rights Commission held that she had not stated a cognizable claim for discrimination, she was free to pursue relief for the alleged tortious conduct in district court, so long as her claim was not grounded upon underlying allegations of discrimination. Since the claims sounded in tort, the guardian was not barred by Mont. Code Ann. § 49-2-509(7) (2001) from proceeding in district court. However, she was barred from proceeding on her discrimination claims against the restaurant chain.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment on the discrimination claims was affirmed. The order granting summary judgment on the tort claims against the restaurant chain and the manager was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.


 

238 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Wamsley v. Nodak Mut. Ins. Co.


DA 06-0194


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 56; 341 Mont. 467; 178 P.3d 102; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 56


February 14, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
February 19, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Cause No. DV 2003-336, Honorable Holly B. Brown, Presiding Judge.
Wamsley v. Nodak Mutual Ins. Co., 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1790 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Gallatin, Montana, rendered judgment against appellant insurer pursuant to Mont. R. Civ. P. 54 on appellees', estate personal representatives (estate), suit for damages from an August 2002 automobile accident in which the decedents were killed. The district court held that the estate could stack all three underinsured motorist (UIM) policies. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the insurer waived its right to argue the defense of lack of personal jurisdiction. The insurer's participation in the court proceedings constituted a voluntary appearance under Mont. R. Civ. P. 4B(2), thus admitting the jurisdiction of the district court. The district court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the insurer's motion to stay the proceedings in Montana until the North Dakota declaratory judgment was decided. Montana law applied to the stacking and coverage issues as Montana was where the accident occurred and the damages arose. The basic elements of res judicata were satisfied by the North Dakota rulings. However, the district court did not err in declining to accord full faith and credit to the rulings issued by the North Dakota courts as the judgment in North Dakota was brought for the purpose of preempting the district court in Montana from exercising control over the judicial processes necessary to resolve the dispute. Collateral estoppel did not preclude the estate from litigating its UIM claims in Montana. Principles of comity did not require Montana courts to defer to the rulings from the North Dakota Supreme Court.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

239 of 699 DOCUMENTS



St. James Healthcare v. Cole


DA 07-0084


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 44; 341 Mont. 368; 178 P.3d 696; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 48


October 24, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
February 12, 2008, Decided 
March 5, 2008, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by St. James Healthcare v. Cole, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 80 (Mont., Feb. 12, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Second Judicial District, In and For the County of Silver Bow, Cause No. DV-2006-264. Honorable Kurt Krueger, Presiding Judge.
St. James Healthcare v. Cole, 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 62 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Second Judicial District, County of Silver Bow, Montana, granted the motion of plaintiff, a health care facility (the facility), to permanently enjoin defendant, a physician who formerly headed the facility's radiology department (the physician), after determining that the facility met its burden under Mont. Code Ann. § 27-19-201. The physician appealed.


OVERVIEW: The physician maintained that the injunction was an unconstitutional prior restraint on his right to free speech under U.S. Const. amend. I and Mont. Const. art. II, § 7. Paragraphs (a), (b), (c), and (f), were not infirm because these paragraphs were all pinpointed precisely toward forms of speech and conduct which were not constitutionally protected. Paragraph (d), however, swept too broadly and was stricken since it did not prohibit conduct which was embarrassing, annoying, or harassing. Paragraph (e) also was overbroad insofar as it enjoined discouraging conversation between the physician and potential candidates for the position of head of the radiology department; on the other hand, portions of paragraph (e), which enjoined the physician from "intimidating" speech and conduct, were not constitutionally protected. Also, (1) sufficient evidence justified enjoining the physician from the harassing and intimidating conduct described in the injunction; (2) the facility had standing to seek a protective order for certain third parties; and (3) injunctive relief was available to the facility even though money damages were available to remedy the alleged harm.


OUTCOME: The district court did not manifestly abuse its discretion in issuing paragraphs (a), (b), (c) and (f) of the injunction; however, the district court did manifestly abuse its discretion in issuing paragraph (d) and a portion of paragraph (e). Consequently, the district court's action was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings.

Wilkes v. Mont. State Fund


DA 07-0206


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 29; 341 Mont. 292; 177 P.3d 483; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 29


December 6, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
February 5, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 25, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana. Honorable James Jeremiah Shea, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged a judgment of the Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana, denying his motion for summary judgment and granting appellee Montana State Fund's motion for summary judgment in his action contending that Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-703(5) was unconstitutional under the Equal Protection Clause, U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Mont. Const. art. II, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sustained a permanent neck injury in the course and scope of his employment as a part-time school bus driver. He worked principally as a farmer and was unable to return to farming. The State Fund denied the claimant permanent partial disability (PPD) benefits after he achieved maximum medical improvement pursuant to § 39-71-703(5) on the ground that he had suffered no actual wage loss from his bus driving job, as he returned to work and earned the same wage. The trial court held that the statute was constitutional because it properly distinguished workers with actual wage loss from workers without actual wage loss in awarding PPD benefits. On appeal, the court held that although there were several similarities between the classes, a difference existed, namely actual wage loss. This difference was fundamental in light of the legislature's declaration that the wage-loss benefit should bear a reasonable relationship to actual wages lost as a result of work-related injury or disease. The distinguishing factor also related to the underlying justification of § 39-71-703(5).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

241 of 699 DOCUMENTS


In re T.S.B.


DA 07-0372


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 23; 341 Mont. 204; 177 P.3d 429; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 18


November 28, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
January 29, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 15, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDJ 07-026-Y (b), Honorable Julie Macek, Presiding Judge.
In re K.J.B., 2007 MT 216, 339 Mont. 28, 168 P.3d 629, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 401 (2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order from the Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County (Montana), terminating his parental rights to his infant child. The issues on appeal were whether the termination, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. §§ 41-3-609(1)(d) and 41-3-423(2)(e), violated the father's constitutional right to due process and whether the district court abused its discretion in terminating the father's parental rights to the child.


OVERVIEW: The father previously had his parental rights involuntarily terminated to all five of his other living children due to his inability to parent. While an adjudication hearing was not required, Mont. Code Ann. § 41-3-609(1)(d) still required a determination that the child was abused or neglected. The statutory scheme did not deprive the father of due process because the district court still had to determine that the child was at substantial risk of harm. The state had to show that the father had his parental rights involuntarily terminated to the child's siblings and that those terminations were relevant to his ability to parent. The father failed to meet his burden of showing that the lack of an adjudication hearing in a Mont. Code Ann. § 41-3-609(1)(d) proceeding was unconstitutional. The statutory scheme did not create a presumption against the father as the burden to show the child was at risk remained on the state. The State established by clear and convincing evidence that the father had his parental rights to all five siblings involuntarily terminated, and that the circumstances related to those terminations were relevant to his inability to care for this child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

Flathead Citizens for Quality Growth, Inc. v. Flathead County Bd. of Adjustment


DA 06-0173


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2008 MT 1; 341 Mont. 1; 175 P.3d 282; 2008 Mont. LEXIS 3


February 28, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
January 3, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 23, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV-2005-503(A) Honorable Stewart E. Stadler, Presiding Judge.
Flathead Citizens for Quality Growth v. Flathead County Bd. of Adjustment, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 360 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens group filed suit against appellee Board of Adjustment, challenging a decision by the Board to issue a conditional use permit (CUP) to allow appellant property owner to extract and crush gravel on the owner's land. The owner intervened, arguing that the CUP was too narrow in scope. The Eleventh Judicial District Court, Flathead County, Montana, granted summary judgment to the Board. The group and the owner both appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the group contended the district court erred in concluding the issuance of the CUP was lawful under the zoning regulations; the owner contended the district court erred in concluding that under Mont. Code Ann. § 76-2-209, the Board could issue a CUP which prohibited asphalt and concrete batch operations. The supreme court disagreed with the owner, finding that the zoning regulations and the neighborhood plan at issue demonstrated that the district had been specifically zoned to promote and regulate residential use and was a "residential" district for purposes of § 76-2-209, even though the district permitted other uses. Thus, the Board was authorized to prohibit concrete and asphalt batch operations. However, the supreme court also agreed with the citizens on their points, finding, inter alia, that the Board abused its discretion in issuing the CUP because it failed to provide a factual foundation for its decision, other than a belief that compliance with unspecified Department of Environmental Quality regulations would automatically be sufficient to discharge its duties under the local zoning regulations.


OUTCOME: The district court's conclusion that the Board had the power to prohibit asphalt and concrete batch plant operations in the CUP was affirmed; the district court's conclusion that the Board did not abuse its discretion in issuing the CUP was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Graham


DA 06-0670


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 358; 340 Mont. 366; 175 P.3d 885; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 612


November 8, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
December 31, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 18, 2008


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC 2005-0944. Honorable Russell C. Fagg, Presiding Judge.
State v. Graham, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 983 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by information with a felony DUI and failure to carry personal liability insurance. At trial before the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Montana, defendant moved to suppress evidence. Defendant was ultimately convicted on both counts. Defendant appealed the district court's denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: An officer saw a pickup stopped on a dirt pull out, within plain sight of the road. The officer noticed defendant and his girlfriend kissing inside the truck, and the officer became concerned that the couple was about to engage in inappropriate sexual behavior. The first issue presented on appeal was whether the district court erred in concluding that there was no particularized suspicion to justify the officer's initial seizure of defendant. Once the officer activated her emergency lights, defendant was seized within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment and Mont. Const. art. II, § 11. Any particularized suspicion which arose did so only after defendant was seized. Moreover, the officer did not approach the vehicle because she believed a crime was being committed, as Mont. Code Ann. § 46-5-401(1) required. The second issue presented was whether the district court erred in concluding that the community caretaker doctrine provided a justification for the officer's seizure of defendant. The supreme court declined to extend the doctrine to include an exception that would allow an officer to detain a person based on solely personal dissatisfaction with the person's conduct.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's conclusion that the officer did not have particularized suspicion for her investigative stop of defendant. The supreme court reversed the district court's denial of defendant's motion to suppress. The matter was remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.

2007 MT 336; 340 Mont. 242; 174 P.3d 475; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 588


July 11, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
December 13, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. ADV 2004-792. Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Presiding Judge.
Adgerson v. State, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 389 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the order entered by the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, denying his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted appellant of felony stalking for conduct he directed toward his ex-wife. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. In postconviction proceedings, he claimed: (1) that the trial court committed evidentiary error; and (2) that he received the ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The Supreme Court of Montana held that appellant's challenge to the trial court's admission of evidence was procedurally barred by Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-105(2). Appellant's claim that due process required reversal of his conviction due to the trial court's erroneous admission of the other crimes/acts evidence was not preserved for review. Appellate counsel did not render ineffective assistance by failing to raise on appeal the issue of whether the trial court abused its discretion in allowing the State to present other crimes/acts evidence at trial. Counsel believed that the determination to admit the other crimes/acts evidence was within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Knudson


DA 06-0485


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 324; 340 Mont. 167; 174 P.3d 469; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 580


October 24, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
December 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 28, 2007.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by State v. Knudson, 2008 MT 43N, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 43 (Feb. 8, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Chouteau, Cause No. DC-05-18, Honorable David Rice, Presiding Judge.
State v. Knudson, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 631 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant registered sexual offender was charged with failing to report his change of address as required by Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-505 (2005), which did not define "address." The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, in and for the County of Chouteau (Montana) denied defendant's motion to dismiss the charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: When defendant first registered his address with the local sheriff's department, as required by the Sexual or Violent Offender Registration Act, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-501, et seq. (2005), he lived in his father's house in a municipality in which all mail was delivered to post office boxes. Defendant registered as his address his post office box rather than the address of his father's house. Defendant later began to reside at his girlfriend's house in the same municipality, although he maintained a room at his father's house and occasionally slept there. Defendant retained the same post office box as his mailing address. The appellate court, referring to U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Mont. Const. art. II, § 17, held that Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-505 was unconstitutionally vague as applied to the particular circumstances of defendant's case; because the statute's text did not require defendant to register using a residential address, he did not have actual notice, from either the statute or the officials enforcing it, that a mailing address was insufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

City of Three Forks v. Schillinger


DA 06-0446


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 331; 340 Mont. 211; 173 P.3d 681; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 582


February 28, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
December 11, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Cause No. DC 05-372, Honorable Mike Salvagni, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Madison County Justice Court, Montana, convicted defendant of one count of endangering the welfare of a minor and acquitted him on three counts of the same offense. Defendant appealed. The District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Montana, remanded the remaining three counts to the Three Forks City Court, Montana, for trial. The City of Three Forks appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in the Three Forks City Court with four counts of endangering the welfare of a minor. The jury convicted him of one count and acquitted him on three counts. On appeal, the Gallatin County District Court erred in remanding the case back to the Three Forks City Court for a new trial. A trial de novo in the district court pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-17-311(1) was the only remedy to which defendant was entitled.

247 of 699 DOCUMENTS



State v. PPL Mont., Inc.


DA 06-0477


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 310; 340 Mont. 124; 172 P.3d 1241; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 567


June 13, 2007, Argued and Submitted 
December 4, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 24, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDV 2005-273. Honorable Dirk M. Sandefur, Presiding Judge.
Mt. Dep't of Revenue v. PPL Mt., LLC, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 524 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility claimed that appellee Montana Department of Revenue (DOR) deprived the utility of constitutional equal protection when it assessed the utility's property taxes. The parties cross-appealed from the determination of the Eight Judicial District Court, Cascade County, Montana.


OVERVIEW: The utility acquired most of a power company's electric generation assets as part of Montana's deregulation of its electric power industry. DOR determined, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 15-23-101(2), that the utility was operating a single and continuous property in more than one county. DOR centrally assessed the utility's newly acquired property. The utility challenged the assessment. The State Tax Appeals Board (STAB) determined that DOR had calculated properly the intangible personal property exemption and the value of the property. STAB then adjusted down the fair market value of the property for all three years. At issue was whether the property tax assessment deprived the utility of constitutional equal protection. The federal Equal Protection Clause did not prevent a State from assessing taxes on a company's property based on the use to which a company put those assets in its larger system or business. The outcome would be the same under Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. The supreme court could not conclude that DOR treated the utility differently. The supreme court could not conclude under these circumstances that STAB's finding was clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the district court's judgment.


 

248 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Oberson v. USDA


No. OP 06-0232


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 293; 339 Mont. 519; 171 P.3d 715; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 536


April 20, 2007, Argued; May 1, 2007, Submitted 
November 7, 2007, Decided 
November 27, 2007, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
ORIGINAL PROCEEDING: Certified Question, U.S. Court of Appeals Ninth Circuit. The Hon. William W. Schwarzer, Senior District Judge; Hon. Ronald M. Gould and Hon. Marsha S. Berzon, Circuit Judges.
Oberson v. USDA, 441 F.3d 703, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 6829 (9th Cir. Mont., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a legal guardian and a mother, sued defendant United States Department of Agriculture, Forest Service, under the Federal Tort Claims Act. The U.S. Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit certified the following: (1) whether the standard in Mont. Code Ann. § 23-2-653 (1996) violated Mont. Const. art. II, § 4, (2) if so, did the standard in Mont. Code Ann. § 70-16-302(1) (1996) apply, and (3) if not, did Mont. Code Ann. § 27-1-701 apply?


OVERVIEW: The guardian alleged that the incapacitated person was injured when the Forest Service failed to correct or warn of a danger posed by a hill. The appellate court certified questions of law to the court regarding the proper standard of care. The court first found that gross negligence provision in Mont. Code Ann. § 23-2-653 (1995) was overbroad and violated the Montana Equal Protection Clause under Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. The court had previously found that the skier responsibility statutes under Mont. Code Ann. §§ 23-2-731 - 23-2-737 violated equal protection guarantees and the court discerned no difference between the snowmobile liability statute's purpose and the skier responsibility statute's purpose. The court struck only those provisions of Mont. Code Ann. § 23-2-653 that applied a gross negligence standard of care and the court left intact the remainder of the statute. The willful or wanton misconduct standard of care in Mont. Code Ann. § 70-16-302(1) had no application under these circumstances. The general statutory duty of due care set forth in Mont. Code Ann. § 27-1-701 provided the standard of care to govern the Forest Services' actions in this case.


OUTCOME: The court answered yes, no, and yes, respectively, to the three questions certified to the court.

 

249 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bullman


DA 06-0761


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 288; 339 Mont. 461; 171 P.3d 681; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 533


October 10, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
November 6, 2007, Decided 
November 27, 2007, Released for Publication


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDC 99-247, Honorable Kenneth R. Neill, Presiding Judge.
State v. Bullman, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 982 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), which denied his petition filed against the State for sex offender re-designation pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-509(4) (2005).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pleaded guilty to sexual intercourse without consent with a 15-year-old. Defendant petitioned the trial court to reduce his level III sexual offender registration to a level II designation based on his successful completion of sex offender treatment. The trial court denied the petition. On appeal, the court reversed. The trial court erred in applying Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-509(4) (2005). The plain language of § 46-23-509(4), when construed with its applicability provision, stood for the proposition that level III sex offenders convicted on or after August 21, 2002, could not petition for re-designation of their sex offender status. Defendant was sentenced in February 2000 and thus the amended statute did not apply to preclude defendant's petition. Thus, the trial court erred in dismissing his petition based on the amended statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

 

250 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Silvestrone v. Park County


DA 06-0843


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 261; 339 Mont. 299; 170 P.3d 950; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 501


August 15, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
October 17, 2007, Decided 
November 14, 2007, Released for Publication


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Silvestrone v. Park County, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 558 (Mont., Nov. 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, In and For the County of Park, Cause No. DV-06-67, Honorable Wm. Nels Swandal, Presiding Judge.
Silvestrone v. Park County, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 941 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizen challenged a decision of the District Court of the Sixth Judicial District, in and for the County of Park (Montana), which denied him summary judgment and granted respondent county summary judgment in connection with the citizen's tort action claiming actual damages and emotional distress.


OVERVIEW: The citizen claimed damage stemming from a justice of the peace's wrongfully issued arrest warrant against him. The trial court granted the county summary judgment and the court affirmed on appeal. The court held that the citizen was not able to avoid the application of Mont. Code Ann. § 2-9-112, which codified the doctrine of judicial immunity. The citizen was not free to challenge the statute's constitutionality for the first time on appeal. The justice of the peace's issuance of the warrant constituted a judicial act for purposes of Mont. Code Ann. § 3-10-401 and the execution of the warrant represented the judicial power of the State put into action. The grant of the citizen's motion to withdraw a guilty plea and the remand of that case to the justice court also constituted judicial acts, for purposes of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-20-703, and the failure of the county courts to remand the matter constituted an omission as opposed to an affirmative judicial act. The acts and omissions that led to the citizen's arrest fell within the immunity afforded to the county under Mont. Code Ann. § 2-9-112(1) and thus the county was entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

251 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ulrigg


DA 06-0213


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 239N; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 426


February 28, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
September 18, 2007, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Ulrigg, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 478 (Mont., Sept. 18, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-04-366. Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Presiding Judge.
State v. Ulrigg, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 410 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), which required him to reimburse the State for the cost of prosecution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised certain issues on appeal, but the court affirmed and remanded for the entry of an amended judgment. The court agreed with the State that the $ 50 fee imposed in defendant's sentence for the "cost of prosecution" was actually imposed to pay the cost of defendant's court-appointed defense counsel, and thus was not improper under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-8-113(1). Although the trial court's written judgment referred to the fee imposed as a "cost of prosecution," this did not accurately identify the purpose for which the fee was really imposed. The record showed that the fee was clearly for the purpose of reimbursing the cost of defendant's two public defenders, but the fee was incorrectly termed a "cost of prosecution." The entry of an amended judgment in this regard was ordered. Although defendant claimed that Mont. Code Ann. § 45-6-101(2) was unconstitutional under Apprendi, this rule did not apply to the imposition of restitution, and thus the trial court did not err in ordering defendant to pay restitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, but remanded for the entry of an amended judgment assessing costs for court-appointed defense counsel instead of the "cost of prosecution."

 

252 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ellis


DA 06-0289


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 210; 339 Mont. 14; 167 P.3d 896; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 394


March 14, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
August 28, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Cause No. DC-05-91. Honorable Jeffrey H. Langton, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the portion of the judgment entered by the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Ravalli County, Montana, ordering him to repay the costs of his appointed counsel upon his guilty plea to a felony criminal offense.


OVERVIEW: In a criminal appeal, defendant claimed that the district court erred in ordering him to repay the costs of his appointed counsel because Mont. Code Ann. § 46-8-113 violated the equal protection clauses of the United States and Montana Constitutions. The Supreme Court of Montana disagreed. Defendant failed to establish that Mont. Code Ann. § 46-8-113 resulted in different treatment of similarly-situated individuals. Contrary to defendant's claim, individuals ordered to pay recoupment costs as a condition of a felony criminal sentence were not similarly situated to civil judgment debtors. The process of adjudicating a civil judgment generally did not include determinations that the judgment debtor committed a criminal offense against the State and its people, that the public purse was expended to defend the judgment debtor, or that the judgment debtor had the ability to pay the debt. Therefore, defendant's equal protection challenge failed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Thompson v. State


DA 06-0365


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 185; 338 Mont. 511; 167 P.3d 867; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 386


November 15, 2006, Argued; December 5, 2006, Submitted 
August 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 7, 2007


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: Montana Workers' Compensation Court, WCC 2004-1089 Honorable James Jeremiah Shea, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent workers petitioned for a declaratory judgment against appellant, the State of Montana. They sought a declaration that the claimant disclosure waiver provisions set forth in Mont. Code Ann. §§ 39-71-604(3), 50-16-527(5) violated their constitutional rights. The Montana Workers' Compensation Court (WCC) granted the workers' summary judgment and awarded attorney's fees and costs against the State. The State and two intervenors appealed.


OVERVIEW: The workers' filed claims for workers' compensation benefits. They sought a declaratory judgment stating that the claimant disclosure procedures, Mont. Code Ann. §§ 39-71-604(3), 50-16-527(5), violated their right to privacy under Mont. Const. II, art. § 10 and the right to due process of law under Mont. Const. art. II, § 17. The WCC erred in concluding that it had jurisdiction to issue a declaratory judgment. The WCC was a court of limited jurisdiction; it had the authority to issue declaratory rulings only in the context of a dispute concerning benefits. Here, the workers' petition did not demand a declaratory judgment concerning the applicability of workers' compensation statutes to a particular dispute over benefits. Mont. Code Ann. § 27-8-311 did not authorize the WCC's award of attorney's fees and costs against the State.


OUTCOME: The WCC's judgment was reversed.


 

254 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jackson


No. DA 06-0168


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 186; 338 Mont. 344; 165 P.3d 321; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 359


June 26, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
August 6, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Released for Publication August 21, 2007


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, In and for the County of Toole, Cause No. DC 02-030, The Honorable Marc G. Buyske, Presiding Judge.
State v. Jackson, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 301 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the District Court of the Ninth Judicial District, in and for the County of Toole (Montana), which, in response to the inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus, sentenced him to six years in the Montana State Prison (MSP) after finding that an illegal sentence had been previously entered.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was sentenced to six years in the Montana Department of Corrections (DOC). In a petition seeking habeas corpus, he alleged that his six-year commitment to the DOC violated Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-201(3)(d)(i). The trial court then entered a six-year sentence in the MSP. This appeal followed. In reversing, the appellate court held that the inmate was allowed to use habeas corpus proceedings in order to attack the illegal sentence given originally, pursuant to Mont. Const. art. II, § 19. The procedural bar to such a challenge set forth in Mont. Code Ann. § 46-22-101(2) was found to be unconstitutional in the Lott case. Next, the inmate did not waive his right to challenge the sentence. The State did not object to the challenge at the time the petition was filed; also, it admitted that the sentence was illegal and stated that the proper remedy was re-sentencing. Finally, the inmate's due process rights were violated because a sentence to the MSP was more burdensome. Nothing in the record indicated that the trial court based the more burdensome sentence on objective information concerning identifiable conduct of the inmate after the original sentencing.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for re-sentencing.

Bingman v. Mahoney


Docket No. OP 07-0371


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 Mont. LEXIS 411



July 31, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Bingman v. State, 2005 MT 272, 329 Mont. 151, 122 P.3d 1235, 2005 Mont. LEXIS 459 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed a petition seeking a writ of habeas corpus in which he alleged that the district court erred in 1986 when it sentenced him to ten years for felony assault plus an additional ten years for use of a weapon, under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-221(1)(1985). He argued that a weapon enhancement for use of a weapon violated the double jeopardy clause. He also contended that the writ of habeas corpus could never be suspended, and thus he could raise this issue some twenty-one years after imposition of the original sentence in 1986. The Supreme Court of Montana held that the habeas claim was barred by res judicata. Petitioner had already filed a postconviction challenge to the weapon enhancement. Furthermore, the collateral attack on his conviction and sentence was barred by the applicable five-year statute of limitations.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

State v. Hamilton


DA 06-0590


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 167; 338 Mont. 142; 164 P.3d 884; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 284


April 25, 2007, Submitted on Briefs 
July 11, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 8, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State v. Hamilton, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 371 (Mont., Aug. 8, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-05-624. Honorable John W. Larson, Presiding Judge.
State v. Hamilton, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 674 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with, and ultimately pled guilty to, felony failure to register as a sexual offender. He appealed an order of the Fourth Judicial District Court, Missoula County, Montana, denying his motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: As a sixteen-year-old youth in 1996, defendant pled guilty to communication with a minor for immoral purposes (CMIP) in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.090. He was ordered to register as a sex offender in Washington. In October 2005, the Montana Legislature amended Montana's Sexual and Violent Offender Registration Act, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-23-502(6), so that offenders had to register in Montana if they had to register for an offense in some other jurisdiction. In November 2005, defendant was implicated in a Montana crime and charged with felony failure to register as a sexual offender. Defendant was not entitled to dismiss the charge. The offense for which he was convicted in Washington was equivalent to the sexual abuse of children under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-625. A youth offender was required to register, and the 2005 amendment to the Act was retroactive. The supreme court held that the Act did not violate Mont. Const. art. XIII, § 1(3), nor was it an ex post facto law in violation of Mont. Const. art. II, § 31.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co. v. Gibson


05-216


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 153; 337 Mont. 509; 163 P.3d 387; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 266


February 23, 2006, Submitted on Briefs 
June 25, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 1, 2007
Rehearing denied by State Farm v. Gibson, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 370 (Mont., Aug. 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:
APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDV 2003-1353, Honorable Julie Macek, Presiding Judge.
State Farm Mut. Ins. Co. v. Gibson, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 950 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insureds sought recovery of medical payments coverage (MPC) under three automobile policies they had with respondent insurance company. The insurance company brought an action for declaratory judgment regarding the scope of the MPC. The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, County of Cascade, Montana, granted summary judgment for the insurance company and held the insureds could not stack the MPC. The insureds appealed.


OVERVIEW: The insureds were involved in a motor vehicle accident while driving a Ford Escort. They suffered injuries and incurred medical expenses in excess of $ 5,000.00. At the time of the accident, they insured three of their vehicles under separate policies with the insurance company, and paid separate premiums for each policy. Each of the three automobile policies included MPC in the amount of $ 5,000.00. The insureds sought to stack the Escort's MPC with the MPC coverages on the other two vehicles. The insurance company refused to provide MPC in excess of that contained in the Escort's policy, because the insureds were not operating or occupying the other two vehicles at the time of the accident. The Supreme Court of Montana held that the insurance company's anti-stacking provisions violated public policy by allowing the insurance company to receive valuable consideration for coverage that was not provided.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court.

State v. Pyette


No. 05-677


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 119; 337 Mont. 265; 159 P.3d 232; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 224


September 26, 2006, Submitted on Briefs 
May 22, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-05-170, The Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Presiding Judge.
State v. Pyette, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1383 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Montana appealed an order entered in the Fourth Judicial District Court, Missoula County, Montana, remanding the case to the Missoula Justice Court, Montana, with an order to dismiss the charge against defendant for driving while license is suspended.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for speeding and cited for operating a vehicle while her driver's license was suspended. She moved the justice court to dismiss the driving while her license was suspended charge, arguing Mont. Code Ann. § 65-4-214 was unconstitutional on its face. Defendant claimed that she was not given fair notice before her license was suspended. The motion was denied. On review, the district court held that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-5-214 did not clearly set forth the procedure under which a driver could appear and contest the notice of license suspension. The Supreme Court of Montana disagreed. In this case, defendant received two notices which were neither confusing nor inconsistent. The notices told defendant that if she did not pay her fine, her license would be suspended. She was also advised that if she did not appear before the justice court within ten days her driver's license would be suspended. Defendant was not denied due process in the suspension of her driver's license.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Gomez


No. 05-651


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 111; 337 Mont. 219; 158 P.3d 442; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 214

May 8, 2007, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC 2004-195(A), Honorable Ted O. Lympus, Presiding Judge.
State v. Gomez, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1679 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court for the Eleventh Judicial District, Flathead County, Montana, convicting him for operating an unlawful clandestine laboratory, a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for trespassing in his girlfriend's apartment. She gave the officers permission to search her car, which defendant had been using. In the trunk, the officers discovered items commonly used in the manufacturing of methamphetamine. A detective became concerned about whether defendant was manufacturing methamphetamine in a motor home where he stayed. The owners gave the detective permission to search the motor home, and the detective saw various items which appeared to have been used to manufacture methamphetamine. The officers were detoxifying the property when a duffle bag was removed from contaminated bedding. The detective suspected the presence of liquids in the bag. He believed applying for a search warrant would have taken at least forty-five minutes. Exigent circumstances justified the officers' warrantless search of the duffle bag to protect the safety of persons and property in the immediate area. Defendant was not entitled to suppress evidence of the bag or its contents.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

2007 MT 87; 337 Mont. 74; 155 P.3d 1282; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 125

April 3, 2007, Decided

Related proceeding at Ft. Rockvale v. 22nd Jud. Dist., 169 P.3d 406, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 468 (Mont., 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC-04-071(c), Honorable Stewart E. Stadler, Presiding Judge.
State v. Dasen, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1678 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Montana, convicting him of promotion of prostitution, sexual abuse of children, misdemeanor prostitution; and felony prostitution.


OVERVIEW: The State applied for search warrants for defendant's residence and two businesses. Although the applications particularly described the items to be seized, the warrants themselves did not. The district court ordered the return of all items seized pursuant to the warrant. Later, the State submitted a second round of warrant applications. A substituted judge had the jurisdiction to issue the second search warrant. The evidence necessary to show probable cause was obtained from a source independent of the first search, and thus met an exception to the exclusionary rule. Defendant was not entitled to suppress items seized pursuant to the second search warrant. The district court gave sufficient unanimity jury instructions on the counts charging defendant with the promotion of prostitution and sexual abuse of children. The district court did not prevent defendant from presenting a mistake of age defense to the charge of sexual abuse of children.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Jones v. Mont. Univ. Sys.


No. 05-142


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 82; 337 Mont. 1; 155 P.3d 1247; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 118


November 9, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
March 23, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Jones v. Mont. Univ. Sys., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11399 (U.S., Oct. 9, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Second Judicial District, In and for the County of Silver Bow, Cause No. DV 47-2004-223. The Honorable Nels Swandal, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant political candidates challenged a decision of the District Court of the Second Judicial District, in and for the County if Silver Bow (Montana), which dismissed their complaint against respondent university system alleging (1) common law conspiracy and conspiracy for purposes of 42 U.S.C.S. §§ 1983, 1985, and the Voting Rights Act of 1965, and (2) a violation of the rights of minors.


OVERVIEW: The candidates were not invited to participate in gubernatorial debates. They brought this action, but the trial court dismissed it. The court affirmed. In light of candidates' failure to file a complaint with the Montana Human Rights Commission under Mont. Code Ann. §§ 49-2-509(7), 49-2-501, the trial court properly dismissed the candidates' state law discrimination claim under Mont. Code Ann. § 49-3-205(1). The candidates failed to present a viable claim of political discrimination for purposes of 42 U.S.C.S. 1983, and thus they had to first exhaust available administrative remedies before pursuing a state law discrimination claim. The court affirmed the dismissal of candidates' action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1985, the Voting Rights Act of 1965, and common law conspiracy because the complaint (1) failed to allege that the candidates were members of a suspect class, (2) failed to allege that the system conspired for an illegal purpose, and (3) was void of any facts that would have sustained a claim under the Act. The trial court properly dismissed the candidates' claim on behalf of minors because the candidates lacked standing to assert the constitutional rights of others.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the caption be stricken with reference to the minors. The court affirmed.

 

262 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Quigg v. Slaughter


No. 05-692, No. DA 06-0013


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 76; 336 Mont. 474; 154 P.3d 1217; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 113


August 16, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
March 20, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 6, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALS FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause CDV-02-174 and CDV-2004-172, Honorable Thomas C. Honzel, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmates challenged a decision of the District Court of the First Judicial District, in and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), which granted summary judgment to respondents, officials of the Montana Department of Corrections, on claims for injunctive and declaratory relief. Appellant prisoner challenged an order granting summary judgment to the officials on his related claims. The court consolidated the cases for appeal.


OVERVIEW: The inmates sought a judgment that persons sentenced to the Montana State Prison at Deer Lodge (MSP) prior to 1999 had to be confined there and other private prisons did not have the same opportunities, thus rendering the inmates' incarceration unlawful. The prisoner sought to be transferred back to MSP and placed in a low security classification. The trial court granted summary judgment to the officials and the court affirmed. The court held that any differences between medical care, visitation, education, and recreation at MSP and the private and regional prisons, as authorized under Mont. Code Ann. tit. 53, ch. 30, pts. 5, 6, did not rise to the level of cruel and unusual punishment under Mont. Const. art. II, § 22 and the Eighth Amendment. The inmates did not provide evidence that the officials acted with deliberate indifference. The court also found no state constitutional violation under Mont. Const. art. II, § 28. The inmates did not possess a state-created liberty interest in being housed at MSP. While the prisoner had a liberty interest in the opportunity for parole, the officials did nothing to impede those opportunities and the court found no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

263 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Wing v. State


No. DA 06-0037


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 72; 336 Mont. 423; 155 P.3d 1224; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 95


December 13, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
March 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 29, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Cause No. DV-04-783, The Honorable John W. Larson, Presiding Judge.
Wing v. State, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1711 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured party challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondent State in an action arising from a car accident.


OVERVIEW: The injured party contended that the State's contractor failed to place adequate signs at a road construction zone. After summary judgment was granted to the State, this appeal followed. In affirming, the supreme court rejected the assertion that Mont. Code Ann. § 2-9-301 was unconstitutionally vague. A person of ordinary intelligence could have comprehended that the term "receipt" meant that the statute of limitations tolled when the claim was actually received. The fact that "receipt" could have varied by the manner of delivery did not render the statute unconstitutional since perfect clarity and precise guidance were not required. Next, the district court's application of § 2-9-301 was proper. Since the claim was received on April 26, 2004, tolling began the next day, pursuant to M.R. Civ.P. 6(a). The limitations period resumed on August 25, 2004, which was 120 days later. The limitations period expired at the end of that day because the injured party had only one day left in the three-year period when the claim was received. The complaint filed the next day was untimely. If the tolling period began on the mailing date instead, the outcome would have been the same.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.


 

264 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Seltzer v. Morton


No. 05-378


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 62; 336 Mont. 225; 154 P.3d 561; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 98


June 28, 2006, Argued and Submitted  
March 12, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 18, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. ADV 2003-173, Honorable Dirk M. Sandefur, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff art appraiser sued defendants, a law firm, an attorney, and his client, for malicious prosecution and abuse of process. The jury found in favor of plaintiff and awarded $ 1.1 million in compensatory damages. The jury assessed punitive damages for $ 20 million against the law firm. The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, County of Cascade, Montana, reduced the sanction against the firm to $ 9.9 million. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff rendered his opinion that a watercolor painting the client owned was not authentic. The client hired an attorney to file a defamation action against plaintiff. The district court dismissed the suit with prejudice, because defendants could not prevail on the merits. Plaintiff incurred over $ 45,000.00 in legal fees. He filed a successful suit for malicious prosecution. The district court reduced the jury's award of punitive damages against the law firm from $20 million to $9.9 million. The state supreme court examined the penalty under the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. Under Mont. Code Ann. § 27-1-221(7)(a), the district court properly admitted evidence of defendants' financial condition during the punitive damages proceedings. The law firm failed to object to the district court's instruction to the jury that it could be held liable for the attorney's actions. Defendants were not harmed by the jury instructions regarding the theories of liability. Because the law firm did not have a history of this kind of misconduct, calculation of the punitive damages award based on a single-digit multiplier comported with due process concerns.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Clark v. Roosevelt County


No. 05-580


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 44; 336 Mont. 118; 154 P.3d 48; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 60



February 21, 2007, Decided  
February 21, 2007, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 19, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: Clark v. Roosevelt County, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1318 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner appealed the order of the District Court for the Fifteenth Judicial District, Roosevelt County, Montana, denying her petition for the release of her property that was seized in connection with a drug investigation. The State filed a motion seeking dismissal of the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant owned a bar in Poplar, Montana. During an investigation, officials arrested an individual who admitted that he had delivered methamphetamine to appellant at her bar. The county attorney and the U.S. attorney advised the task force that appellant's bar was subject to forfeiture. Without a warrant, an agent for the task force seized the bar, the contents therein, and appellant's liquor license. The district court ruled that probable cause existed for the seizure of appellant's property. After the bar was destroyed by a fire, the district court dismissed the petition for forfeiture. However, the district court denied appellant's petition for the release of her property. On appeal, she challenged whether the district court erred in determining that probable cause existed for the seizure of her property. The issue was moot, as there was no justiciable controversy before the state supreme court.


OUTCOME: The State's motion to dismiss was granted. The appeal was dismissed with prejudice.

City of Kalispell v. Burgert


No. DA 06-0083


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 39N; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 51


January 10, 2007, Submitted on Briefs  
February 13, 2007, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at City of Kalispell v. Burgert, 168 P.3d 701, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 160 (Mont., Feb. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC-02-253A, Honorable Ted O. Lympus, Presiding Judge.
City of Kalispell v. Burgert, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 166 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the municipal court found defendant guilty of resisting arrest and obstructing a police officer. The Eleventh Judicial District Court, Flathead County, Montana, affirmed his conviction. Defendant appealed the district court's order denying his request for reconsideration.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with resisting arrest and obstructing a police officer. He filed a pretrial motion to dismiss based on the lack of evidence to establish probable cause that he acted knowingly to impede a police officer. The city presented several police officers' testimony to show that defendant knowingly obstructed a police officer and resisted arrest. The municipal court did not abuse its discretion in denying his motion to dismiss and the district court did not err in affirming that determination. The municipal court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a directed verdict. The district court did not err in its failure to inform defendant of the potential pitfalls of proceeding pro se. He never waived his right to counsel. While defendant argued that Montana's statutes on resisting arrest and obstructing a peace officer were unconstitutional, the state supreme court would not address a matter raised for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Adams v. State


No. 05-610


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 35; 336 Mont. 63; 153 P.3d 601; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 54


November 22, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
February 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 2, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Cause No. DC-98-144, Honorable Jeffrey H. Langton, Presiding Judge.
State V.adams, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1498 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Montana, denying his amended petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The jury found appellant guilty of aggravated assault, and the criminal possession of dangerous drugs and drug paraphernalia. The time between appellant's arrest and the first trial date amounted to 267 days, and from his arrest to the trial amounted to 372 days. Appellant's requests for continuances and his counsel's motion to withdraw were the cause for 169 days of the delay. Appellant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating impairment in his ability to defend himself. Counsel was not ineffective for his failure to file a motion to dismiss for lack of a speedy trial; nor was counsel ineffective for failure to move for a directed verdict or for failing to object to the jury instruction on aggravated assault as a lesser included offense of attempted deliberate homicide. At sentencing, the district court's failure to submit the issue of a weapons enhancement to the jury was harmless error; appellant was not illegally sentenced. The district court did not err by denying his request for postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

268 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Johnson v. Costco Wholesale


No. 04-835


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 43; 336 Mont. 105; 152 P.3d 727; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 46; 25 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1164; 154 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,352


July 13, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
February 13, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 5, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DV 2003-0741, Honorable Gregory R. Todd, Presiding Judge.
Johnson v. Costco Wholesale, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 3395, 2004 ML 3863 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged a decision of the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Yellowstone (Montana), which granted appellee former employer attorney fees and its motion for judgment as a matter of law and held that the employee's violation of a grazing policy was good cause for termination under Mont. Code Ann. § 39-2-904(1)(b), (c) of the Wrongful Discharge From Employment Act.


OVERVIEW: The employee was fired for violating a grazing policy. He brought this action under the Act, Mont. Code Ann. §§ 39-2-901 - 39-2-915, but the trial court ruled in the employer's favor. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that it was going to review a trial court's grant or denial of a motion for judgment as a matter of law as a legal question for which the de novo standard was appropriate. Those decisions, including Wallin v. Kinyon Estate, 164 Mont. 160 (1974), and any other decisions, including Somont Oil. Com. v. A. & G Drilling, Inc., 332 Mont. 56 (2006), Glacier Tennis Club v. Treweek Const., 320 Mont. 351 (2004), Onstad v. Payless Shoesource, 301 Mont. 259 (2000), In re Mental Health of D.L.T., 314 Mont. 297 (2003), Buhr on Behalf of Lloyd v. Flathead County, 268 Mont. 223 (1994), Nelson v. Flathead Valley Transit, 251 Mont. 269 (1992), and Davis v. Sheriff, 234 Mont. 126 (1988), applying an abuse of discretion standard of review, were overruled to that extent. The trial court erred in granting the employer's motion under Mont. Code Ann. § 39-2-904(1)(b) because a jury might have found the employer lacked good cause to discharge the employee.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court erred in granting judgment as a matter of law regarding the employee's argument under the first section of the statute in question, but the trial court did not err in granting judgment as a matter of law under the second section of the statute. The court vacated the award of fees and did not address another of the employee's contentions. The court remanded.

State ex rel. Long v. Justice Court


No. OP06-0602


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2007 MT 3; 335 Mont. 219; 156 P.3d 5; 2007 Mont. LEXIS 8



January 9, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 29, 2007.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the State of Montana, filed an application for writ of supervisory control and a motion for stay of proceedings pending before respondent, the Lake County Justice Court, Montana.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with speeding, driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while under the influence of alcohol, and possession of an open alcohol beverage container. He sought a waiver of a jury trial and argued that Mont. Code Ann. § 46-17-201 (2005) was unconstitutional to the extent that it required both parties to consent to the waiver. The justice court erred by declaring the statute unconstitutional and granting defendant's request for waiver of a jury trial over the State's objection. Mont. Const. art. II, § 26 required the State's consent prior to the waiver of a jury trial. This case was appropriate for the exercise of supervisory control. The appeal process would have provided an inadequate remedy, because the State would have lost its right to consent or object to the waiver of a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The State's application for a writ of supervisory control was granted. The justice court's order granting defendant's request for waiver of a jury trial over the State's objection was vacated, and the case was remanded to the justice court for further proceedings.
