In re Mental Health of V.K.


No. 05-547


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 347N; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 682


July 19, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
December 27, 2006, Decided


NOTICE: PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Mental Health of V.K., 149 P.3d 915, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 749 (Mont., Dec. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. CDI 2005-022, Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mental health patient appealed the judgment of the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, ordering that she be committed to the Montana State Hospital and ordering involuntary medications based on the testimony of a licensed clinical professional counselor.


OVERVIEW: The patient presented several issues on appeal of her commitment order, including her attorney's alleged ineffectiveness, the constitutionality of Montana's civil commitment statutes, and the authority of the district court to order involuntary medications based on the testimony of a licensed clinical professional counselor. The patient did not raise these issues in the district court. The Supreme Court of Montana would not review the issues, because they were outside of the record. The patient's ineffective assistance of counsel claim was based on a medical journal article and a record of complaints that was not part of the district court record. There was no basis in the record for the Supreme Court of Montana to vacate her commitment after the fact, declare certain statutory provisions unconstitutional, and adopt guidelines for future involuntary medication cases.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

271 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Matz


No. 05-345


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 348; 335 Mont. 201; 150 P.3d 367; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 679


May 24, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
December 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 16, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause DC-04-541, Honorable Russell C. Fagg, Presiding Judge.
State v. Matz, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1023, 2005 ML 1650 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Yellowstone (Montana) of aggravated assault. His sentence was enhanced based on a finding that defendant used a weapon in the commission of the offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant raised many issues on appeal, none of which had merit. Because defendant raised justifiable use of force as an affirmative defense, it was defendant's burden at trial, and the State was not obligated to prove that defendant did not act with such justification. Therefore, the trial court properly instructed the jury to that effect, and the court agreed that a statement in State v. Azure, 181 Mont. 47 (1979), which approved a jury instruction that placed the burden on the State to establish the absence of justification of use of force, was no longer good law. The trial court did not err in enhancing defendant's sentence, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-221(1) for use of a weapon, where he was found guilty of aggravated assault under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-202 and he was separately found by the jury to have used a weapon in the commission of the offense. The application of the enhancement statute was not a violation of the double jeopardy principles in Mont. Const. art. II, § 25. As defendant was only charged with one criminal offense, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in instructing the jury regarding unanimity. Evidence was properly excluded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Billings High Sch. Dist. No. 2 v. Billings Gazette


No. 05-406


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 329; 335 Mont. 94; 149 P.3d 565; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 656; 25 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1014


March 22, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
December 12, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 5, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DV-04-1030, The Honorable Susan P. Watters, Presiding Judge.
High School District No. 2 v. The Billings Gazette, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2814, 2004 ML 4012 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, an education association and two teachers, challenged a decision of the District Court of Thirteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Yellowstone (Montana), which, after dissolving a stay of the proceedings, ordered petitioner school district to release documents to respondent newspaper under Mont. Const. art. II, § 9. The newspaper challenged the denial of fees under Mont. Code Ann. §§ 2-3-221, 27-8-313.


OVERVIEW: After having found that the teachers lacked an expectation of privacy in the documents sought, the trial court ordered the release of the documents to the newspaper. On appeal, the court affirmed. Because the association and teachers failed to utilize procedures to preserve the ability to appeal the trial court's finding of no expectations and the trial court's order releasing the documents, the association and teachers were not entitled to use the "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception to the mootness doctrine. Because the issues were rendered moot by the trial court's order releasing the documents, the court declined to address the merits of the issues. The trial court did not err in denying the newspaper's request for attorney fees. For purposes of Mont. Code Ann. § 2-3-221, the newspaper was not a plaintiff who prevailed according to the statute. The district's seeking a judicial determination of the issues did not serve to automatically subject the district to pay an award of fees under Mont. Code Ann. § 27-8-313. The court found no abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re M.A.L.


No. 05-262


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 299; 334 Mont. 436; 148 P.3d 606; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 609

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause BDJ 02-175-Y, Honorable Julie Macek, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Montana, terminating his parental rights to his children.


OVERVIEW: The father's children were adjudicated as youths in need of care, making his prior convictions relevant. The Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services (DPHHS) learned that he had a 1985 sexual offense involving a minor in Texas. The father had subjected a child to one of the aggravated circumstances listed in Mont. Code Ann. § 41-3-423(2)(a)-(e), by reason of his adjudication for indecency with a child. Based upon the aggravated circumstance, DPHHS was not required to provide rehabilitative services. This was not an unlawful retroactive application of the statute. The father's children were in the State's custody for 29 months preceding the hearing, creating a presumption that the termination of parental rights was in their best interests under Mont. Code Ann. § 41-3-604. The district court's termination order was not clearly erroneous. The father's motion for judgment as a matter of law was not properly before the court. His equal protection argument was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Mont. Supreme Court Comm'n on the Unauthorized Practice of Law v. O'Neil


No. 04-857


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 284; 334 Mont. 311; 147 P.3d 200; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 600


April 5, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
November 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 6, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Comm'n on Unauthorized Practice v. O'Neil, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 661 (Mont., Dec. 6, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by O'Neil v. Mont. Supreme Court Comm'n on Unauthorized Practice of Law, 127 S. Ct. 1868, 167 L. Ed. 2d 324, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3080 (U.S., 2007)
Related proceeding at State v. O'Neil, 2008 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 120 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV 02-378B, Honorable Deborah Kim Christopher, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District for Flathead County (Montana), granting appellee State Bar of Montana (Bar) summary judgment on appellant's third-party complaint, granting appellee Montana Supreme Court Commission on the Unauthorized Practice of Law summary judgment on appellant's counterclaim, and finding appellant in contempt and enjoining him from practicing law.


OVERVIEW: The Commission filed a petition seeking that appellant be held in civil contempt for engaging in the unauthorized practice of law in violation of Mont. Code Ann. §§ 37-61-201, 37-61-210. Appellant had never been licensed to practice law in Montana or any other state, he did not attend law school, and he did not sit for Montana's bar exam. On appeal, the court held that the district court did not err by finding that appellant engaged in the unauthorized practice of law because his conduct of drafting pleadings for his customers, providing them with legal advice, and appearing in court with his customers constituted "practicing law" under Mont. Code Ann. § 37-61-201. Appellant readily admitted that he did so without having received a license to practice law under Mont. Code Ann. § 37-61-210. The court further held that §§ 37-61-201, 37-61-210 were constitutional because they were narrowly tailored to target only the provision of legal services in Montana by individuals who had not proven through examination and admission to the bar that they were qualified and possessed a familiarity with Montana law. The statutes also provided fair notice of the prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

275 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Gratzer v. Mahoney


No. 05-075


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 282; 334 Mont. 297; 150 P.3d 343; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 591



November 1, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Gratzer, 209 Mont. 308, 682 P.2d 141, 1984 Mont. LEXIS 878 (Mont., 1984).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of deliberate homicide in 1982. He was serving a life sentence without the possibility of parole, plus ten additional years for using a dangerous weapon while perpetrating the deliberate homicide. He petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: In the habeas proceeding, the petitioner challenged the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-22-101(2)(2003), suggesting that the statute, by prohibiting a petitioner from challenging the validity of a sentence, impermissibly suspended the writ of habeas corpus. Since petitioner's challenge drew into question the facial validity of his sentence, the state supreme court concluded that the procedural bar to his habeas corpus petition was not applicable and addressed the merits of his claims. The district court did not violate petitioner's constitutional rights when it declared him ineligible for parole while serving a life sentence; nor did the court violate his constitutional rights when it designated him a "dangerous offender" for all purposes. Petitioner was not entitled to relief from the ten-year weapons enhancement added to his sentence by the district court. Petitioner's conviction became final long before the United States Supreme Court decided Apprendi; the case did not apply retroactively on collateral review.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

Lambert v. Mahoney


Docket No. OP 06-0310


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 Mont. LEXIS 765



November 1, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Lambert v. Mahoney, 149 P.3d 913, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 709 (Mont., 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition against respondent warden for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought habeas corpus relief for an alleged illegal sentence. The court granted the inmate relief and remanded for resentencing. The inmate raised a facial challenge to the sentence and contended that the sentencing court had no authority to impose an enhanced sentence for the use of a firearm under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-221(1) (1997) for the reason that the inmate was convicted of assault on a peace officer under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-210(1)(b) (1997). As applied to the inmate's challenge to the validity of the enhanced sentence, Mont. Code Ann. § 46-22-101(1) (1997) unconstitutionally suspended the writ of habeas corpus and there was no procedural bar to the court's entertaining the inmate's facial challenge. The inmate was sentenced to 10 years in prison. The inmate had pointed a gun at policemen but did not shoot. The offense constituted causing apprehension of serious bodily injury to a peace officer by use of a weapon and the use of a weapon was required. Therefore, the enhancement of the sentence was in violation of a later case and was illegal, such that relief was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court granted the petition and remanded for resentencing.

 

277 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Lott v. State


No. 05-617


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 279; 334 Mont. 270; 150 P.3d 337; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 585



October 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 17, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Lott v. State, 2006 MT 240, 333 Mont. 531, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 461 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was sentenced to 20 years in prison for aggravated burglary, which included a 10-year enhancement for the use of a dangerous weapon, and to 20 years in prison for felony assault, which also included a 10-year enhancement for the use of a dangerous weapon. The inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus under MCA § 46-22-101 challenging those sentences.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that the district court unconstitutionally enhanced his sentences in violation of the prohibition against double jeopardy under the decisions in the Guillaume and Whitehorn cases, which were decided after the inmate was sentenced. The State argued that the inmate was not entitled to relief because habeas corpus was not available to attack the validity of his sentence, as he had not filed a direct appeal or postconviction petition, and the one-year statute of limitations for seeking postconviction relief under MCA § 46-21-102 had expired. The court held that the inmate was entitled to habeas corpus relief because the district court unconstitutionally enhanced the inmate's sentences because the offenses required proving the use of a weapon in violation of the inmate's double jeopardy rights, and because the procedural bar created by MCA § 46-22-101(2) unconstitutionally suspended the writ of habeas corpus. Had the inmate filed a timely direct appeal or petition for postconviction relief, his double jeopardy argument would have been unavailing because the decisions on which he relied were not issued until well after both filing dates had expired.


OUTCOME: The inmate's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was granted and the case was remanded to the district court for resentencing.

Montanans v. State


No. DA 06-0634


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 277; 334 Mont. 237; 146 P.3d 759; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 580


October 5, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 26, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 16, 2006.
Related proceeding at Not in Montana: Citizens Against Ci-97 v. State, 2006 MT 278, 2006 MT 278, 334 Mont. 265, 147 P.3d 174, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 588 (Oct. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDV 06-1162 (d), Honorable Dirk M. Sandefur, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action filed by plaintiff initiative opponents, the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), invalidated the signatures obtained by specific signature gatherers and invalidated the Montana Secretary of State's certifications of three initiatives. Defendant initiative proponents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The proponents attempted to place three initiatives on the November 2006 ballot. The opponents filed suit, alleging that the proponents engaged in signature gathering practices that violated state law. The district court agreed and invalidated the initiatives' certifications. On appeal, the court affirmed. The district court did not err when it determined that the signature gathering process was permeated by a pervasive and general pattern and practice of fraud and procedural noncompliance. The opponents presented uncontradicted evidence that the five most prolific signature gatherers swore to signatures obtained outside of their presence in violation of MCA §§ 13-27-302, 13-27-111(4). Substantial evidence was presented that the affiants provided bogus or false addresses for where they could be contacted in violation of MCA 13-27-302, evidence that was not rebutted. The district court's finding that a significantly large percentage of the paid, out-of-state signature gatherers working for the proponents' employed a "bait and switch" tactic to induce people who knowingly signed one petition to unknowingly sign the other two was supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment invalidating the initiatives' certifications was affirmed.

Elliott v. State Dep't of Revenue


No. 05-336


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 267; 334 Mont. 195; 146 P.3d 741; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 579


June 13, 2006, Submitted  
October 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. CDV 2004-777, Honorable Thomas C. Honzel, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a senator, requested certain state tax information from the Montana Legislative Auditor for "C" corporations doing business in Montana. Respondent, the State Department of Revenue (DOR), denied the senator access to the tax information. The senator filed a petition to obtain public documents. The District Court of the First Judicial District, County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, denied the petition. The senator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The senator requested the release of state tax information on corporations. The senator invoked the right to know provisions of Mont. Const. art. II, § 9 in support of his contention that state corporate tax records were subject to public disclosure. However, Mont. Code Ann. § 15-31-511 prohibited the disclosure of tax records provided to the State Department of Revenue by Montana corporate taxpayers. The senator did not challenge the constitutionality of the statutory prohibition on the disclosure of corporate tax information. Rather, he viewed the statute as "a nullity" in light of case law interpreting Mont. Const. art. II, § 9. Without a direct constitutional challenge to Mont. Code Ann. § 15-31-511, there was no basis for disturbing its prohibition on the disclosure of state corporate tax records.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

280 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Benders


No. 05-327


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 275; 334 Mont. 231; 146 P.3d 751; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 576


June 21, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
October 24, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC-03-908, Honorable Ingrid G. Gustafson, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Yellowstone County, Montana, denying his motion to suppress evidence relating to his conviction for driving under the influence.


OVERVIEW: A deputy observed defendant driving his vehicle between twenty-five and forty miles-per-hour on a road that had a fifty mile-per-hour speed limit. Defendant continued at that speed even after the speed limit had increased to seventy miles-per-hour. Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-311(1) gave law enforcement the discretion to determine when a speed was slow enough to impede the flow of traffic. The officer then initiated a stop of the vehicle and advised defendant that he was being stopped for impeding traffic. Based upon his contact with defendant, the deputy believed that he was under the influence of alcohol or drugs. Defendant filed a motion to suppress the evidence relating to the stop. The district court ruled that the officer had particularized suspicion to conduct the stop based on Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-311(1). Defendant's argument that Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-311(1) was unconstitutionally vague was not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Huffine v. Brown


Docket No. OP 06-0674


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 Mont. LEXIS 754



October 18, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Estate of Huffine, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 527 (2006)
Huffine v. Brown, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 695 (Mont., Oct. 18, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a document entitled "Combined Petition for Writs of Certiorari Mandate, and Stay of Order Appealed, and Prohibition, Supervisory Control," against respondent, the judge of the Eighteenth Judicial District Court, Gallatin County, Montana, in light of the judge's actions in an estate matter.


OVERVIEW: In a dispute concerning decedent's estate, petitioner sought a writ of certiorari pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 27-25-102 to review the judge's actions. Petitioner asserted that the judge had taken actions in the case that were unconstitutional and in violation of statutes. Petitioner's request for a writ did not comply with Mont. Code Ann. § 27-25-202, which required more than general allegations. Petitioner also sought a writ of mandate pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 27-26-102, directing the judge to enjoin the public administrator from proceeding in this matter, order that the family trust prevailed over decedent's will, or mandate a trial by jury. However, petitioner failed to specify what act the law specially enjoined the public administrator from performing. Petitioner also failed to explain why an appeal would not be an adequate remedy for the alleged errors by the judge. Therefore, supervisory control was not appropriate.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

 

282 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Stavenjord v. Mont. State Fund


No. 04-737


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 257; 334 Mont. 117; 146 P.3d 724; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 489


October 26, 2005, Heard on Oral Argument  
October 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Stavenjord v. State Fund, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 623 (Mont., Nov. 9, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM: The Montana Workers' Compensation Court, WWC 2000-0207, Honorable Mike McCarter, Presiding Judge.
Stavenjord v. Mont. State Fund, 2003 MT 67, 314 Mont. 466, 67 P.3d 229, 2003 Mont. LEXIS 69 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee and cross-appellant, the Montana State Fund, appealed an order of the Montana Workers' Compensation Court (WCC) related to common fund attorney fees and the retroactive application of the Stavenjord rule that an employee should receive benefits related to her occupational disease equal to benefits she would have received had she been injured.


OVERVIEW: The WCC determined that application of Mont. Code Ann. § 39-72-405(2)(1997) to the employee's claim against the State Fund violated her constitutional equal protection rights. The employee was entitled to receive benefits related to her occupational disease equal to benefits she would have received had she been injured. The State Fund paid the employee's additional benefits. The employee then sought retroactive application of the Stavenjord rule, and the recovery of common fund attorney fees for Stavenjord-type benefits secured by non-participating claimants. An analysis of the Chevron factors revealed that retroactive application of the Stavenjord rule was proper. There was no reason to create a distinction between litigants based on the timing of their claims. Stavenjord did not create a common fund. Thus, the employee's counsel was not entitled to recover fees from cases brought by other claimants.


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the WCC for further proceedings to include the determination of an appropriate procedure by which potential Stavenjord beneficiaries could be identified and notified of their interests related to increased Stavenjord-type permanent partial disability benefits.


 

283 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Garrymore


No. 04-644


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 245; 334 Mont. 1; 145 P.3d 946; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 468


November 30, 2005, Heard; June 6, 2006, Submitted  
October 2, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 20, 2006.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Garrymore v. Frink, 2014 Mont. LEXIS 219 (Mont., Jan. 14, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-2003-37, Honorable John S. Henson, Presiding Judge.
State v. Garrymore, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1720 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), of deliberate homicide in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-102 (2001). He was sentenced to life in prison without parole. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant challenged the parole restriction. The court affirmed. The trial court's imposition of a parole eligibility restriction pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-202(2) (2001) did not violate defendant's constitutional rights under the Sixth Amendment. Because the State did not seek the death penalty, and because neither Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-219 nor Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-222 was applicable to defendant's case, the maximum sentence that could have been imposed on defendant for deliberate homicide was life imprisonment. The parole eligibility restriction imposed on defendant fell within the statutory range for the offense. The court rejected defendant's claim that Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-102(2) contained an implicit presumption of parole eligibility. The trial court's restriction on defendant's parole eligibility did not violate defendant's statutory rights under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-1-401. Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-102(2) authorized a district court to impose both life imprisonment and life imprisonment without the possibility of parole, and thus Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-202(2) did not allow or require a sentencing court to increase punishment for a charged offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

284 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Yellowstone County v. Billings Gazette


No. 05-019


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 218; 333 Mont. 390; 143 P.3d 135; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 417; 34 Media L. Rep. 2350


October 5, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
September 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 28, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DV 2003-0180, Honorable G. Todd Baugh, Presiding Judge.
Yellowstone County v. Billings Gazette, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2811, 2004 ML 4013 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Montana, which determined that all documents requested by the newspaper should be disclosed by respondent county with some redactions, and denied the newspaper's request for costs and attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The newspaper sought access to public documents held by the county concerning civil litigation brought against county officials. The county filed a declaratory action seeking a determination of which documents had to be disclosed. The district court authorized disclosure of the chief public defender's deposition testimony with redactions. The public's right to know about his management of the public defender's office outweighed any privacy interest non-parties may have had in the redacted portions of his testimony. Therefore, the public had a right to inspect the entirety of his deposition so long as the names of the non-parties were withheld. The district court erred in denying the newspaper's motion for attorney fees without rationale. Due to the public benefits gained by the vindication of the public's right to know, the costs of litigation to secure these rights should have been spread among beneficiaries.


OUTCOME: The district court's authorization of redactions which eliminated more than non-party names from the chief public defender's deposition testimony was reversed, and the case was remanded for further consideration of the newspaper's request for attorney fees and entry of an order thereon with supporting rationale.


 

285 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Havre Daily News, LLC v. City of Havre


No. 05-292


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 215; 333 Mont. 331; 142 P.3d 864; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 410


March 8, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 30, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Hill, Cause No. DV 04-039, Honorable David Rice, Presiding Judge.
Havre Daily News v. City of Havre, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1017 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff newspapers sued defendants, a city, a police chief, and police members, seeking an unredacted incident report and an order to implement a general related policy of dissemination. The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, in and for the County of Hill (Montana), denied the newspapers' default judgment motion, granted defendants summary judgment, and granted the newspapers fees under Mont. Code Ann. § 2-3-221. All appealed.


OVERVIEW: The newspapers sought an unredacted incident report, which defendants originally refused to give. After the newspapers filed this lawsuit, defendants gave the requested information to the newspapers. The trial court ultimately ruled in defendants' favor on summary judgment, but awarded the newspapers fees. On appeal, the court affirmed in part and remanded. The trial court did not err in denying the newspapers' motion for a default judgment. Defendants' summary judgment motion sufficed to prevent the trial court from entering a default judgment. The newspapers' request for prospective relief lacked any concrete factual basis and was a request for relief from a purely hypothetical future violation of its right to know under Mont. Const. art. II, § 9. This was an unripe and nonjusticiable controversy. Because the issue related to the release of the report was mooted after the newspapers obtained receipt thereof, the trial court should have dismissed the case instead of granting summary judgment. For purposes of Mont. Code Ann. § 2-3-221, the newspapers were entitled to recover only those fees incurred in securing the unredacted reports.


OUTCOME: Defendants' cross-appeal was not ripe. Fees incurred in securing the unredacted report were proper. The court affirmed and remanded for a hearing to determine those fees. Any other fees incurred, including those to obtain prospective relief, were not recoverable. The court remanded for dismissal the claims without prejudice, as the trial court should have done this rather than grant summary judgment. Denial of default judgment was proper.

In re M.H.


No. 05-549


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 208; 333 Mont. 286; 143 P.3d 103; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 405


June 28, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 21, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDJ 04-071, Honorable Kenneth R. Neill, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), which, on a petition filed by respondent Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services, terminated his parental rights to two children.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that no treatment plan was necessary because the father was not able to assume the role of parent. On appeal, the court affirmed the termination decision. The father failed to tie the proposition that parent-child bonds were not to be lightly disregarded to the jury trial right he asserted under Mont. Const. art. II, § 26. The adoption of the father's argument would have required the court to overrule case law and Mont. Code Ann. § 41-3-607(5), which provided that there was no right to a jury trial in termination of parental right proceedings. Two psychologists testified that the father would not be able to parent within a reasonable time and another testified that someone would have to be with the father every minute for months or more to get him to function adequately as a parent. The trial court found that the accommodations necessary to keep the children safe were beyond the scope of the Americans with Disabilities Act, even if it applied in this case, and the father failed to establish error in the trial court's rejection of his claim that the Department violated the Act under 42 U.S.C.S. § 12132 by failing to accommodate his mental illness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Wood


No. 05-564


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 206N; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 406


August 3, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 29, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Wood, 333 Mont. 552, 143 P.3d 704, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 528 (Mont., Aug. 29, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC 2004-302, Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), which convicted him of driving under the influence of alcohol or drugs (DUI).


OVERVIEW: During a trial for DUI, the State offered an instruction under Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-404(2) regarding the refusal to submit to testing. The instruction stated that there was an inference that a person was under the influence if a refusal was given. Defendant contended that this inference improperly placed the burden of proof on him. In affirming, the appellate court determined that it had decided the exact same issue in the Great Falls case. Section 61-8-404(2) was read as requiring the production of other competent evidence of a DUI since § 61-8-404(1)(a) required corroborating evidence when a person actually took a test. In this case, the State presented that corroborating evidence in the form of witness testimony that defendant was driving erratically, appeared unsteady on his feet, and was incoherent and belligerent.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Barnaby


No. 05-013


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 203; 333 Mont. 220; 142 P.3d 809; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 399


January 11, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
August 23, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and for the County of Lake, Cause No. DC 02-121. The Honorable Deborah Kim Christopher, Judge presiding.
State v. Barnaby, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 3463, 2004 ML 3957 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and for the County of Lake (Montana), which convicted him of operating a clandestine laboratory. He also challenged the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: Based on citizen complaints and other information known about a person staying at defendant's residence, a search warrant was issued. A motion to suppress evidence found in the search was denied, and defendant was convicted. In partially affirming, the appellate court determined that the "totality of the circumstances" test was used to evaluate whether probable cause supported the issuance of a warrant. It was proper to consider information that the person staying at defendant's house was involved in methamphetamine use, along with suspicious activity at the residence, in determining whether probable cause existed. The proposition that independent police work represented the only method of corroboration under the totality of the circumstances test was wrong as a matter of law. Next, defendant's Batson challenge was properly denied because of the race neutral explanations provided by the prosecutor: one potential juror was related to defendant, and the other one considered his attorney a good friend. Finally, a remand was necessary as to the sentence imposed because the record did not show that the criteria under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-225 was considered.


OUTCOME: The sentencing decision was vacated, and that portion of the case was remanded for consideration of alternatives to imprisonment. The rest of the decision was affirmed.

Faulconbridge v. State


No. 04-592


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 198; 333 Mont. 186; 142 P.3d 777; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 388


August 30, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
August 22, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 11, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DV 94-79995, Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Presiding Judge.
Faulconbridge v. State, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2571, 2004 ML 2927 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents filed a wrongful death and survival action against defendants, the State and a company. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), entered a judgment for the State on a jury verdict after denying the State summary judgment and excluding evidence of a prior accident, a maintenance contract, and another's alleged negligence and conduct. The parents and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The parents' daughter was killed in a motorcycle accident. The parents brought an action, but the trial court entered a judgment on a jury verdict in the State's favor. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial. The trial court abused its discretion in excluding evidence of a prior accident because it was relevant to the question of the State's notice of the road's conditions as well as to questions of road defect and causation. Thus, the court remanded for a new trial. Because many questions presented on appeal were likely to arise again, the court addressed other issues raised. The plain language of Mont. R. Evid. 615 demonstrated that Rule 615(2) permitted a validly designated representative to both remain in the courtroom during the trial and testify. Consequently, the court overruled State v. Flowers, 320 Mont. 49 (2004) and State v. Claric, 271 Mont. 141 (1995), to the extent that the court stated that a valid designated representative under Rule 615(2) could not both remain in the courtroom during trial and also testify. One witness, as a former State employee, did not qualify as a proper representative under Tex. R. Evid. 615(2) at retrial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for a new trial. The trial court erred in excluding evidence of the prior accident, refusing to permit the introduction of a maintenance contract, and excluding the introduction of another's conduct to establish the victim's alleged negligence. The trial court did not err in denying summary judgment and in refusing to allow the jury to consider another's alleged negligence.

State v. Rensvold


No. 05-543


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 146; 332 Mont. 392; 139 P.3d 154; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 236


May 24, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
June 27, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 14, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and For the County of Lake, Cause No. DC 2005-87, Honorable C. B. McNeil, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State challenged a decision of the District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, in and for the County of Lake (Montana), which (1) entered an order granting a motion to dismiss filed by defendant and (2) dismissed the State's appeal from a justice court order that dismissed the State's case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally charged with driving under the influence of alcohol and appeared in the justice court. The matter was set for an omnibus hearing that the State did not attend. The justice court dismissed the action. Instead of refiling in the justice court, the State filed a notice of appeal in the trial court regarding the dismissal order. The trial court dismissed the appeal and the charge against defendant. The court affirmed. The State had to file the charge against defendant in the justice court and had no power to file the complaint first in the trial court, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 3-10-303(1)(a) and Mont. Const. art. VII, § 5(2). Defendant had an absolute right to two jury trials, one in the justice court and one in the trial court. The State, by not participating in the justice court proceedings, was not permitted to deny defendant's rights to a jury trial in both courts, and thus the trial court's decision was proper. To the extent an accused was legally entitled to prosecution in one or more courts, then he was, under Mont. Const. art. II, §§ 24, 26, also entitled to have those facts found by a jury in each court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Trull


No. 04-705


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 119; 332 Mont. 233; 136 P.3d 551; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 210


November 16, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
May 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 15, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and For the County of Sanders, Cause No. DC 2003-33, Honorable Deborah Kim Christopher, Presiding Judge.
State v. Trull, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2995, 2004 ML 1121 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Twentieth Judicial District, In and For the County of Sanders, Montana, convicting him of felony aggravated assault and denying his motion for a new trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that he purposely hit the victim during a barroom brawl; therefore, the first element of aggravated assault was undisputed. He challenged the finding that the victim sustained "serious bodily injury." Pretrial, the victim said only that he suffered blurred vision. At trial, the victim complained of sharp shooting pains in his head and double-vision; he also stated that three teeth were loosen. The new testimony was immaterial; therefore, the district court did not abuse its discretion when it denied defendant's motion for a new trial based on allegations of perjury. Defense counsel was not ineffective for failing to request a continuance on the second day of trial when he received the victim's undisclosed medical records. The aggravated assault statute, Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-202(1), was not misleading or unconstitutionally vague. As used in Mont. Code Ann. § 45-2-101(66), the terms "protracted" and "impairment" were not obscure or incomprehensible.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Galpin v. State


No. 05-289


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 108N; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 188


January 19, 2006, Submitted on Briefs  
May 16, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Galpin v. State, 138 P.3d 426, 2006 Mont. LEXIS 276 (Mont., 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Cause No. DC 2000-50, Honorable Jeffrey H. Langton, Presiding Judge.
State v. Galpin, 2003 MT 324, 318 Mont. 318, 80 P.3d 1207, 2003 Mont. LEXIS 793 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, In and For the County of Ravalli, Montana, denying his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: After two jury trials, appellant was convicted of the possession of dangerous drugs and production of methamphetamines. He was sentenced to fifty years in prison with twenty years suspended. He filed a petition for postconviction relief. Five of appellant's claims could have been raised on direct appeal, and therefore were procedurally barred. Counsel acted reasonably in deciding not to object to the portion of appellant's sentence resulting from his designation as a persistent felony offender under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-13-108. The elements of proof required for conviction of possession of precursors to dangerous drugs under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-9-107, differed from those required to prove production of dangerous drugs under Mont. Code Ann. § 45-9-110. Therefore, appellant's double jeopardy claim was meritless. Counsel did not err in refusing to move to dismiss the criminal endangerment charge for lack of evidence. The Supreme Court of Montana issued a memorandum opinion affirming the denial of postconviction relief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County Gallatin, Montana, convicting him on guilty pleas to escape, a felony in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-7-306; and theft, a felony in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-6-301.

Polasek v. Omura


No. 05-107


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 103; 332 Mont. 157; 136 P.3d 519; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 179


December 21, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
May 9, 2006, Decided  
Released for Publication May 26, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDR 97-390, Honorable Kenneth R. Neill, Presiding Judge.
In re Polasek, 2005 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 953, 2005 ML 1551 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a decision of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), which awarded respondent grandparents contact with the mother's daughter, pursuant to the grandparents' petition for contact under Mont. Code Ann. § 40-9-102(2).


OVERVIEW: After the relationship between the parties deteriorated, the mother forbade all contact between the grandparents and the child. The trial court ultimately awarded the grandparents contact with the child, but the court reversed and remanded on appeal. The court held that, for purposes of Mont. Code Ann. § 40-9-102(2), grandparent proceedings had to being with the presumption that a fit parent acted in the child's best interest, and the statute's best interest standard, as enacted, remained intact as the standard by which a grandparent's request for contact had to be judged. The court did not declare the statute to be unconstitutional. In this case, there was no indication that the trial court inquired into the mother's fitness as a parent, and the trial court failed to accord the mother's wishes any deference. Thus, the trial court failed to apply the correct analysis and remand was required. Given that the mother's appeal was a request for a proper delineation of parental rights, not whether the best interest standard under the statute was unconstitutional, the court did not address another argument that claimed the mother's appeal was procedurally barred.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded.

City of Great Falls v. Morris

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following jury convictions in the municipal court on charges of misdemeanor driving under the influence (DUI) and careless driving, defendant filed an appeal in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County, Montana. The district court affirmed. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with DUI and careless driving following a traffic stop. He refused to perform sobriety tests and would not take a breath test. The burden of proof did not unconstitutionally shift to defendant. The municipal court did not err in failing to instruct the jury to distrust weaker and less satisfactory evidence. In light of the evidence, a rational jury could have determined that defendant drove carelessly in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 61-8-302(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Wiser v. State


No. 04-587


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 20; 331 Mont. 28; 129 P.3d 133; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 31


June 21, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
January 31, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 16, 2006.
Related proceeding at Wiser v. Mont. Bd. of Dentistry, 2010 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 416 (2010)
Related proceeding at Denturist Assoc. of MT v. State Dept. of Labor and Industry, 2015 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 66 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV 2001-647, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Presiding Judge.
Board of Dentistry v. Kandarian, 248 Mont. 444, 813 P.2d 409, 1991 Mont. LEXIS 135 (Mont., 1991)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant denturists and denture patients appealed the order of the First Judicial District Court, Lewis and Clark County, Montana, granting summary judgment in favor of respondents, the Montana Department of Commerce, Department of Labor and Industry, and the Montana Board of Dentistry (BOD), on appellants' claims challenging state regulation of the denturity profession.


OVERVIEW: In Montana, denturists and denture patients challenged the constitutionality of both the Partial Denture Rule and the statutory framework which placed the profession of denturity under the regulatory thumb of the BOD. The court rejected both challenges, upholding both the constitutionality of Mont. Admin. R. 24.138.416, the partial denture rule, and the placement of denturity under the control of the BOD. While the denturists had a fundamental right to pursue denturity as a profession under Mont. Const. art. II, § 3, it did not follow that denturists had a fundamental right to practice denturity free of all regulation. Appellants' claim under the Montana Unfair Trade Practices and Consumer Protection Act (MUTPA), Mont. Code Ann. § 30-14-205(2)(c), failed as a matter of law. The BOD was not subject to MUTPA. Appellants were not deprived of due process; therefore, their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claimed fails.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Matter of R.E.A.


No. 04-058


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 12; 330 Mont. 392; 127 P.3d 517; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 12


November 3, 2004, Heard and Submitted  
January 17, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 2, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDP 2000-205. Honorable Julie Macek, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services (DPHHS), appealed the judgment entered in the Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County, Montana, requiring DPHHS to provide community-based services to respondent, an adult male with a developmental disability. The district court held Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The district court found respondent to be "seriously developmentally disabled" as defined in Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-102(15) (1999), and committed him involuntarily to the Montana Developmental Center. One month before the end of his commitment, the residential facility screening team, acting pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-133, and under DPHHS's authority, determined respondent was no longer seriously developmentally disabled. Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 did not prohibit the court from ordering the provision of community-based services. In the event Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 did prohibit such an order, the statute was unconstitutional because it violated respondent's rights to due process, dignity, equal protection, and speedy remedy for every injury. Given respondent's placement in community-based services, the case was moot.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

State v. Mizenko


No. 04-488


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2006 MT 11; 330 Mont. 299; 127 P.3d 458; 2006 Mont. LEXIS 11


April 15, 2005, Heard; April 26, 2005, Submitted  
January 11, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Released for Publication: January 30, 2006.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Mizenko v. Montana, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 5705 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and For the County of Chouteau, Cause No. DC 2003-13, Honorable David G. Rice, Presiding Judge.
Mont. v. Mizenko, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2953 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, in and for the County of Chouteau (Montana) of a third offense of partner or family member assault in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-206. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged in the assault on his wife. She did not testify at trial, but her neighbor, the 911 operator, and the responding officer did. Defendant had objected to the hearsay statements on the ground that they denied him the right to confrontation under U.S. Const. amend. VI, but the trial court admitted the statements. Defendant was convicted and the court affirmed on appeal. The court held that generally, when a declarant knowingly spoke to a government agent, the statements were presumed testimonial. Because the 911-taped statements that defendant had hurt his wife were admitted without objection, the operator's testimony and the officer's testimony about the same actions, even if objectionable, were cumulative and thus harmless error. As to the neighbor's testimony about what defendant's wife said, given that the wife was in distress and addressing a non-governmental agent, she had no objective reason to believe or anticipate that her statement was going to be used in court. The wife's statement was non-testimonial, the admission of the neighbor's hearsay testimony did not offend the Confrontation Clause, and was admissible under Mont. R. Evid. 803(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Friends of the Wild Swan v. Dep't of Natural Res. & Conservation


No. 04-862


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 351; 330 Mont. 186; 127 P.3d 394; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 625


July 13, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
December 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: January 25, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV-2003-527, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Presiding Judge.
Friends of the Wild Swan v. Department of Natural Resources and Conservation, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2478, 2004 ML 87 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant environmental group challenged a decision of the District Court of the First Judicial District, in and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), which granted summary judgment in favor of respondents, Montana Department of Natural Resources and Conservation and Montana Board of Land Commissioners, regarding the group's claim that Mont. Code Ann. § 77-1-202 (2003) required harvest-specific accountings. The group sought attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: The group challenged the Board's methodology in evaluating timber sale transactions and claimed that Mont. Code Ann. § 77-1-202(1) (2003) required accountings that were harvest-specific. The trial court rejected the group's challenge and ruled in favor of the Department and Board, and the court affirmed on appeal. In interpreting § 77-1-202(1) in accordance with Mont. Code Ann. § 1-2-101, the court noted that the plain language of the statute did not require the accountings suggested by the group. Other statutes, including Mont. Code Ann. §§ 77-1-223, 77-1-224, required the Board to account for costs and profits in the timber-sale process, and in light of the explicit accounting directives in these statutes, the court could not conclude that the Montana Legislature meant to imply a more specific accounting requirement within Mont. Code Ann. § 77-1-202(1) (2003). The court held that a harvest-level accounting of timber sales was not implicit within § 77-1-202(1), and the Board was not in violation of the statute when it did not conduct harvest-level financial reconciliation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and denied the group's request for attorney fees.

In re T.W.


No. 04-064


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 340; 330 Mont. 84; 126 P.3d 491; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 532


November 3, 2004, Heard; June 25, 2005, Submitted  
December 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: January 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and For the County of Missoula, Cause No. DD 99-4, Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient challenged a decision of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, in and for the County of Missoula (Montana), which denied her motion for injunctive and declaratory relief against respondent State. The trial court found that Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 was constitutional and the patient was not entitled to immediate placement in community-based services after her involuntary commitment expired.


OVERVIEW: The patient was ordered involuntarily committed for one year to receive treatment and habilitation. The patient filed a motion for declaratory and injunctive relief, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The trial court did not err in finding that Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 was constitutional. The patient's challenge to the statute as an unconstitutional bar to services and the courts, for purposes of Mont. Const. art. II, § 16, was flawed partially because it did not recognize that the statute worked with the administrative process. In light of Mont. Const. art. XII, § 3 and the patient's narrow focus of challenge, the court found that Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 was facially constitutional, and the patient's claim, that the statute barred her only remedy, was inaccurate, given that it ignored administrative remedies she could have pursued to address her claim of delayed placement. The court was unable to determine whether the patient's individual constitutional rights, such as privacy, were violated as a result of the delay in her placement in community-based services because she did not exhaust her administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

In re Custody & Parental Rights of D.S.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother appealed the order of the District Court for the First Judicial District, Lewis and Clark County, Montana, terminating her parental rights to her son and granting legal custody of him to the respondent Department of Public Health and Human Services (DPHHS) (Montana) with the right to consent to his adoption or guardianship.

Bingman v. State, 2003 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2653 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was convicted of driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI), a felony. He was sentenced to Montana State Prison for twenty years, with ten years suspended. The District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, Montana, denied his petition for post-conviction relief. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner did not appeal his 1986 conviction or sentences for felony assault and felony tampering with a witness. He was released from prison in 1997. In 2001, he was convicted of DUI. He filed a petition for postconviction relief, challenging his designation as a persistent felony offender. The district court correctly denied the petition. Petitioner could not prohibit the use of his 1986 conviction for assault to designate him as a persistent felony offender.

303 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Killam


No. 05-016


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 255; 329 Mont. 50; 122 P.3d 439; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 428


August 30, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
October 18, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: November 03, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. ADC 03-603. Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana) to aggravated assault. He was sentenced by the trial court and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During plea negotiations, the State apparently offered to recommend a sentence of 20 years on the assault charge, with an additional five years suspended for the use of a dangerous weapon. Defendant rejected the plea and later entered an open guilty plea. At the sentencing hearing, the State recommended a sentence greater than the one it earlier offered to recommend. Defendant argued that this violated his right to due process. The court disagreed on appeal and affirmed. The State's sentencing recommendation to which defendant objected did not occur during proceedings on retrial. The State, after defendant rejected the plea agreement, was free to proceed with the case and make any legal sentencing recommendation because no agreement to the contrary had been reached. When defendant entered his guilty plea, the trial court informed defendant of the 30-year maximum possible sentence. With no plea agreement in place, the State was not prevented from recommending the maximum sentence. There was no due process violation as claimed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Farrier v. Teacher's Ret. Bd.


No. 04-760


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 229; 328 Mont. 375; 120 P.3d 390; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 397


July 26, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
September 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: September 29, 2005.
On remand at Farrier v. Teacher's Ret. Bd., 2007 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 306 (2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV 2001-402, The Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Judge presiding.
Farrier v. Teachers' Ret. Bd. of the Mt., 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2427 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent retired teacher challenged the statutory scheme governing the eligibility for public pensions of employees who worked for a local school district, retired, and then began work at the University of Montana. The First Judicial District Court, Lewis and Clark County, Montana, granted summary judgment for the teacher. Appellant, the teacher's retirement board, filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The teacher retired from her position with the school district, and then accepted a position with the University of Montana. Her employment with the University triggered the application of two inter-locking provisions of Montana's teacher retirement system: Mont. Code Ann. § 19-21-202 and Mont. Admin. R. 2.44.305. These provisions prevented a retired teacher from receiving retirement benefits from a state sponsored retirement program while he remained an employee of the University and a contributing member of another private retirement program. The Supreme Court of Montana held that the statutory scheme did not violate the teacher's right to equal protection. The district court erred by concluding otherwise. The teacher was given an opportunity to make an election of benefits.


OUTCOME: The district court's determination was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Damon


No. 04-294


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 218; 328 Mont. 276; 119 P.3d 1194; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 381


May 2, 2005, Argued; May 10, 2005, Submitted  
September 6, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: September 22, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDC 2002-542, The Honorable Kenneth R. Neill, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a criminal prosecution for felony driving under the influence (DUI), the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, County of Cascade, Montana, ruled that the State could admit the results of defendant's preliminary breath test at trial. Defendant was convicted, designated as a persistent felony offender, and sentenced to 10 years, with five years suspended. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer observed defendant driving erratically and pulled him over. A preliminary alcohol screening test revealed defendant's blood alcohol content (BAC) to be 0.274. The State charged defendant with fourth offense DUI. The State presented sufficient evidence supporting the reliability of the preliminary breath test (PBT) to permit the results of defendant's test as substantive evidence at his trial. The district court did not abuse its discretion in admitting statements that defendant made to police during an investigatory stop in spite of the officer's failure to recite the advisories required by Mont. Code Ann. § 46-5-402(4)(2001). Defendant uttered the statements "just give me a DUI," and "I'm already drunk," without any prompting by the investigating officer. The district court properly designed defendant as a persistent felony offender pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-502.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment entered by the Fourth Judicial District Court, Missoula County, Montana, on his conviction and sentence for the offense of sexual intercourse without consent.


OVERVIEW: During voir dire on the first day of trial, defense counsel questioned the panel regarding whether any of them considered the act of anal sexual intercourse between two males so abhorrent that it would affect their ability to weigh the evidence fairly. Defendant also failed to prove that the district court improperly instructed the jury regarding witness credibility. The jury was correctly instructed on the applicable law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Montanans for the Responsible Use of the School Trust v. Darkenwald

SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 190; 328 Mont. 105; 119 P.3d 27; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 347


February 2, 2005, Argued; February 8, 2005, Submitted  
August 9, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: September 06, 2005.
Rehearing denied by Mont. For The Responsible Use of The School Trust v. Darkenwald, 2005 Mont. LEXIS 387 (Mont., Sept. 6, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. ADV-2001-130, The Honorable Dorothy McCarter, Judge presiding.
Montanans for the Responsible Use of the School Trust v. State ex rel. Bd. of Land Comm'rs, 1999 MT 263, 296 Mont. 402, 989 P.2d 800, 1999 Mont. LEXIS 277 (1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant citizens group challenged a decision from the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), which entered judgment in favor of respondents, a state treasurer, a land board, an investment board, and an agency director, in a dispute regarding the administration of school trust lands.


OVERVIEW: The group contended that the land board violated the Montana Constitution and breached its duty of trust by the commingling of trust assets into the general fund and the sale of a future stream of mineral royalties from school trust land in exchange for an immediate cash infusion. After judgment was entered against the group, it sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the commingling of interest income under Mont. Code Ann. § 17-6-202(2) did not necessarily mean that any duty had been violated. The land board accounted for the exact amount of interest and bonuses deposited into the general fund. Further, the enactment of Mont. Senate Bill 495, 2001 Mont. Laws 418, partially codified at Mont. Code Ann. § 17-6-340, did not violate the Montana Constitution and the Enabling Act, Act of February 22, 1889, § 11, ch. 180, 25 Stat. 676 (1889) because it did not abrogate the requirement to obtain full market value for school trust lands. The district court did not err by finding one expert witness on the issue of valuation more credible. Finally, the interests of the present and future beneficiaries were balanced when the sale of the future mineral royalties was conducted.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Kellogg v. Dearborn Info. Servs., L.L.C.


No. 04-623


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 188; 328 Mont. 83; 119 P.3d 20; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 345


May 3, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
July 28, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: September 01, 2005.

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV 2001-0689, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cotenant brought suit against defendant cotenant, requesting a partition of the property they held as tenants-in-common. The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, appointed referees pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 70-29-202(1). The referees settled on a plan of division. The district court adopted the referees' report. Plaintiff appealed the imposition of "no build" zones.


OVERVIEW: This action involved a tenancy in a rural valley. The parties owned the property as tenants-in-common. The district court referred the question of whether the property should be partitioned to a referee. The referees' plan of division included the imposition of a "no build" zone. The district court did not err by adopting the plan. Given that Mont. Code Ann. § 70-29-209(2) gave the district court broad equitable powers, it was within the district court's powers to impose a servitude such as a "no build" zone.

State v. Allum

SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 150; 327 Mont. 363; 114 P.3d 233; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 233

PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Cause No. DC 2002-216, Honorable Mike Salvagni, Presiding Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Montana, convicting him of criminal trespass.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal trespass for refusing to leave a bank after the teller refused to cash a check without defendant's thumbprint. Defendant's claim that the method of jury selection violated his right to trial by jury was not preserved for review. Jury instructions regarding criminal trespass correctly stated the law; and jury instructions on entrapment were not required. The criminal trespass statute was not vague or overbroad. Procedural irregularities did not prejudice defendant's trial. Specifically, the State did not commit a Brady violation in moving to quash several witness subpoenas on evidentiary grounds.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Seven Up Pete Venture v. Mont.


No. 03-154


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 146; 327 Mont. 306; 114 P.3d 1009; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 228; 60 ERC (BNA) 1869


October 28, 2003, Argued and Submitted  
June 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Released for Publication: July 11, 2005.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Seven Up Pete Venture v. Montana, 126 S. Ct. 1332, 164 L. Ed. 2d 48, 2006 U.S. LEXIS 1152 (U.S., 2006)
Companion case at Seven-Up Pete Venture v. Schweitzer, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28335 (D. Mont., Apr. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV 2000-250, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mining companies sued defendant, the State of Montana, alleging that Montana Initiative 137 interfered with their rights to mine property leased from the State. The District Court of the First Judicial District, County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, granted the State's motion for summary judgment. The plaintiffs appealed the district court's order denying their takings, contract impairment, and lease termination claims.


OVERVIEW: In 1986, the State of Montana leased six state properties for mining purposes. In one of the largest areas, a mining company operating as a joint venture discovered 9 million ounces of gold, and 20 million ounces of silver, which could be profitably recovered through a surface mine combined with cyanide leaching of the ore. In 1998, the citizens passed Montana Initiative 137 (I-137), which prohibited cyanide leaching for mining purposes. The district court held that I-137 did not effectuate a regulatory taking, because the joint venture had not secured an operating permit giving it the right to mine. While the law substantially impaired the contractual relationship between the joint venture and the State, the Contracts Clause was not violated; I-137 was reasonably related to the legitimate purpose of protecting the environment. The Department of Natural Resources and Conservation was not obligated to extend the mineral leases to give the joint venture time to seek the invalidation of I-137.


OUTCOME: The judgment entered by the district court was affirmed.

Schmill v. Liberty Northwest Ins. Corp.
