2005 MT 144; 327 Mont. 293; 114 P.3d 204; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 226


April 20, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
June 7, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: June 24, 2005.
Decision reached on appeal by, Subsequent appeal at Schmill v. Liberty Northwest Ins. Corp., 2009 MT 430, 2009 Mont. LEXIS 675 (Dec. 22, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The Workers' Compensation Court, Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge.
Schmill v. Liberty Northwest Ins. Corp., 2003 MT 80, 315 Mont. 51, 67 P.3d 290, 2003 Mont. LEXIS 153 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurer and the Montana State Fund, challenged a decision of the Workers' Compensation Court (Montana), which held that (1) the rule that the Occupational Disease Act was unable to allow apportionment deductions in certain instances was retroactive, (2) a common fund was created, (3) respondent employee's attorneys were entitled to common fund fees, and (4) the common fund did not create a global lien. The employee also appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held in Schmill v. Liberty Northwest Ins. Corp. that under an equal protection analysis, the Occupational Disease Act (ODA) could not allow for apportionment deductions for non-occupational factors if the Montana Workers' Compensation Act (WCA) did not allow for such deductions. The trial court found that this rule was retroactive. The court affirmed in part on appeal. The court agreed that the rule announced in Schmill was retroactive. The court found that the lower court had jurisdiction to award common fund attorney fees, given Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-2905. The common fund did not arise until after the court issued the Schmill decision, and therefore it was proper for the employee's attorneys to wait until post-remand proceedings to request common fund attorney fees. The attorneys were not now estopped from requesting common fund attorney fees and there was no due process violation. The court held that the common fund created in Schmill applied a global lien against all claimants who might have benefitted from the decision, not just those whose benefits were paid by the insurer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the Schmill decision was retroactive to all cases not yet final or settled at the time of its issuance. The attorneys properly requested common fund attorney fees and the common fund did result in a global lien. The court did not disturb the finding that Schmill created a common fund.


 

313 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tracy


No. 04-081


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 128; 327 Mont. 220; 113 P.3d 297; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 204


April 25, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
May 26, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: June 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDC-97-354, The Honorable Dirk M. Sandefur, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Tracy's sentence of December 16, 2003, is vacated. This case is remanded to the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, Cascade County, to enter a judgment imposing the same or a lesser sentence as that contained in the judgment of May 24, 2000.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County, Montana, revoked defendant's suspended commitment for felony theft, sentenced him to Montana State Prison for ten years, and denied credit for time he was in detention serving concurrent sentences entered in Yellowstone County, Montana. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a plea of guilty to felony theft. The offense was committed in December of 1996. He was committed to the Department of Corrections (DOC), for ten years with all time suspended. In 2003, defendant's suspended sentence was revoked and he was resentenced under the new law. The reimposed prison sentence was more burdensome, because it required defendant go to prison. The district court's application of the 2003 version of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-203 to defendant was an ex post facto application of the law. Mont. Code Ann. §§ 46-18-203(7)(b), 46-18-401(1)(a) required that defendant be given sentencing credit for time spent in a detention center or on home arrest on concurrent sentences entered in Yellowstone County.


OUTCOME: The sentence imposed was vacated. The case was remanded to the district court to enter a judgment imposing the same or a lesser sentence as that contained in the original judgment. As a part of such sentence, defendant was entitled to credit for time served in connection with the concurrent Yellowstone County sentences.

 

314 of 699 DOCUMENTS



Fellenberg v. Transp. Ins. Co.


No. 04-276


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 90; 326 Mont. 467; 110 P.3d 464; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 160


October 14, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
April 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: April 28, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana, Cause No. WCC 2002-0704, The Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee filed a workers' compensation claim. The Workers' Compensation Court, Montana, denied the claim under the Occupational Disease Act of 1985. The employee challenged the ruling.


OVERVIEW: The employee was diagnosed with asbestosis; one year later, he decided to retire at the age of 62. Years later, the asbestosis had grown much worse. The issues presented on appeal were: (1) whether the Workers' Compensation Court (WCC) erred in concluding that he was not entitled to permanent total disability (PTD) benefits; (2) whether the WCC erred in concluding that he was not entitled to 500 weeks of permanent partial disability (PPD) benefits; and (3) whether the WCC erred in concluding that he was not entitled to an impairment award. The WCC found that, while still capable of working, the employee voluntarily retired for reasons unrelated to his occupational asbestos disease. The WCC's ruling was properly based on the lack of causal connection between the claimed loss of wages and earning capability, and the illness. Even if the supreme court were to accept as true the employee's contention that he was 100 percent disabled because he had no earning capability in his labor market, the fact remained that his decision not to work again had been both long-standing and resolute. The supreme court also affirmed with respect to the claim for PPD benefits.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


 

315 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 03-563


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 87; 326 Mont. 427; 114 P.3d 1001; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 153


December 8, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
April 5, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: April 21, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDC 2002-319. The Honorable Julie Macek, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, Cascade County, Montana, entered a jury verdict finding defendant guilty of the offense of driving while under the influence of alcohol (DUI). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: An officer detected the odor of alcohol when he stopped defendant. At trial, defendant objected to the admission of the weekly field certification report on the intoxilyzer prepared by another officer, the yearly certification report, and the state crime lab report. Two issues were presented on appeal: (1) whether the appeal was properly before the supreme court; and (2) whether defendant's Sixth Amendment right to confrontation was implicated when the State introduced a certification report for a breath analysis instrument without also providing the author of the report for cross-examination? The supreme court held that the matter was properly before it, although the second issue had not been raised below; relevant caselaw was recently decided by the United States Supreme Court. The decision in this case turned on the issue of whether the certification reports were properly categorized as testimonial or nontestimonial evidence. The supreme court agreed with the State that the certification reports were nontestimonial evidence because they did not fall within the core group of statements which the Confrontation Clause was meant to address. The Sixth Amendment was not implicated.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the judgment.

 

316 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Columbia Falls Elem. Sch. Dist. No. 6 v. State


No. 04-390


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 69; 326 Mont. 304; 109 P.3d 257; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 79


October 20, 2004, Heard and Submitted  
March 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: April 06, 2005.
Request denied by Columbia Falls Elem. Sch. Dist. No. 6 v. State, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 509 (2006)
Findings of fact/conclusions of law at Columbia Falls Elem. Sch. Dist. No. 6 & H.S. Dist. No. 6 v. State, 2008 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 483 (2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV 2002-528, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Presiding Judge.
Columbia Falls Elem. Sch. Dist. No. 6 & H.S. Dist. No. 6 v. State, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 684 (Mont., Nov. 9, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, a coalition of schools and parents, contended that appellant state had acted unconstitutionally in administering and funding Montana's constitutionally-mandated public school system. The state appealed from the order of the District Court of the First Judicial District, County of Lewis and Clark (Montana) that determined that Montana's public school system violated the public schools clause, Mont. Const. art. X, § 1(3).


OVERVIEW: The state argued that the Supreme Court of Montana could not reach the issue of whether the current school system violated art. X, § 1(3), because the issue was a political question. The supreme court concluded that, since the legislature had addressed the threshold political question by implementing art. X, § 1(3), the question whether the system it created violated the constitution was not a political question. The requirement that the legislature should provide a basic system of free quality public schools, had to be read in conjunction with art. X, § 1, which guaranteed a right to education. Thus, the issue was justiciable and the supreme court affirmed the district court's determination. As the final guardian and protector of the right to education, it was incumbent upon the supreme court to assure that the system enacted by the legislature enforced, protected, and fulfilled the right. But, the legislature had not defined what "quality," as used in art. X, § 1(3), meant, thus the court could not conclude that the current system was designed to provide a "quality" education. Therefore, the supreme court deferred to the legislature for the definition of " quality."


OUTCOME: The opinion of the district court was affirmed in part. The effective date of the district court's opinion was affirmed. The issue of attorney fees was vacated and remanded and the issue was remanded for reconsideration. The district court's conclusion that the system did not violate the equal protection clause of the Montana Constitution was vacated.

State v. Johnson


No. 04-002


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 48; 326 Mont. 161; 108 P.3d 485; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 56


September 9, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
March 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication: March 17, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and for the County of Hill, Cause No. DC 2003-032. The Honorable John C. McKeon, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to three felony charges pursuant to a plea agreement with the State. The District Court of the Twelfth Judicial District, In and for the County of Hill, Montana, sentenced defendant to the Department of Corrections for eight years, with five years suspended. Among other conditions of release to probation or parole, defendant was ordered to submit to DNA testing. Defendant appealed the DNA testing requirement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered into a plea agreement with the State in which he agreed to plead guilty to the crimes of burglary, theft, and forgery by common scheme. On appeal, defendant argued that it was unconstitutional to force someone convicted of and incarcerated for non-violent felony offenses to submit to DNA testing. Defendant argued that this violated his right to privacy, as well as his right to be free from unreasonable searches and seizures. He did not, however, refute the State's assertion that he did not object on the search and seizure grounds in the sentencing court. Thus, this argument was not properly before the court. On the issue of whether the DNA test would violate defendant's right to privacy, it was unclear to the court whether defendant intended his argument to be construed as a constitutional challenge to Mont. Code Ann. § 44-6-103 (2003). Assuming that he did, the court could not make such a determination on the basis of the abbreviated arguments before it. Pursuant to § 44-6-103, a person convicted of a felony was required to submit to DNA testing. Defendant was convicted of a crime which met the definition of a "felony offense." Thus, his sentence was not illegal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence.

In re T.S.D.


No. 03-816


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 35; 326 Mont. 82; 107 P.3d 481; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 39


November 3, 2004, Orally Argued and Submitted  
February 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 9, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Second Judicial District, In and For the County of Butte-Silver Bow. Cause No. DD 99-1. Honorable Kurt D. Krueger, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Montana Department of Public Health and Human Services, challenged orders of the District Court of the Second Judicial District, Butte-Silver Bow County (Montana) that held respondent was not seriously developmentally disabled, concluded that Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-132 was unconstitutional, and ordered the Department to provide respondent with appropriate individualized community-based developmental disability services.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was a developmentally disabled adult diagnosed with personality disorders due to a childhood near-drowning incident that caused neurological damage. Respondent was committed to the state residential facility based on a report that he had sexually assaulted his three-year-old niece. When the Department petitioned for another one-year commitment term, the trial court found that respondent was not seriously developmentally disabled and ordered that he be provided with individualized community-based services. On appeal, the court held that the record of the hearing was devoid of any evidence that respondent could be "safely" habilitated in the community; therefore, the trial court erred in concluding he was not disabled. The court held that because respondent could not be safely habilitated in the community, he was seriously developmentally disabled as defined in Mont. Code Ann. § 53-20-102(15). The court noted that it was undisputed that respondent had behaviors which posed an imminent risk of serious harm to himself or others, that he needed constant supervision and structure, and that if placed in community services he could voluntarily refuse treatment and medication.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court orders that held respondent was not seriously developmentally disabled. The court did not address the issue of whether the statute, which provided that a court could not order the placement of or delivery of services to a developmentally disabled person in community-based services, was unconstitutional.

State v. Whiteman


No. 04-629


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 15; 325 Mont. 358; 106 P.3d 543; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 20


January 4, 2005, Submitted on Briefs  
February 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication February 17, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-Second Judicial District, In and for the County of Big Horn, Cause No. DC 04-12, The Honorable Blair Jones, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition of delinquency against defendant, a juvenile. The petition arose out of an alleged beating resulting in death and serious injury. The State then filed in district court a notice of its intent to transfer the case to district court. The Twenty-Second Judicial District Court, Big Horn County, Montana, entered a decision to allow prosecution of defendant's case in district court. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State alleged that defendant, using a baseball bat, beat and killed one victim and severely injured another victim. At the time, defendant was 13 years old. The district court eventually assigned to the State the burden of proof under the transfer statute. Defendant asserted that the district court contemplated only selective factual allegations, proposed by the State and adopted verbatim by the court, that falsely portrayed the nature of the alleged incident. The supreme court concluded that the district court made comprehensive findings of fact that intimately detailed the testimony offered at trial. As to defendant's allegations of clear error, the district court received testimony at trial from both parties concerning the interests of the community and of defendant. The supreme court concluded that substantial credible evidence supported the findings that probable cause existed for the charge of deliberate homicide and thus prosecution in district court under Mont. Code Ann. § 41-5-206(3)(b).


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Rule v. Burlington Northern & Santa Fe Ry.


No. 04-145


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 6; 325 Mont. 329; 106 P.3d 533; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 5


August 25, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
January 25, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:
Released for Publication February 09, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDV 2003-975, Honorable Julie Macek, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed an order of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade (Montana) that granted defendant railroads' motion for a change of venue pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. §§ 25-2-122(2) and 25-2-201(1) in the employee's action to recover for injuries under the Federal Employers' Liability Act (FELA), 45 U.S.C.S. § 51.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that the Legislature did not intend Mont. Code Ann. § 25-2-122(2) to apply to FELA cases; that § 25-2-122(2) could not coexist with the liberal forum selection policy under FELA; and that § 25-2-122(2) was unconstitutional because it constituted an arbitrary and capricious limitation on FELA venue practice in Montana. The court concluded that the Legislature did not create an exception from the provisions of § 25-2-122(2) for FELA claims because § 25-2-122 did not expressly exclude FELA claims, thus it applied to FELA claims. The court held that under Mont. Code Ann. § 25-2-122(2), the state courts of Montana remained open to FELA plaintiffs on the same basis that they were open to tort litigants with causes of action springing from a different source. The court held that the employee failed to establish any reason why application of § 25-2-122(2) to FELA cases exceeded legislative discretion in enacting venue statutes. Therefore the court concluded that the employee had not met his burden of proving § 25-2-122(2) was unconstitutional. The court held that the trial court properly applied the venue statutes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that granted the railroads' motion for a change of venue.

State v. Webb

SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA

Post-conviction relief denied at, Motion denied by Webb v. State, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 491 (2006)

State v. Webb, 2003 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2527 (2003)



DISPOSITION: The District Court is affirmed on all issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, (Montana) that sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-219 for his conviction for Sexual Intercourse Without Consent, Second Offense, in violation of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-503, a felony.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for raping a handicapped neighbor after attempting to kill her by breaking her neck. Defendant challenged the mandatory life sentence imposed pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-219 for a second offense, and claimed the trial court erred in finding that the exception to the mandatory sentence provided in Mont. Code Ann. § 46-18-222(3) was not applicable. The court rejected defendant's claim of procedural and substantive due process violations, holding that the trial court correctly interpreted Mont. The court also rejected defendant's cruel and unusual punishment claim on the grounds that defendant was a serial rapist with a high risk to reoffend and was not likely he would be rehabilitated, and that the sentence was commensurate with the gravity of his crime. The court also held that there was no violation of separation of powers concerning the mandatory sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Motta v. Philipsburg Sch. Bd. Trs.


No. 04-296


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2005 MT 1N; 2005 Mont. LEXIS 1


October 14, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
January 3, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Motta v. Philipsburg Sch. Dist., 110 P.3d 1055, 2005 Mont. LEXIS 92 (Mont., Jan. 3, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Third Judicial District, In and For the County of Granite, Cause No. DV 2001-04, Honorable Ted L. Mizner, Presiding Judge.
Motta v. Philipsburg Sch. Bd. Trs., 2004 MT 386N, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 666 (Dec. 28, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen brought suit against defendant school board trustees alleging the board violated open meeting laws when a contract was made between a school district and a contractor without any bidding. The District Court of the Third Judicial District, Granite County, Montana, entered a summary judgment in the board's favor. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the citizen contended, inter alia, that the school superintendent did not have the authority to apply federal grants, the trial court abused its discretion by failing to void the contract in question, and the school district should have bid out the contract. While the superintendent did not have statutory authority to apply for grants, there was an affidavit stating that the school board delegated it's authority to apply for grants to the superintendent. As the citizen only offered a speculative statement that this affidavit was insufficient proof, the appellate court held that he failed to raise a genuine issue of material fact. However, the superintendent signed the contract before obtaining the school board's approval; thus, the contract exceeded the superintendent's authority. Still, the appellate court could not determine a specific remedy, as the contract had already run its course and had presumably expired; this was a question more appropriately addressed by the trial court. As this was a public services contract, the school district was required to let the contract to the lowest responsible bidder in accordance with Mont. Code Ann. § 20-9-204(3) (2001).


OUTCOME: The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Snetsinger v. Mont. Univ. Sys.


No. 03-238


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 390; 325 Mont. 148; 104 P.3d 445; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 675


November 13, 2003, Orally Argued and Submitted  
December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. CDV 2002-097, The Honorable Thomas C. Honzel, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Decision of the District Court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, several employees and their same-sex partners, challenged a decision from the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark (Montana), which granted respondent university's motion to dismiss a case challenging the constitutionality of its benefits policy.


OVERVIEW: The university's policy prohibited gay employees from receiving insurance coverage for their same-sex domestic partners. The employees and their partners contended that this violated Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. After the district court granted the university's motion to dismiss the declaratory action, the employees and their partners sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the district court erred by finding that the university's classification was based on martial status. Actually, the policy allowed the opposite-sex partners of employees to apply for benefits by signing an affidavit. The signing of the affidavit did not create a common law marriage between the parties under Mont. Code Ann. § 40-1-403. In order to establish a common law marriage, three elements had to be satisfied. A mere affidavit was insufficient. Because the unmarried partners of employees were treated differently by the university's policy, and there was no justification for such, Mont. Const. art. II, § 4 was violated because the policy was not rationally related to a legitimate governmental interest.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed.

State v. Baker


No. 03-098


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 393; 325 Mont. 229; 104 P.3d 491; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 671


January 27, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDC 2002-294 The Honorable Julie Macek, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: District Court's decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, Cascade County, Montana, for the misdemeanor offense of attempting to obstruct a peace officer. She was sentenced to six months in prison, with all but four days suspended, and was also sentenced to pay a $ 500 fine, with $ 250 suspended. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: As police officers were executing a high risk search warrant on a suspected drug dealer's home, defendant, the drug dealer's neighbor, telephoned and advised him through a telephone answering machine that police officers were surrounding his house. Defendant was arrested and later convicted for attempting to obstruct a peace officer. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying her motion to suppress, in admitting certain evidence, and by failing to fully and fairly instruct the jury on the law applicable to the case. The appellate court noted that despite defendant's protestations that she did not intend, or have the purpose, to hinder the officers, the evidence was sufficient to convict her of attempting to obstruct the police in their efforts to perform a legally authorized search; thus, her motion to suppress was properly denied. The appellate court held that under the transaction rule, the trial court did not abuse its discretion when it allowed the State to introduce evidence regarding the high-risk nature of the law enforcement event. The appellate court concluded that the jury was fairly and fully instructed on the law applicable to the case.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

325 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Dempsey v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 04-032


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 391; 325 Mont. 207; 104 P.3d 483; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 673


July 14, 2004, Argued; August 31, 2004, Submitted  
December 30, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 20, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIFIED QUESTION FROM: The United States District Court, District of Montana, Butte Division, Honorable Sam E. Haddon, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Court concluded that Hardy decision applies retroactively to require payment of stacked uninsured, underinsured motorist and medical payment insurance coverages in qualifying circumstances on open claims arising before its issuance. Court limited this retroactivity to cases pending on direct review or not yet final.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff class members filed an action against defendant insurer to recover benefits under their policies. The insurer filed a motion to dismiss. The United States District Court, District of Montana, Butte Division, certified a question concerning the retroactive application of case law involving the stacking of underinsured motorist (UIM) benefits and medical payments to the court.


OVERVIEW: The class members contended that the retroactive application of Hardy v. Progressive Specialty Insurance Co. entitled them to recover payments previously denied based on stacking limitations in the policies. The question of whether the case was retroactively applied was certified to the court. In finding that the case did have retroactive application to cases not yet final, the court examined its rules on the issue. It determined that the rules of retroactivity set forth in Chevron Oil v. Hudson still applied in Montana as an exception. All civil decisions from the Montana Supreme Court applied retroactively to cases pending on direct review or not yet final, unless all three of the Chevron Oil v. Hudson factors were satisfied. The court then determined that the Hardy case applied retroactively because the insurer was unable to even meet the first Chevron factor. The court held that Hardy did not establish a new principal of law because it did not clearly overrule past precedent or decide an issue of first impression whose resolution was not clearly foreshadowed. Dissatisfaction with Mont. Code Ann. § 33-23-203 had been expressed in other cases.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the case applied retroactively to all cases pending on direct review or not yet final.

 

326 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Motta v. Philipsburg Sch. Bd. Trs.


No. 04-295


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 387N; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 662


October 14, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 28, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Motta v. Philipsburg Sch. Dist., 106 P.3d 133, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 745 (Mont., Dec. 28, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: The District Court of the Third Judicial District, In and For the County of Granite, Cause No. DV 2001-03, Honorable Ted L. Mizner, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: District Court's decision affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of a judgment from the District Court of the Third Judicial District, In and For the County of Granite (Montana) rendered in favor of appellees the school board and the trustees in an action brought by the individual seeking to void the board's goals grant.


OVERVIEW: The school board developed a goals granted and vested the superintendent with the authority to apply for the grant. The superintendent made application and then set aside funds for various teacher education programs. The individual brought an action against the school board and the trustees seeking to void the grant. The matter was arbitrated, but the individual failed to cooperate. As a result the trial court refused to void the goals grant and issued sanctions against the individual. The individual appealed the judgment. The court noted that the school board was vested with the discretion to delegate authority with regard to grants. However, the authority in this case was delegated to the superintendent only to apply for the grant, and it did not include spending the money. The dilemma was what to do with the violation when the grant had been approved, the money had been spent, and the grant had expired. The court opted to reverse and remand the matter to the district court for further proceedings on this dilemma. Furthermore, the court found that the application of sanctions under Mont. R. Civ. P. 11 was erroneous, which mandated reversal as well.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Am. Cancer Soc'y v. State


No. 03-453


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 376; 325 Mont. 70; 103 P.3d 1085; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 655


April 29, 2004, Argued; October 19, 2004, Submitted  
December 28, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment in original proceeding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff activists filed an original proceeding against defendant State to have Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-120 declared unconstitutional as violating the local self-governing provisions of Mont. Const. art. XI, § 6. The activists sought attorney fees under the private attorney general theory.


OVERVIEW: Activists sued to challenge the constitutionality of Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-120, which exempted licensed video gambling machine operators from local anti-smoking ordinances that were more restrictive than the Montana Clean Indoor Air Act of 1979, Mont. Code Ann. §§ 50-40-101 to 109. The court held that the exemption in Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-120 was not a prohibition because the exemption did not deny cities the power to act, but merely created an exception to certain ordinances. Although Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-112(5) prohibited local governments from regulating gaming establishments, local anti-smoking did not regulate gaming, but merely regulated the air inside all buildings, whether or not gaming occurred in such buildings. Therefore, because Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-120 did not expressly prohibit local governments from enacting restrictive anti-smoking ordinances, and because such ordinances were not inconsistent with Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-112(5), Mont. Code Ann. § 7-1-120 did not preempt any local anti-smoking ordinance and was ineffective. Because § 7-1-120 was ineffective rather than unconstitutional, the activists were not entitled to attorney fees.


OUTCOME: The court held that the statute was ineffective but not unconstitutional, and that the activists were not entitled to attorney fees under the private attorney general theory.

 

328 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Burkhart


No. 03-108


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 372; 325 Mont. 27; 103 P.3d 1037; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 654


July 7, 2004, Argued; July 13, 2004, Submitted  
December 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 23, 2011.
Released for Publication January 12, 2005.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Burkhart v. Mahoney, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 47683 (D. Mont., Apr. 2, 2010)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Findings of fact/conclusions of law at Burkhart v. State, 2016 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 42 (Nov. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. ADC-01-493-2, The Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Judge presiding.
Montana v. Burkhart, 2002 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 2303 (Nov. 8, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade (Montana) of deliberate homicide, felony-murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the eyewitness testimony and forensic evidence presented by the State failed to corroborate his accomplice's testimony, proving only suspicion and not justifying a conviction. The supreme court disagreed. Setting aside the testimony of the accomplice entirely, the jury heard eye-witness testimony that defendant pursued two men towards the place where the victim was walking home. The jury also heard that defendant was extremely angry about his car being broken into. A witness testified that defendant confronted someone resembling the victim in the alley. Jurors also heard evidence that an altercation probably ensued in the alley. Police found the victim's body several feet away from the initial confrontation spot with at least four severe blows to the head. In particular, two skull wounds that produced a depression were matched with the ball-peen hammer found in proximity to the victim's body. Further, the shape and the size of the fractures in the skull were a signature of the instrument and accounted for the multiple fractures. Therefore, the corroborating evidence was sufficient.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

329 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Reesor v. Mont. State Fund


No. 03-639


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 370; 325 Mont. 1; 103 P.3d 1019; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 658


May 5, 2004, Argued and Submitted  
December 22, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 12, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana, The Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Montana Workers' Compensation Court granted judgment in favor of respondent Montana State Compensation Insurance Fund by rejecting appellant employee's workers' compensation claim, holding that Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-710 was constitutionally sound because the receipt of social security retirement benefits was a yardstick for determining whether there would be future wage loss and it did not violate equal protection. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that the age limitation on permanent partial disability (PPD) benefits, set forth in Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-710, violated Mont. Const. art. II, § 4. The employee maintained that the two classes involved were PPD eligible claimants who received or were eligible to receive social security retirement benefits and PPD claimants who did not receive and were not eligible to receive social security retirement benefits. The appellate court concluded that the classes were similarly situated for equal protection purposes. The disparate treatment of partially disabled claimants based upon their age, because they were receiving or were eligible to receive social security retirement benefits, was not rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest of establishing a wage replacement for injured workers. Social security retirement benefits and social security disability benefits were two distinct programs and could not offset one another due to the fact that both were based on completely different concepts. There was no rational basis to deny a class of injured workers a category of benefits based upon their age.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the workers' compensation court for redetermination of benefits due to the employee.

 

330 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Bustell v. AIG Claims Serv., Inc.


No. 04-124


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 362; 324 Mont. 478; 105 P.3d 286; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 630


June 29, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 07, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: Workers' Compensation Court, State of Montana, The Honorable Mike McCarter, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: WCC decision affirmed on all issues.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee sought review of a judgment of the Workers' Compensation Court (Montana), which awarded her attorney's fees in her action against respondent insurers.


OVERVIEW: The employee was rendered a quadriplegic in an accident. She filed a workers' compensation claim arising out of the accident and hired an attorney to represent her. The employee and attorney entered into a contingent fee arrangement whereby the attorney was to recover 25 percent of the post-judgment award. The matter proceeded to trial and the claim was found to be compensable. The compensation court awarded attorney fees at an hourly rate instead of the amount requested by the employee. The employee appealed. The court affirmed the compensation court's ruling that the hourly attorney fee rule of Mont. Code Ann. § 39-71-614 (1999) passed scrutiny under substantive due process. The court also agreed that § 39-71-614 did not violate equal protection because workers with large awards were not a separate class from workers with smaller awards. The compensation court's increase of the maximum attorney fee was proper; the variance was determined correctly.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

331 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Thaut


No. 02-460


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 359; 324 Mont. 460; 103 P.3d 1012; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 629


December 15, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 20, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication January 06, 2005.
Post-conviction relief denied at Thaut v. State, 2007 MT 19N, 2007 Mont. LEXIS 24 (Jan. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and for the County of Flathead, Cause No. DC 98-369B, The Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a supplemental order of the District Court for the Eleventh Judicial District, Flathead County (Montana), which reduced the amount of restitution that he was required to pay after he pled guilty to felony aggravated assault and criminal mischief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot his victim in the face as the victim sat in a car. His prison sentence was conditioned on the payment of restitution in the event he was paroled. At a resentencing hearing, the restitution was decreased. On appeal, the court declined to address defendant's constitutional challenges to the amended restitution statutes, as he did not establish standing by showing a direct or threatened personal injury resulting from application of the statutes. Rather, his restitution was determined under a previous version of the statutes and, according to the length of time he would have to pay it, only part of it was for property damages, and the only effect the amended statutes would have had on him was requiring him to pay the department of corrections rather than the clerk. The court held that the district court adequately complied with the statutory requirements in determining the amount of restitution, which was based on the victim's special damages and a grant from the board of crime control, because it relied on testimony, a psychiatric evaluation, and presentence investigations showing that defendant had no documented disabilities and stated that he was a hard worker.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order requiring defendant to pay restitution in the reduced amount.

 

332 of 699 DOCUMENTS


In re P.D.L.


No. 03-801


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 346; 324 Mont. 327; 102 P.3d 1225; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 612


June 8, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
December 7, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 29, 2004.
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by P. S. v. Montana, 544 U.S. 1023, 125 S. Ct. 1988, 161 L. Ed. 2d 866, 2005 U.S. LEXIS 3845 (2005)
Related proceeding at Smrz v. Smith, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 60518 (D. Mont., Jan. 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Mineral, Cause No. DN99-21, The Honorable Edward P. McLean, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee department of human services filed a petition seeking permanent legal custody of the child and termination of appellant father's parental rights with right to consent to adopt. The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Mineral County, Montana, terminated the parental rights of the father, and the child was adopted. His motion seeking relief from judgment was denied. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that the father had essentially abandoned his child, as he had not developed a substantial relationship with the child, had not provided support for the child for over a year, and was serving a lengthy incarceration for sexually abusing the mother's other children. On review, the father contended the trial court erred when it denied his motion for relief from judgment because his parental rights were terminated without providing him certain required due process protections. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the record did not support the father's lack of notice argument, as the department made numerous attempts to obtain information from the father and he failed to respond. Further, the father's motion was over two years late. Contrary to the father's contention, the record indicated that he was, at the very least, aware that termination proceedings were pending against him and a hearing to terminate his parental rights was imminent; regardless of any technical deviation from the requirements controlling service of process, it was unreasonable to wait more than two years after becoming aware that his parental rights were about to be terminated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

333 of 699 DOCUMENTS



State v. Snell


No. 03-109


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 334; 324 Mont. 173; 103 P.3d 503; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 599


January 24, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
November 23, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication December 9, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Cause No. DC-99-13969, The Honorable Douglas G. Harkin, Judge presiding.
State v. Snell, 2004 MT 258, 323 Mont. 84, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 430 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, Missoula County (Montana), convicted defendant of operating a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol or drugs, fourth offense, and driving while license suspended or revoked, a misdemeanor. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: When defendant was stopped, he smelled of alcohol and had bloodshot eyes. The officer read him the required preliminary alcohol screening test (PAST) implied consent warning and defendant provided a breath sample. He later provided a second sample, which the trial court excluded, as it was seized unlawfully. Only one PAST was allowed to be taken. The trial court properly concluded defendant's earlier DUI convictions were constitutionally firm. Defendant did not overcome the presumption of regularity through direct evidence. The trial court abused its discretion in denying defendant's motion in limine that questioned the reliability of the PAST and contended it was inadmissible as evidence of his guilt. Because the PAST was presented for the purpose of proving an element of the charged crime, intoxication, the State had to prove it would not have contributed to the conviction. The State did not meet this burden. The trial court properly allowed the officer to testify that defendant was under the influence of alcohol. He testified that, based on the odor of alcohol, defendant's bloodshot eyes and slurred speech, and defendant's driving behavior, defendant was under the influence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded to the trial court for retrial, during which the State could pursue a DUI conviction utilizing admissible evidence consistent with this opinion. The trial court's decision regarding the admissibility of the PAST evidence was reversed. The trial court abused its discretion in allowing even the first Alco-Sensor III test to be used as evidence of defendant's guilt at trial.

Basto v. State


No. 03-193


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 257; 323 Mont. 80; 97 P.3d 1113; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 434


October 30, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
September 14, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 29, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. ADC 2001-153-1. Honorable Thomas M. McKittrick, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed an order of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), dismissing his petition for postconviction relief, after he had pled guilty to charges of possession of a deadly weapon by a prisoner in a facility.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and his co-defendants, while in their respective cells, each knowingly possessed a sharpened metal object known as a "shank." After they refused to surrender the shanks, an officer successfully forced each to submit the shanks. After his plea was entered, the district court sentenced the inmate to five years in prison to be served concurrently with a sentence for criminal mischief the inmate received in a companion case. On appeal, the inmate argued that, pursuant to the Eighth Amendment of the United States Constitution, his sentence was disproportionately severe when compared to his co-defendants' sentences, and therefore constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court held that the inmate received the sentence he bargained for in his plea bargain, the voluntariness of his guilty pleas were not at issue, and his sentence fell within the maximum guidelines. Thus, the sentence did not violate cruel and unusual punishment protections. Moreover, because the inmate failed to raise any Eighth Amendment claim on direct appeal, it was barred under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-105(2). The inmate's remaining claims were also barred and not preserved for review.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

State v. Lucero

SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 248; 323 Mont. 42; 97 P.3d 1106; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 423


July 3, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
September 8, 2004, Decided

Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition dismissed by, Motion denied by Lucero v. MacDonald, 186 P.3d 876, 2008 Mont. LEXIS 357 (Mont., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DC 2001-309. Honorable Susan P. Watters, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirteenth Judicial District Court, Yellowstone County, (Montana) of assault on a peace officer. The court denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that counsel was ineffective for failing to adequately explain the nature and terms of a plea offer. Defendant testified at the hearing and was afforded ample opportunity to present arguments and raise objections. Throughout his testimony, defendant repeatedly denied having received any information from counsel concerning the State's plea offer. Counsel testified that he conveyed the State's oral plea offer of 10 years and withdrawal of the persistent felony offender designation to defendant, but conceded that he might have stated that the offer was illusory, since the maximum sentence was 10 years. Counsel further described defendant as insistent about his innocence and in his desire to go to trial. The trial court concluded that counsel's conduct in communicating the plea offer did not fall below the standard of reasonable representation required of criminal defense attorneys and that defendant was fully informed of any plea offer made by the State, and defendant chose to proceed to trial.


OUTCOME: Four sentencing conditions were reversed and stricken from the written judgment on remand. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

Advocates for Educ., Inc. v. Mont. Dep't of Natural Res. & Conservation


No. 03-587


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 230; 322 Mont. 429; 97 P.3d 553; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 403


December 23, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
August 24, 2004, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and for the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV 2002-334(B). The Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant advocates sought a declaratory judgment in the District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, Flathead County, Montana, that respondent Montana Department of Natural Resources unlawfully determined that Mont. Code Ann. § 20-6-621(4) was unconstitutional and improperly used school trust lands. The trial court dismissed the complaint. The advocates appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department moved to dismiss the complaint on the basis that no justiciable controversy existed and that the complaint alleged no cause of action upon which relief could be granted. The trial court agreed and dismissed the complaint concluding that the advocates were not entitled to relief under any set of facts which could be proved in support of its claim. The appellate court held that any determination that the department exceeded its authority and failed in its duty to uphold the legality of Montana laws when it stipulated that the statute in question was unconstitutional, had absolutely no bearing on existing rights or interests at issue between the parties, and a judgment from an appellate court granting the relief sought would not effectively operate to resolve any controversy. The appellate court further held that any declaratory judgment would have been abstract and theoretical because the claim applied to no specific statute at issue or specific rights of the litigants in the case; therefore, there was no justiciable case or controversy.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Geil v. Missoula Irrigation Dist.


No. 03-664


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 217; 322 Mont. 388; 96 P.3d 1127; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 389


January 21, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
August 17, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 2, 2004.
Subsequent appeal at Larango v. Missoula Irrigation Dist., 2004 MT 369, 324 Mont. 534, 103 P.3d 552, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 642 (Dec. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Cause No. DV 97-8751-10, The Hon. Ed McLean, Hon. John S. Henson, Hon. John W. Larson, Hon. Douglas Harkin, Judges presiding.
Geil v. Missoula Irrigation Dist., 2002 MT 269, 312 Mont. 320, 59 P.3d 398, 2002 Mont. LEXIS 533 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, landowners, petitioned for exclusion of their land from inclusion within respondent irrigation district pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 85-7-1846 (1997). The District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Montana, entered a decree granting their exclusion. The irrigation district appealed both the trial court's earlier order denying its motion to amend its response and the decree.


OVERVIEW: The irrigation district asserted the trial court denied it due process by making findings without a hearing. The legislature had passed a bill, which provided, temporarily, a less stringent process for landowners to petition for exclusion of their tracts. In a prior appeal by the irrigation district, the Montana Supreme Court held that relevant legislation satisfied due process. Further, Mont. Code Ann. § 85-7-1846 (1997) comported with the fundamental due process requirement of an opportunity to be heard, even though the district court was not required to hold a hearing. In fact, despite three opportunities, including hearings before an appointed Standing Master, the irrigation district never submitted new information to support its position. Thus, there was no denial of due process. However, the district court did not have any authority to order the irrigation district to reimburse taxes paid without protest by the landowners, as tax refunds were a matter of legislative discretion. Finally, the district court did not abuse its discretion when it denied the irrigation district's motion to amend, as the issues it sought to raise were barred by collateral estoppel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part. The trial court's ruling that the landowners were entitled to reimbursement for taxes paid where they had made no protest in regard to same was reversed.

State v. McCaslin


No. 03-519


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 212; 322 Mont. 350; 96 P.3d 722; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 385


April 26, 2004, Submitted  
August 10, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 26, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, Cause No. DC 2002-44, The Honorable Mark L. Guenther, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Gallatin, (Montana) of aggravated assault, assault, and assault with a weapon. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in giving an intoxication instruction to the jury because it impermissibly shifted the burden of proof, and violated his right to due process. The supreme court disagreed. The jury was instructed on: (1) the elements of each offense charged and the State's burden of proving each element beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) the definition of the mental states, purposely and knowingly; (3) that the existence of a mental state may be inferred from the acts of the accused and the facts and circumstances connected with the offense; (4) the difference between direct and circumstantial evidence; (5) witness credibility; and (6) the need for a unanimous verdict. The instructions fully and fairly instructed the jury on the law applicable to the case. Accordingly, the trial did not abuse its discretion in instructing the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Weinert v. City of Great Falls


No. 03-823


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 168; 322 Mont. 38; 97 P.3d 1079; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 253; 29 A.L.R.6th 783


April 20, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
June 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and For the County of Cascade, Cause No. CDV-02-440. Honorable Kenneth R. Neill, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured sledder appealed from a judgment of the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, in and for the County of Cascade (Montana), which granted summary judgment to defendant City in the sledder's negligence and willful or wanton misconduct action, arising from injuries she sustained when she slid into a safety net that the City had installed at the bottom of a sledding hill.


OVERVIEW: The City had installed a safety net at the bottom of the sledding hill in order to cushion sledders who did not stop on their own. The sledder was injured, and she sued the City. The City sought summary judgment, claiming that it was immune from the negligence claim under Mont. Code Ann. § 70-16-302, which was part of the Recreational Use Act. The trial court granted summary judgment to the City, finding it was immune from the negligence claim and that willful or wanton misconduct was not shown. It also rejected the sledder's challenge to the constitutionality of § 70-16-302, holding that it was time-barred under Mont. Const. art. VI, § 11(6). On appeal, the court declined to consider the constitutionality question, as there was no compliance by the sledder with the notice requirements of Mont. R. App. P. 38. The court found that the immunity of Mont. Code Ann. § 70-16-302 applied, as sledding was within the definition of "recreational uses" under Mont. Code Ann. § 70-16-301. The City showed that it had investigated ways to prevent injuries, and the sledder did not meet her burden of offering evidence to raise an issue of fact as to the City's willful or wanton misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Merrill


No. 03-418


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 169; 322 Mont. 47; 93 P.3d 1227; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 256

June 29, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 15, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Nineteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Lincoln, Cause No. DC 2002-91, Honorable Michael C. Prezeau, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the District Court of the Nineteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Lincoln (Montana), which denied her motion to suppress evidence that was obtained from a search of her person and of the car that she was in. Defendant was charged and found guilty of possession of dangerous drugs.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was pulled over by the police for making an improper lane change. The police discovered that the car that defendant was driving belonged to an individual who was suspected of involvement with dangerous drugs. The police indicated that defendant was going to be issued a warning. However, one officer noticed that she appeared nervous, and he asked if she would empty her pockets and if he could search the vehicle, both of which she consented to. A piece of cellophane that was suspected of containing illegal drugs came from defendant's pocket. Defendant admitted it contained methamphetamine, and, after it field tested positive for that, defendant was arrested and charged. Her motion to suppress was denied, and she was convicted. On appeal, the court found that suppression was properly denied, as defendant was lawfully detained subsequent to the traffic stop, and the duration was not overly long under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-5-403. However, a reasonable person would have felt free to leave in the circumstances. Thereafter, defendant's consent to the warrantless search was based on a voluntary exchange with the officer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

Drew v. Mont. Tenth Judicial Dist. Court


No. 04-254


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 154; 321 Mont. 520; 92 P.3d 1195; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 240


April 15, 2004, Submitted  
June 21, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 7, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: ORIGINAL PROCEEDING: Writ of Supervisory Control.



DISPOSITION: Writ of Certiorari is denied. We therefore lift the stay previously entered in this cause.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorney filed a petition for a writ of certiorari to challenge a decision from respondents, a trial court and a presiding judge, which found her in contempt and imposed sanctions including the service of jail time.


OVERVIEW: The attorney was appointed to represent a client in a post-conviction proceeding. After many months had passed, the trial court inquired into the attorney's failure to take action. The attorney explained that she had personal problems, but assured the trial court that a brief and motion to withdraw from the case were forthcoming by a certain date. The attorney failed to file the papers, and she refused to take a phone call from the trial court. In a later hearing, the attorney was found in contempt, ordered to pay a fine, and sentenced to jail time. She then filed a petition for a writ of certiorari. In denying the writ, the court determined that the trial court was permitted to hear the contempt case under Mont. Code Ann. § 3-1-518 (2001), as amended, because the contempt arose from the violation of an order issued after a hearing on the merits. Section 3-1-518 was not unconstitutional because due process was clearly provided in the terms of the statute. The attorney failed to show that the judge was not impartial simply based on a statement regarding the attorney's credibility. The attorney did not present any other grounds in support of her request for a neutral magistrate.


OUTCOME: The attorney's petition was denied.

 

343 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Veis v. State


No. 02-671


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 139N; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 222


March 20, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
June 7, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Veis v. State, 94 P.3d 766, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 322 (Mont., June 7, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Cause No. DV 56-2002-744, Honorable G. Todd Baugh, Presiding Judge.
State v. Veis, 1998 MT 162, 289 Mont. 450, 962 P.2d 1153, 1998 Mont. LEXIS 139 (1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with three felony counts of sexual intercourse without consent, in violation of Mont. Code Ann. §45-5-503. A jury before the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Yellowstone, Montana, convicted defendant on all counts. Defendant petitioned for postconviction relief; the petition was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in dismissing his petition for postconviction relief on the basis that it was time-barred. Defendant maintained that the amendment of Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-102, which reduced the time for filing of a petition for postconviction relief, deprived him of the five-year filing period to which he was entitled. The supreme court concluded that defendant had approximately a year and a half prior to his conviction becoming final to absorb this change. The district court did not err in its determination that the petition was time-barred. Defendant also argued that the statute of limitation should be equitably tolled during the time defendant was incarcerated in another state. Nevertheless § 46-21-102 was a jurisdictional limit on postconviction litigation, and the supreme court held its waiver may only be justified by a clear miscarriage of justice. Further, the time bar did not constitute a violation of defendant's constitutional right against ex post facto laws. Finally, 13 of the 14 issues defendant raised were procedurally barred for failing to raise them on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Paulson v. Flathead Conservation Dist.


No. 02-733


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 136; 321 Mont. 364; 91 P.3d 569; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 216


May 13, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
May 25, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 20, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead, Cause No. DV 2001-420B, Honorable Katherine R. Curtis, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An arbitration panel found that respondent Flathead Conservation District (FCD) had jurisdiction over appellant property owners' waterfront project. The owners filed a motion to vacate the arbitration award. The District Court of the Eleventh Judicial District, In and For the County of Flathead (Montana), granted a motion for judgment on the pleadings by the FCD and respondent Montana Department of Fish, Wildlife and Parks. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The case involved a dispute between the owners and two agencies, the FCD and the Flathead Regional Development Office (FRDO). The FCD administered the Natural Streambed and Land Preservation Act of 1975 (Streambed Act), Mont. Code Ann. § 75-7-101 et seq., and the FRDO administered the Flathead County Lakeshore Protection Program (Lakeshore Program), governed by Mont. Code Ann. § 75-7-201 et seq. The owners argued that the arbitration panel was without authority to decide the jurisdictional question as to whether the situs of their project was a lake or a stream. The court stated that the FCD could determine what bodies of water were streams. Accordingly, an arbitration panel could review that determination. Application of the Lakeshore Program did not preclude application of the Streambed Act to a particular area, especially in situations where a construction project might be located simultaneously in a lake and where a river once flowed before lake waters were expanded as a result of construction of a dam. The court also held that the owners' partiality allegations relating to one of the arbitrators did not establish "evident partiality" under Mont. Code Ann. § 27-5-312(1)(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

Blake v. State


No. 03-619


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 118N; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 197


January 27, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
May 4, 2004, Decided

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision of the District Court of the Tenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Judith Basin (Montana), which denied his motion to correct his sentence, which motion was viewed as a petition for postconviction relief filed against respondent State.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had pleaded guilty to deliberate homicide and was sentenced to a total of 90 years in prison. The inmate's sentence was affirmed. The inmate then sought postconviction relief, which was denied as time-barred under Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-102. The inmate then filed the instant motion to correct his sentence. The trial court denied the motion, because the authority on which the inmate relied did not apply to the inmate, because he had not maintained his innocence of the crime. The court found that the inmate's motion fell within the statutes on postconviction relief, including Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-103, because the motion was a collateral attack on his sentence. The court noted that the inmate's first petition for postconviction relief was time-barred, and thus this second petition was also time-barred. There was no error.

State v. Richeson


No. 02-600


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 113; 321 Mont. 126; 89 P.3d 958; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 192


October 30, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
May 3, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication May 18,2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, Cause No. BDC-01-383, The Honorable Julie Macek, Judge presiding.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of four counts of sexual intercourse without consent and of three counts of unlawful transactions with minors. During jury selection, the District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade (Montana), denied defendant's motion to disqualify a juror for cause. Defendant appealed the denial and also argued that he was given ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's trial counsel moved to disqualify a juror for cause based on the juror's employment as a detention officer. The district denied the motion after the juror was questioned outside the presence of the jury panel. On appeal, the court affirmed the denial. The court stated that the bare fact that a potential juror was connected with law enforcement did not, without more, necessitate a finding of bias resulting in a dismissal for cause. Here, the juror's testimony did not reveal a state of mind in reference to defendant that would have prevented her from acting with entire impartiality and without prejudice to the substantial rights of defendant. Defendant also argued that he was given ineffective assistance of counsel because his trial counsel failed to advance the statutory criteria of a guardian-and-ward relationship, pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-16-115(2)(b) (1999), to remove the juror for cause. The court rejected defendant's argument, concluding that, notwithstanding any constitutional or statutory responsibilities a detention officer or guard might have toward a detainee, such responsibilities did not meet the requirements of a guardian-ward relationship.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's decision.

McDonald v. State


No. 03-366


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 79N; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 82


February 17, 2004, Submitted on Briefs  
March 30, 2004, Decided


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at McDonald v. State, 87 P.3d 1044, 2004 Mont. LEXIS 174 (Mont., Mar. 30, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Third Judicial District, In and For the County of Granite, Cause No. DC 97-08, Honorable Ted L. Mizner, Presiding Judge.
State v. McDonald, 299 Mont. 545, 4 P.3d 1219, 2000 Mont. LEXIS 419 (Mont., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, inmate, challenged the order of the District Court of the Third Judicial District, Granite County, Montana, denying his petition for postconviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The inmate and his friend fired over a dozen shots at a herd of 20 elk that were grazing in a fenced pasture near several hundred cattle. The inmate was found guilty of hunting a bull elk without a proper license, failure to wear the required orange-colored garments while hunting, hunting more than one game animal, and creating a hazard in the act of game hunting. The inmate claimed he received ineffective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal and that his consecutive sentences should have been concurrent. The appellate court ruled that trial counsel was not ineffective. Concerning each issued raised by the inmate, the record established that trial counsel conferred with the inmate in regard to the decision at issue, and the record established that each of the issues were discussed with the inmate and that a strategic decision was made about each. Also, appellate counsel made an informed and strategic decision to raise the single, best claim that he could, and the inmate failed to show that appellate counsel made the decision through neglect or through ignorance of the law.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

348 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Ravalli County v. Erickson


No. 03-593


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 35; 320 Mont. 31; 85 P.3d 772; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 37


December 11, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
February 19, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 9, 2004.
Summary judgment granted, in part, summary judgment denied, in part by Ravalli County v. Erickson, 2006 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1070 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged a decision from the District Court of the Twenty-First Judicial District, in and for the County of Ravalli (Montana), which refused to review the constitutionality of the subject matter of two ordinances proposed by respondent individual prior to their placement on an election ballot.


OVERVIEW: The individual sought to place two obscenity ordinances on the election ballot. Previous ordinances had been struck down by the Montana courts. The county filed a complaint requesting that the district court issue an opinion concerning the constitutionality of such ordinances under Mont. Code Ann. § 7-5-135. The district court declined to make such a determination regarding the subject matter contained therein, stating that it would result in the rendering of an advisory opinion. Thereafter, the county sought review. In reversing, the court determined that the intent of the Montana Legislature could have been determined from the plain meaning of the words in § 7-5-135(1). The language was plain, unambiguous, direct, and certain. When a suit was filed pursuant to § 7-5-135(1), a district court, after any briefing and fact-finding it deems appropriate, was required to determine whether a proposed ordinance would be valid and constitutional if passed. Therefore, § 7-5-135(1) required substantive review of the proposed ordinances by the district court.


OUTCOME: The decision of the district court was reversed. The case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

349 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Wagner v. State


No. 02-571


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2004 MT 31; 319 Mont. 413; 85 P.3d 750; 2004 Mont. LEXIS 33


December 30, 2003, Submitted on Briefs  
February 18, 2004, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication March 4, 2004.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Cause No. BDV-2002-214. Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon release from prison, the State informed plaintiff sex offender that he had to register as a sexual/violent offender pursuant to the Montana Sexual or Violent Offender Registration Act (SVORA), codified at Mont. Code Ann. §§ 46-18-255 and 46-23-501 to 46-23-520. The District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, dismissed the sex offender's declaratory action. The sex offender appealed.


OVERVIEW: Mont. Const. art. II, § 28(2) provided that full rights were restored by termination of state supervision for any offense against the State. Thus, the sex offender contended that retroactive application of SVORAs continuing registration requirements abridged his full restoration of rights, including rights to exist free from State regulation, to travel and to pursue employment, all of which he asserted were encompassed in Mont. Const. art. II, § 28(2). However, the Montana Supreme Court had previously ruled on the constitutionality of SVORA in State v. Mount. There, the supreme court held the "full rights" restored under art. II, § 28 following termination of state supervision for a criminal offense were civil and political rights incident to citizenship, including the right to vote, hold office, and enter occupations that required state licensing, and that privacy was not a right protected under art. II, § 28. The State had the requisite compelling interests in enacting SVORA, including protecting the public. The supreme court held that requirements under SVORA did not deprive defendant of any rights under Mont. Const. art. II, § 28.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, denying defendant's action for a declaratory judgment that the requirement that defendant register as a sex offender was a violation of his constitutional rights, was affirmed.
