Grabow v. Mont. High Sch. Ass'n


No. 01-633


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 242; 312 Mont. 92; 59 P.3d 14; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 503


May 9, 2002, Argued and Submitted  
November 4, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 2002, Reported at: 2002 Mont. LEXIS 597. Released for Publication December 6, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and for the County of Lewis and Clark, The Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of the First Judicial District, in and for the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, granted judgment in favor of appellee high school association in appellant student's action seeking declaratory judgment and injunctive relief from the association's decision to declare him ineligible to play basketball. The student appealed.


OVERVIEW: The student argued that the earlier order, granting him a preliminary and permanent injunction, entitled him to attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 and the private attorney general doctrine. The appellate court found that he could not receive attorney's fees because he had not prevailed in the case for purposes of § 1988 because he had not received a final judgment in his favor. Awarding attorney's fees without a determination of the merits against the other party violated due process. Although the school board adopted the association's rules as their own, the association's decision to exclude the student from participating in basketball was not the board's own decision. Mont. Code Ann. § 20-3-210 only applied to matters of controversy arising in the county. The student had no right to administrative appeal of the association's decisions. No authority empowered the Office of Public Instruction to review all of the association's regarding eligibility. Students could immediately seek judicial review after the association had reached a final decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Kiely Constr. L.L.C. v. City of Red Lodge


No. 01-200


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 241; 312 Mont. 52; 57 P.3d 836; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 502


September 20, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
November 1, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-Second Judicial District, In and for the County of Carbon, The Honorable Robert W. Holmstrom, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant City of Red Lodge, Montana, appealed the order of the District Court of the Twenty-Second Judicial District, County of Carbon, Montana, requiring the City to pay damages to cross-appellant construction company for a delay in approving the construction company's land use application. The construction company appealed the partial grant of summary judgment denying its request to approve the application.


OVERVIEW: After receiving a preliminary plat application for a proposed subdivision from a construction company, the Carbon County Planning Board, Montana, recommended approval of the proposed subdivision, subject to 18 conditions, to the City of Red Lodge, Montana. Red Lodge received the application, but failed to act upon it within 60 days. The construction company filed a complaint, alleging that Red Lodge failed to act within the mandatory 60-day time frame, that imposition of the conditions was an abuse of discretion, and that its due process rights were violated. The district court awarded the construction company $ 250,243 in attorney fees, pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, and also awarded costs. The district court declined to grant approval the application. The appellate court granted review and held the construction company failed to establish a property interest sufficient to maintain its § 1983 claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

392 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Dorwart v. Caraway


No. 01-199


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 240; 312 Mont. 1; 58 P.3d 128; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 504


March 19, 2002, Argued and Submitted  
October 31, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Twenty-Second Judicial District, In and for the County of Stillwater, The Honorable Maurice R. Colberg, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a criminal defendant who claimed his constitutional rights were deprived by respondent deputies who arrested him, sought review of the order of the District Court of the Twenty-Second Judicial District, in and for the County of Stillwater, Montana, granting summary judgment of his civil rights action.


OVERVIEW: While operating his motor vehicle, defendant was stopped and served with two writs of execution. Defendant was also arrested for driving under the influence of alcohol. Defendant advised the deputies that his wallet and driver's license were on the dashboard of his mother's car, which was parked in his driveway. The deputies interpreted defendant's remarks as permission to enter his home. The deputies proceeded to defendant's residence, entered the house and the garage, and seized various items of personal property. Defendant filed a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action claiming his civil rights were violated. The matter was set for judicial review. The court concluded that defendant was entitled to bring a claim for money damages based on the violation of his state constitutional rights. The deputies were not entitled to statutory immunity pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 2-9-103(1) against a claim for violation of Montana constitutional rights. The defendant was not entitled to attorney's fees.


OUTCOME: The district court's order of summary judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

393 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carson


No. 01-030


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 234; 311 Mont. 485; 56 P.3d 844; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 493


March 21, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
October 17, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication November 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Sixteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Rosebud, The Honorable Joe L. Hegel, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Petition for a writ of habeas corpus granted, to the extent it requested reconsideration by the Board of Pardons and Parole; remanded for a new parole hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was sentenced to a three-year deferred imposition of sentence after pleading guilty to felony theft. The District Court of the Sixteenth Judicial District, Rosebud County, Montana, subsequently imposed an 18-month jail sentence when defendant admitted to violating the conditions of his deferred sentence. Defendant's motion to modify the sentence and petitions for postconviction and habeas relief were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the trial court erred by denying his petition for postconviction relief and that he was entitled to legal representation at his parole hearing. The supreme court found that defendant did not file his petition for postconviction relief, in which he sought relief from an amended sentencing order, within the prescribed time period pursuant to Mont. Code Ann. § 46-21-102 (1999); therefore, the trial court did not err in concluding that it did not have jurisdiction to entertain the petition. Defendant contended that the board rejected his attorney's request to attend the parole hearing because his attorney submitted the request less than 10 days prior to the hearing. The supreme court found no such requirement within Mont. Code Ann. 46-23-202 or Mont. Admin. R. 20.25.401(4); therefore, the board violated defendant's statutory right to counsel at the parole hearing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus was granted as to his request to be represented by counsel at the parole hearing; the matter was remanded for a new parole hearing.

 

394 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Spoklie v. Mont. Dep't of Fish, Wildlife & Parks


No. 02-462


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 228; 311 Mont. 427; 56 P.3d 349; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 490


September 26, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
October 10, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 25, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fifteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Sheridan, The Honorable David Cybulski, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alternative livestock licensees sought to enjoin defendant Montana Department of Fish, Wildlife & Parks from enforcing its interpretation of the "fee shooting" provisions of Mont. Code Ann. § 87-4-414(2). The District Court of the Fifteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Sheridan, Montana, denied a motion to dissolve its preliminary injunction. The Department and intervenor sports groups appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Department interpreted the "fee shooting" provisions of Initiative 143, codified at Mont. Code Ann. § 87-4-414(2), to limit the shooting of animals on alternative livestock facilities to the license owner or principal manager. The district court restrained the Department from initiating enforcement actions against licensees for selling alternative livestock to third parties who would then seek to harvest their property at the licensees' facility. On appeal the Department characterized such sales as "canned hunting" experiences, and argued that the district court's preliminary injunction interfered with its enforcement of Mont. Code Ann. § 87-4-414(2), and was thus prohibited by Mont. Code Ann. § 27-19-103(4). The court concluded that the activity at issue constituted the type of activity prohibited by § 87-4-414(2), that the preliminary injunction interfered with the Department's execution of § 87-4-414(2), a statute enacted for the public benefit, and that, as the licensees neither alleged nor demonstrated that the initiative or § 87-4-414(2) were unconstitutional, the district court erred, as a matter of law, when it enjoined the Department's execution of § 87-4-414(2).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court order denying the motion by the Department and the sports groups to dissolve the district court's preliminary injunction, and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the instant opinion.

State v. Price


No. 01-810


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 229; 311 Mont. 439; 57 P.3d 42; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 491


April 4, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
October 10, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 25, 2002.
Judgment entered by State v. Price, 2002 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1436 (2002)
Motion denied by State v. Price, 2004 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1821 (2004)
Magistrate's recommendation at Price v. Heedon, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 125715 (D. Mont., Dec. 18, 2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Price v. AG of Montana, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25520 (D. Mont., Feb. 22, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Request granted Spain v. Mahoney, 2010 Mont. LEXIS 541 (Mont., May 25, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Price v. State, 360 Mont. 543, 2011 Mont. LEXIS 74 (Mont., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Dismissed by Price v. State, 2011 Mont. LEXIS 283 (Mont., May 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, The Honorable Edward P. McLean, Judge presiding.
State v. Price, 2002 Mont. Dist. LEXIS 1947, 2002 ML 1823 (2002)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of custodial interference pursuant to a plea agreement in the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, Montana. Defendant appealed both the district court's denial of his motion to dismiss on the grounds that Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-304(3) was violative of equal protection and void for vagueness, and its denial of his motion to dismiss for improper venue.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took his daughter away in the middle of the night preceding the day he was to return her to her mother, and changed locations over a three day period in attempts to hide his daughter. On appeal defendant asserted the district court erred in denying his motion to dismiss for improper venue. The court disagreed. As at least one of the requisite elements of Mont. Code Ann. § 45-5-304(1), depriving the girl's mother of lawful custody, occurred in Missoula, Missoula County constituted proper venue in defendant's prosecution. The court also denied defendant's contention under a rational relation test that § 45-5-304(3) violated equal protection as applied to him, or that, considered facially, § 45-5-304(3) was void for vagueness. The court held that the defense under § 45-5-304(3) for those who did not leave the state was available at trial to all defendants, but that defendant was not unconstitutionally deprived of an opportunity to assert the defense at trial because a reasonable person would be put on notice that he or she may not return a child to law enforcement upon arrest in an attempt to avoid culpability under § 45-5-304(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court, holding that the district court did not err in denying defendant's motions to dismiss on constitutional grounds or for improper venue.

 

396 of 699 DOCUMENTS


Merlin Myers Revocable Trust v. Yellowstone County


No. 01-676


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 201; 311 Mont. 194; 53 P.3d 1268; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 391; 158 Oil & Gas Rep. 431


February 21, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
September 5, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, In and for the County of Yellowstone, The Honorable Russell C. Fagg, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee landowner petitioned the District Court of the Thirteenth Judicial District, County of Yellowstone, Montana, to review a decision of appellant county commissioners denying its request for a special review of a denied application to conduct gravel mining. The trial court granted the landowner relief. The county commissioners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner filed an application for a gravel mining permit on land it owned and was zoned as agricultural open space. The county planning department could not reach a consensus and sent the matter to the county commissioners. The county commissioners denied the application, and any special review, on the basis that the application violated the state constitution regarding the right to a clean, healthful and safe environment. The trial court reversed the decision. The county commissioners appealed, arguing state statutes did not preclude a county from denying a special review to mine gravel with an open cut mine in a nonresidential area within its jurisdictional zoning area. The appellate court held the county commissioners did not have the authority to deny a special review under the plain language of Mont. Code Ann. § 76-2-209. The appellate court concluded the commission also exceeded their jurisdiction and authority under the separation of powers provision of the constitution by interpreting the foregoing statute as being violative of the state constitution right to a clean, healthful, and safe environment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

397 of 699 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Smartt v. Judicial Stds. Comm'n


No. 01-768


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 148; 310 Mont. 295; 50 P.3d 150; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 252


May 2, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
July 2, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Honorable Jeffrey M. Sherlock, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant justice of the peace petitioned the District Court of the First Judicial District, In and For the County of Lewis and Clark, Montana, for a writ of prohibition to bar respondent Judicial Standards Commission from commencing further proceedings against him. The justice appealed after the trial court modified the writ of prohibition that allowed the commission to proceed and granted the commission's summary judgment motion.


OVERVIEW: The commission received a written unverified complaint against the justice for sexual assault. The commission obtained a court order that allowed it to view a criminal investigation report (CIB) on the justice. The commission filed a formal complaint based on the unverified complaint. Initially, the trial court granted a writ of prohibition as the unverified complaint was not presented on the standardized form. The appellate court held that Mont. R. Jud. Standards Comm'n 10(b)did not prevent the commission from carrying out its constitutional duty to investigate complaints from citizens, and nothing in the Montana Constitution barred the commission from investigating willful misconduct in office or violations of the canons of judicial ethics. The court also held that the commission did not exceed its jurisdiction in obtaining a copy of the CIB file on the justice or by undertaking its own investigation. As the form of a complaint alleging judicial misconduct was not critical to the commission's fulfilling its constitutional mandate, the commission did not act without or in excess of its jurisdiction in its investigation or in filing the complaint.


OUTCOME: The district court's grant of the Commission's summary judgment motion and dismissal of the writ of prohibition was affirmed.

Spain v. Mont. Dep't of Revenue


No. 01-556


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 146; 310 Mont. 282; 49 P.3d 615; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 249


February 14, 2002, Submitted on Briefs  
June 27, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, In and For the County of Gallatin, Honorable Mike Salvagni, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, each individually and doing business as a construction company, appealed from the order of the District Court of the Eighteenth Judicial District, in and for the County of Gallatin, Montana, affirming the determination of the State Tax Appeal Board that certain workers were employees rather than independent contractors for purposes of state income tax withholding.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Department of Revenue (DOR) determined that some of the general contractor's workers were employees rather than independent contractors and that their income was not reported to the DOR for state withholding tax purposes, nor had withholding taxes for these workers been paid. The DOR submitted a notice of assessment for tax and interest due. The DOR also submitted a notice of assessment to petitioner, as although deemed an employee for unemployment insurance purposes for the years at issue, he nevertheless filed income tax returns as an independent contractor for those years. A hearing officer upheld the assessments, the State Tax Appeal Board (STAB) affirmed the hearing officer, and the district court reviewed the record, addressed petitioner's constitutional claims, and affirmed the STAB. The appellate court held that the district did not err in upholding the State Tax Appeal Board's determination under Mont. Code Ann. § §39-51-201(14) (1987) that the workers in question were employees rather than independent contractors, and that Mont. Code Ann. § 15-30-203(1) and Mont. Admin. R. 42.17.120 did not constitute a form of unconstitutional dual taxation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the district court.

Kloss v. Edward D. Jones & Co.


No. 00-507


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 129; 310 Mont. 123; 54 P.3d 1; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 223


October 11, 2001, Submitted on Briefs  
June 13, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Rehearing Denied September 25, 2002. Released for Publication September 26, 2002.
Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part Kloss v. Edward D. Jones & Co., 2002 MT 129A, 310 Mont. 147, 310 Mont. 147A, 57 P.3d 41, 2002 Mont. LEXIS 413 (2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Edward D. Jones & Co. v. Kloss, 538 U.S. 956, 155 L. Ed. 2d 506, 123 S. Ct. 1633, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 2696 (2003)
Related proceeding at In re Conservatorship of Kloss, 2005 MT 39, 2005 Mont. LEXIS 45 (Feb. 22, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Eighth Judicial District, In and for the County of Cascade, The Honorable Julie Macek, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sued defendants, a financial services company and its stockbroker, for damages allegedly caused by the stockbroker's wrongful conduct. The Eighth Judicial District Court, Cascade County, Montana, granted defendants' motion to compel arbitration. The client appealed the trial court's order compelling arbitration as well as an order denying her motion for attorney fees and costs.


OVERVIEW: The client opened financial services accounts with the company in 1992 and 1998. The agreements between the client and the company contained pre-dispute arbitration clauses. On appeal, the client argued that the trial court erred when it: (1) concluded that the arbitration clauses were enforceable; (2) failed to consider whether defendants owed the client a fiduciary duty to explain the arbitration provisions; and (3) denied the client's motion for attorney fees and costs. The instant court concluded that the trial court erred when it concluded that the arbitration clauses were enforceable. The arbitration provisions were not in the client's reasonable expectations. The stockbroker owed the client a fiduciary duty which included explaining the consequences of the arbitration provision defendants sought to enforce. Accordingly, the trial court erred when it failed to consider whether a fiduciary duty existed. Regarding the trial court's denial of the client's motion for attorney fees and costs, the instant court concluded that the trial court's finding that defendants did not unreasonably or vexatiously multiply the proceedings was not clearly erroneous.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order compelling arbitration was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings consistent with the instant court's opinion. The trial court's order denying the client's motion for attorney fees and costs was affirmed.

In re Marriage of Caffrey


No. 00-307


SUPREME COURT OF MONTANA


2002 MT 72N; 2002 Mont. LEXIS 90



April 11, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [**1] PURSUANT TO THE APPLICABLE MONTANA CODE SECTION THIS OPINION IS NOT DESIGNATED FOR PUBLICATION.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported in Table Case Format: 2002 Mont. LEXIS 263.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM: District Court of the Fourth Judicial District, In and for the County of Missoula, The Honorable John W. Larson, Judge presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged the order of the District Court of the Fourth Judicial District Missoula County (Montana) modifying his monthly child support payment to appellee mother.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that the district court erred in modifying child support without finding substantial and continuing changed circumstances. The appellate court ruled that it was not necessary for the district court to find that there were changed circumstances so substantial and continuing as to make the terms unconscionable before the district court could modify child support. As the parties' marital and property settlement agreement contained provisions relating to child support were not incorporated into the decree of dissolution, the provisions of Mont. Code Ann. § 40-4-208(2)(b) were not applicable. The appellate court also ruled that the district court correctly determined that the father's expenditures on vacations with the children did not relieve him of an actual child support contribution towards their daily needs. Furthermore, the father's fundamental liberty interests in parenting his children were not jeopardized, only his decision to withhold child support for his children's needs were affected by the district court's decision.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.
